Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Definition and Obligation of Salah
Definition and obligation of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of salah, identify its cause (sabab), and list its four essential arkan.

Core Idea
The cause of salah is time; its essential pillars are four, and the final sitting is wajib not rukn.

In this opening of the Book of Prayer, the author defines salah both linguistically and technically, establishes its obligation as fard 'ayn, and clarifies its cause (sabab) – the entrance of the prayer time. Understanding this foundation is key to distinguishing the arkan (pillars) from the wajibat (obligatory elements) that follow.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic vs. technical definition
The passage first defines 'salah' in language (supplication, praise, recitation, mercy) citing Quranic verses, then gives the shar'i definition: the specific prescribed actions (arkan).
The Hanafi technical definition focuses on the actions, not just verbal supplication.
2
Identify the cause of obligation (sabab)
The text states 'سبب وجوبها الوقت' – the cause is time itself. Each prayer becomes obligatory when its time enters.
This is distinct from the conditions (shurut) which are external prerequisites.
3
Recall the historical origin of obligation
Salah was made fard on the Night of Ascension, 18 months before Hijrah. Before that, only two daily prayers were required.
This historical fact affirms the universal obligation for all Muslims.
4
List the four essential pillars (arkan asliyyah)
The text specifies four: qiyam (standing), qira'ah (recitation), ruku' (bowing), and sujud (prostration).
The final sitting (qa'dah akhir) is NOT an essential pillar – it is wajib, differing from other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة: [لما فرغ من بيان الطهارة التي كانت شرطاً للصلاة شرع في بيان المشروط، وسبب وجوبها الوقت، فبينه أولاً. (ع ، ط] الصلاة في اللغة: اسم للدعاء والثناء والقراءة والرحمة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَصَلَّ علَيْهِم﴾ (التوبة: ۱۰۳)، أي ادع لهم، وقال: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ﴾ (الأحزاب:٥٦) قيل: هي وقال: ﴿وَلا تَجْهَرْ بِصَلَاتِكَ﴾ (الإسراء:۱۱۰) أي بقراءتك، وقال: ﴿أُولَئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَاتٌ مِنْ رَبِّهِمْ﴾ (البقرة: ١٥٧) أي رحمة، وشرعاً: الأركان المعهودة المخصوصة سميت بها لما في قيامها من القراءة، وفي قعودها من والدعاء، ولفاعلها من الرحمة وقيل في وجه التسمية أقوال أخر. فرضت ليلة المعراج وهي ليلة السبت لسبع عشرة خلت من رمضان قبل الهجرة بثمانية عشر شهرا وكانت قبل ذلك صلاتين صلاة قبل طلوع الشمس وصلاة قبل غروبها، وفرضيتها ثابت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع كما لا يخفى وسبب وجوبها الوقت؛ لأنها تضاف إليه، وشروطها تجيء في بابها وأركانها الأصلية أربعة: القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود، والقعدة الآخيرة ليست بركن أصلى وحكمها سقوط الوجوب عن الذمة في الدنيا ونيل الثواب في الآخرة، ولما كان السبب مقدماً تبعاً قدمه وضعاً وقال وقت الفجر إلخ. (مستخلص وغيره)
Book of Prayer: Having finished explaining purification which is a condition for prayer, he begins to explain the conditional, and the cause of its obligation is time, so he explains it first. Salah in language is a name for supplication, praise, recitation, and mercy. Allah said: 'And pray for them' meaning supplicate for them. And He said: 'Indeed Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet' – it is said it means. And He said: 'And do not be loud in your prayer' meaning in your recitation. And He said: 'Upon them are blessings from their Lord' meaning mercy. And in sacred law: the specific well-known actions (arkan). It is named for the recitation in its standing, the supplication in its sitting, and the mercy for the performer. Other opinions have been mentioned regarding the naming. It was made obligatory on the Night of Ascension, which was the night of Saturday, seventeen days into Ramadan, eighteen months before the Hijrah. Before that, there were two prayers: one before sunrise and one before sunset. Its obligatory nature is established by the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma, as is not hidden. The cause of its obligation is time, because it is added to it. Its conditions will come in their chapter. Its essential pillars (arkan asliyyah) are four: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The final sitting is not an essential pillar. Its ruling is the removal of obligation from the conscience in this world and attaining reward in the Hereafter. Since the cause is prior, he followed it and placed it first, saying 'The time of Fajr etc.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is the introductory section to the Book of Prayer (Kitab al-Salah) in Kanz al-Daqaiq. The commentator explains that after completing the section on purification (which is a condition for prayer), the author now turns to the thing conditioned, i.e., prayer itself. The cause (sabab) of the obligation of prayer is time (al-waqt). He first defines the word 'salah' linguistically, citing Quranic verses: it can mean supplication (du'a), praise (thana'), recitation (qira'ah), or mercy (rahmah). Then he gives the technical definition: the specific prescribed actions (arkan) consisting of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration, with the final sitting being not an essential pillar. He mentions that salah was made obligatory during the Night of Ascension (Mi'raj) about 18 months before the Hijrah, and that before that there were only two daily prayers (morning and evening). The obligation is proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'. The 'cause' (sabab) of prayer being wajib is the entrance of the time, because prayer is attributed to time (e.g., salat al-zuhr). The 'pillars' are four essential ones; the final sitting is not an essential pillar (meaning it is included as a wajib but not rukn). The 'ruling' (hukm) is that by performing it, the obligation falls from the conscience and one earns reward. Then the author will begin discussing the times.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salāh): In this text, shari'ah definition: the specific prescribed actions (arkan) including standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.
سبب (sabab): Cause of obligation: the time (waqt) of each prayer.
الأركان الأصلية (al-arkan al-asliyyah): The essential pillars: standing, recitation, bowing, prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of the five daily prayers?
A) The start of the month of Ramadan.
B) The entering of the specific prayer time.
C) The command of the ruler.
D) Reaching the age of fifteen.

Key Takeaway
Salah is fard 'ayn, its cause is time, and its essential pillars are four (standing, recitation, bowing, prostration); the final sitting is wajib, not rukn.

The End Time of Zuhr: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr end time with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the end time of Zuhr, cite the proofs for each, and identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling) with its justification.

Core Idea
Zuhr's end: shadow equal to object per mufta bihi; Abu Hanifa held double.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines the times for Fajr and Zuhr prayers, but the key point is the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school regarding the end of Zuhr. Abu Hanifa taught that Zuhr extends until the shadow is twice the object's height, while his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held it ends when shadow equals height. The text presents the evidence for each side and concludes that later fatwa follows the Sahibayn. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how intra-madhhab ikhtilaf is resolved through tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the exact criterion for Zuhr end time according to Abu Hanifa and according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Remember that both exclude the shadow at zenith (fay' al-zawal).
2
Examine the proof for the Sahibayn
Analyze the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet on two consecutive days: on the second day, he led Zuhr when the shadow was equal to the object's height.
This hadith is also used by Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Examine the proof for Abu Hanifa
Analyze the hadith 'Delay the Zuhr prayer, for the intense heat is from the blast of Hell.' Abu Hanifa uses this to imply a longer time.
The Sahibayn interpret this as a recommendation about timing, not a definition of the end.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Understand why later scholars preferred the Sahibayn's view: the explicit timing of Jibril, ease for the ummah, and the fatwa in the Haramayn.
The text states: 'الفتوى في الحرمين وغيرهما في هذا الزمان على قولهما'.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
See how a worshipper today should determine the end of Zuhr: when the shadow equals the object's height (excluding zenith shadow).
This affects the start of Asr and the validity of prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقت الفجر إلخ الصبح الصادق، هو البياض المعترض في الأفق، والمستطيل الذي يبدو في الأفق طولاً ليس بصبح، فإنه يكون بعده ظلمة، ولا يحرم الأكل والشرب والجماع في الصوم؛ لقوله عليها: "لا يغرنكم أذان بلال والفجر المستطيل، وإنما الفجر هو المستطير في الأفق"، أي المنتشر، وآخر وقت الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس وإنما قدم وقت الفجر، لعدم الاختلاف في أوله وآخره والأصل فيه إمامة جبرئيل عليها، فإنه أم النبي في الفجر في اليوم الأول حين طلع الفجر الثاني، وفي الثاني حين أسفر جداً تكاد الشمس تطلع، ثم قال: "ما بين هذين الوقتين وقت لك ولأمتك". (مستخلص) والظهر من الزوال إلخ : أي أول وقت الظهر إذا زالت الشمس؛ لإمامة جبريل عليه في اليوم الأول حين زالت الشمس، وآخر الوقت عند أبي حنيفة إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثليه سوى فيء الزوال، وقالا : إذا صار ظل شيء مثله سوى الفيء، وهو رواية عنه، وهو قول زفر والشافعي، لهم: أن إمامة جبريل في اليوم الأول كان في أول الوقت، وفي الثاني كان في آخر الوقت فإمامته في اليوم الثاني كان في هذا الوقت، فعلم أنه آخر وقت الظهر، ولأبي حنيفة قوله علي : أبردوا بالظهر، فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم"، وأشد الحر في ديارهم في هذا الوقت والفتوى في الحرمين وغيرهما في هذا الزمان على قولهما والفيء - بوزن الشيء - هو الظل قبيل الزوال؛ سمي لأنه فاء من المغرب إلى المشرق، أي رجع، وإنما استثني فيء الزوال؛ لأنه في بعض المواضع في بعض الأوقات يكون مثلاً أو مثلين. (فتح، مستخلص)
The time of Fajr etc. The true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq) is the whiteness spread horizontally across the horizon. The elongated dawn that appears vertically is not dawn, for after it comes darkness, and it does not make eating, drinking, and intercourse forbidden during fasting. Due to his saying: 'Do not be deceived by the adhan of Bilal nor by the elongated dawn; rather dawn is the spreading whiteness in the horizon.' The end time of Fajr is just before sunrise. He introduced the time of Fajr first because there is no disagreement regarding its beginning and end. The basis for it is the leadership of Jibril (peace be upon him), for he led the Prophet in Fajr on the first day when the second dawn rose, and on the second day when it was very bright, almost until sunrise. Then he said: 'Between these two times is a time for you and for your community.' And Zuhr from zenith etc.: meaning the beginning of Zuhr time is when the sun passes its zenith, due to the leadership of Jibril on the first day when the sun passed its zenith. The end time according to Abu Hanifa is when the shadow of every object becomes twice its height, excluding the shadow of the zenith (fay' al-zawal). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: when the shadow becomes the same length as the object, excluding the shadow of the zenith. This is also a narration from Abu Hanifa, and it is the view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Their evidence: that the leadership of Jibril on the first day was at the beginning of the time, and on the second day it was at the end; and his leadership on the second day was at that time, so it is known that that is the end of Zuhr time. And for Abu Hanifa is his saying: 'Delay the Zuhr prayer, for the intense heat is from the blast of Hell.' The most intense heat in their lands occurs at that time. The fatwa in the two sanctuaries and elsewhere in this time is according to their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Al-fay' (shadow) is the shade before zenith; it is named because it returns (fa'a) from the west to the east. It is excluded because in some places at some times it may be the same or double.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage details the times of Fajr and Zuhr prayers. For Fajr, the beginning is at 'true dawn' (al-subh al-sadiq), which is the horizontal white light spreading across the horizon, as opposed to the false vertical dawn which is not considered. The end time is just before sunrise. The evidence is the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer. For Zuhr, the beginning is when the sun passes the zenith. The dispute is over the end time: Abu Hanifa holds that Zuhr ends when the shadow of an object becomes twice its height (excluding the shadow at zenith), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (and also Shafi'i) hold that it ends when the shadow equals the object's height. Each uses evidence: the Sahibayn cite the timing of Jibril's second day prayer, while Abu Hanifa uses the hadith 'Delay the Zuhr prayer' indicating that in extreme heat it is better to wait, which implies a longer time. The fatwa nowadays, especially in the Two Holy Sanctuaries, follows the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (i.e., the shorter end time).

Key Terms
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawāl): The shadow of an object at the moment the sun passes its zenith; excluded in the calculation of Zuhr end time.
صبح صادق (subh sādiq): The true dawn: the horizontal whiteness that spreads across the horizon, marking the beginning of Fajr time.
صبح كاذب (subh kādhib): The false dawn: a vertical pillar of light that appears before true dawn, not considered for prayer or fasting times.
زوال (zawāl): The moment the sun passes its zenith; marks the beginning of Zuhr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school, when does the time for Zuhr prayer end?
A) When the shadow of an object becomes twice its height, excluding the zenith shadow.
B) When the shadow of an object becomes equal to its height, excluding the zenith shadow.
C) When the sun sets.
D) When the shadow disappears.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that Zuhr ends when the shadow of an object equals its height (excluding zenith shadow), as established by the fatwa of the later scholars following the Sahibayn.

The Time of Fajr Prayer: True Dawn vs False Dawn
Ruling with proof on Fajr time definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq) from the false dawn (al-subh al-kadhib) and state the time of Fajr prayer according to the Hanafi school, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Fajr time begins with horizontal spreading light, not vertical light.

Knowing exactly when Fajr begins is crucial for the validity of your prayer and fast. The Prophet ﷺ warned against mistaking the false dawn—a vertical column of light—for the true dawn, which spreads horizontally. This lesson unpacks the evidence from the Hadith of Jibril and other narrations, showing you how to confidently identify the correct time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that the passage gives a ruling on the time of Fajr. The ruling is: Fajr prayer begins at true dawn, ends at sunrise.
No ikhtilaf among schools on this.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Two hadiths are cited. First: the Prophet ﷺ said, 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal and the elongated dawn deceive you; verily the dawn is that which spreads in the horizon.' Second: the Hadith of Jibril (Gabriel) leading the Prophet at Fajr at two different times.
The first hadith defines true dawn; the second defines the full time window.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The phrase 'إنما الفجر هو المستطير' (verily the dawn is that which spreads) indicates that the true dawn is the horizontal spreading light. The Hadith of Jibril shows that the time spans from when true dawn appears until just before sunrise.
This is a clear dalālah (indication) – qat'ī in meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقت الفجر إلخ الصبح الصادق، هو البياض المعترض في الأفق، والمستطيل الذي يبدو في الأفق طولاً ليس بصبح، فإنه يكون بعده ظلمة، ولا يحرم الأكل والشرب والجماع في الصوم؛ لقوله عليه : 'لا يغرنكم أذان بلال والفجر المستطيل، وإنما الفجر هو المستطير في الأفق'، أي المنتشر، وآخر وقت الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس وإنما قدم وقت الفجر، لعدم الاختلاف في أوله وآخره والأصل فيه إمامة جبرئيل عليه ، فإنه أم النبي في الفجر في اليوم الأول حين طلع الفجر الثاني، وفي الثاني حين أسفر جداً تكاد الشمس تطلع، ثم قال: 'ما بين هذين الوقتين وقت لك ولأمتك'. (مستخلص)
The time of Fajr, etc. The true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq) is the whiteness spreading horizontally in the horizon. The elongated whiteness that appears vertically in the horizon is not dawn; darkness follows it. Eating, drinking, and intercourse are not prohibited during fasting because of it. The Prophet said: 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal and the elongated dawn deceive you; verily the dawn is that which spreads in the horizon.' Its end is before sunrise. The time of Fajr is mentioned first because there is no difference of opinion regarding its beginning and end. The basis for it is the leadership of Jibril, peace be upon him, as he led the Prophet in Fajr on the first day when the second dawn appeared, and on the second day when it was very bright almost as if the sun was about to rise, then he said: 'Between these two times is the time for you and your ummah.' (Summarized)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage explains the time of Fajr prayer. The true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq) is the horizontal whiteness that spreads across the horizon. There is also a false dawn (al-subh al-kadhib) which is vertical and is followed by darkness; it is not the proper time. The proof is the hadith that warns against being deceived by Bilal's adhan and the false dawn, and confirms that the true dawn is the spreading light. The end of Fajr time is at sunrise. The basis for the time is the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet at Fajr at two different times on consecutive days, indicating the entire span of time. There is no disagreement on the Fajr time, so it is mentioned first.

Key Terms
الصبح الصادق (al-subh al-sadiq): The horizontal whiteness that spreads across the horizon, marking the true beginning of Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What marks the beginning of Fajr prayer time?
A) The elongated vertical light in the horizon
B) The horizontal spreading whiteness in the horizon
C) The adhan of Bilal
D) The appearance of the first star

Key Takeaway
The time for Fajr prayer is determined by the true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq), which is the horizontal spreading light, not the false dawn.

The End of Zuhr Time: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States Zuhr time and the end-time dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the end of Zuhr time, identify the proofs each side uses, and explain why the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Zuhr's end differs: Abu Hanifa says shadow twice, Sahibayn says shadow equals. The fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

The beginning of Zuhr time is agreed upon, but the endpoint sparked a notable disagreement within the Hanafi school itself. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and guides you to the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed start of Zuhr
All agree Zuhr begins at zawal (sun's decline). Confirm from the hadith of Jibril.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position on the end
Abu Hanifa holds that Zuhr ends when the shadow of an object (excluding fay') reaches twice its height.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the height (excluding fay').
This is also a narration from Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the proofs
Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Jibril (praying at the end on day two). Abu Hanifa relies on 'Delay the Zuhr' and the link to intense heat.
Note how each text is interpreted.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and justification
The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's saying. The text mentions this is the case in the Two Sanctuaries and nowadays.
Al-Marghinani confirms this tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والظهر من الزوال إلخ : أي أول وقت الظهر إذا زالت الشمس؛ لإمامة جبريل عليه في اليوم الأول حين زالت الشمس، وآخر الوقت عند أبي حنيفة إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثليه سوى فيء الزوال، وقالا : إذا صار ظل شيء مثله سوى الفيء، وهو رواية عنه، وهو قول زفر والشافعي، لهم: أن إمامة جبريل في اليوم الأول كان في أول الوقت، وفي الثاني كان في آخر الوقت فإمامته في اليوم الثاني كان في هذا الوقت، فعلم أنه آخر وقت الظهر، ولأبي حنيفة قوله عليه : 'أبردوا بالظهر، فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم'، وأشد الحر في ديارهم في هذا الوقت والفتوى في الحرمين وغيرهما في هذا الزمان على قولهما والفيء - بوزن الشيء - هو الظل قبيل الزوال؛ سمي لأنه فاء من المغرب إلى المشرق، أي رجع، وإنما استثني فيء الزوال؛ لأنه في بعض المواضع في بعض الأوقات يكون مثلاً أو مثلين. (فتح، مستخلص)
And Zuhr from zawal, etc.: i.e., the beginning of Zuhr time is when the sun declines, due to the imamate of Jibril on the first day when the sun declined. The end of the time according to Abu Hanifa is when the shadow of each thing becomes twice its length excluding the shadow of zawal. And the two said: when the shadow of a thing becomes equal to its length excluding the shadow, and this is a narration from him, and it is the view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Their proof: that the imamate of Jibril on the first day was at the beginning of time, and on the second day at the end of time, so his imamate on the second day was at this time, so it is known that this is the end of Zuhr time. And for Abu Hanifa is his saying: 'Delay the Zuhr prayer, for intense heat is from the blazing of Hell,' and the most intense heat in their lands occurs at this time. The fatwa in the Two Sanctuaries and elsewhere nowadays is according to their saying. And al-fay' (shadow) before zawal is called because it returns from the west to the east. It is excluded because in some places at some times it may be one or two lengths. (Fath, summarized)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage addresses the time of Zuhr prayer. The beginning of Zuhr is agreed upon: when the sun passes its zenith (zawal). The dispute is about the end of Zuhr time. According to Abu Hanifa, Zuhr ends when the shadow of any object becomes twice its height, excluding the shadow that existed at zawal. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), Zuhr ends when the shadow becomes equal to the object's height, excluding the zawal shadow. This is also a narration from Abu Hanifa and the view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i. The Sahibayn argue based on the hadith of Jibril: Jibril led the Prophet at the beginning of Zuhr on the first day, and at the end on the second day when the shadow was one length. Abu Hanifa uses the hadith 'Delay the Zuhr' as evidence that the time extends until the shadow is twice, because the most intense heat is at that later time. The fatwa in the Two Sanctuaries and nowadays follows the Sahibayn. The term fay' refers to the shadow before zawal; it is excluded because it varies.

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay'): The shadow before zawal (declination of the sun). It is excluded when measuring the shadow for the end of Zuhr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) in this text, when does Zuhr time end?
A) When shadow is twice the height
B) When shadow equals the height
C) At the zenith
D) At sunset

Key Takeaway
The end of Zuhr time is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn (shadow equals height), not Abu Hanifa's original view (shadow twice).

The Beginning of Asr Prayer: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
States the beginning of Asr depends on the end of Zuhr, with same ikhtilaf; ends at sunset.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions on the beginning of Asr time within the Hanafi school and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The Asr time begins when the shadow equals height (Sahibayn) not twice height (Abu Hanifa) in the operative fatwa.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute over when Asr prayer time begins. All scholars agree Asr ends at sunset, but its start is tied to the end of Zuhr, which itself is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly determining prayer times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and its scope
The text states that the beginning of Asr depends on the end of Zuhr, with the same ikhtilaf. The core issue is: when does Zuhr time exit and Asr time enter?
The dispute is only about the start; the end of Asr is at sunset by consensus.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa (the single 'him' in the text), Asr begins when the shadow of each object becomes twice its height (zill mithlayn). Zuhr ends at that same moment.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, referred to as 'the two'), Asr begins when the shadow equals the object's height (zill mithl). Zuhr ends at that earlier point.
The text says this is 'the apparent school' (zahir al-madhhab).
4
Note the third narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad
A narration from Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad states that Zuhr ends at shadow equal, but Asr does not begin until shadow double, leaving an 'abandoned time' (waqt muhmal) between them, similar to the gap between Fajr and sunrise.
This view is not widely followed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if someone prays Asr when shadow is between one and two lengths, according to Abu Hanifa it is qada' (if before Asr time), but according to the Sahibayn it is within time. The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view, so the Asr time begins earlier.
The end of Asr is sunset, based on the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset. Hasan ibn Ziyad's minority view that it ends at yellowing is also noted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعصر منه إلخ: أي أول وقت العصر إذا خرج وقت الظهر على اختلاف القولين، فعنده إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثليه يخرج وقت الظهر ويدخل وقت العصر، وعندهما إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثله يدخل وقت العصر، فالاختلاف ثابت في أول وقت العصر وآخر وقت الظهر، وهو ظاهر المذهب. وفي رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثله يخرج وقت الظهر، ولا يدخل وقت العصر حتى يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه، فكان بينهما وقت مهمل كما بين الفجر والظهر، فعلى هذا يكون الاختلاف في دخول وقت العصر، وفي خروج وقت الظهر اتفاق. إلى الغروب: أي زمان قبيل غروب الشمس؛ لقوله عليه: 'من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدركها، فعلم منه أن آخر وقت العصر ما لم تغرب الشمس. (مستخلص) وقال الحسن بن زياد: آخر وقت العصر حين تصفر الشمس. (ط)
And Asr from it, etc.: i.e., the beginning of Asr time is when Zuhr time exits according to the two different views. According to him [Abu Hanifa], when the shadow of every thing becomes twice its height, Zuhr time exits and Asr time enters. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], when the shadow of every thing becomes equal to its height, Asr time enters. So the difference is established in the beginning of Asr time and the end of Zuhr time, and this is the apparent school. And in the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa: when the shadow of every thing becomes equal to its height, Zuhr time exits, and Asr time does not enter until the shadow becomes twice its height, so there is an abandoned time between them like between Fajr and Zuhr. According to this, the difference is in the entry of Asr time and there is agreement on the exit of Zuhr time. Up to sunset: i.e., a time just before sunset; due to his saying: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught it.' So it is known that the end of Asr time is as long as the sun has not set. (Summarized) And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: the end of Asr time is when the sun becomes yellow. (Reported)
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage explains the time of Asr. The beginning of Asr is directly tied to the end of Zuhr, so the same ikhtilaf applies: according to Abu Hanifa, Asr begins when the shadow is twice; according to the Sahibayn, when it equals. The text also mentions a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that there is an interval (waqt muhmal) between Zuhr and Asr when no prayer is valid, similar to the gap between Fajr and Zuhr. The end of Asr is at sunset, as indicated by the hadith. Another view from Hasan ibn Ziyad says it ends when the sun turns yellow, which is a minority view.

Key Terms
الظل المثل (al-zill al-mithl): Shadow equal to the height of the object, used as a measure for the end of Zuhr and beginning of Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does Asr prayer time begin?
A) Immediately after the sun passes the zenith
B) When the shadow of each thing equals its height
C) When the shadow of each thing is twice its height
D) At the time of the sun's yellowing

Key Takeaway
The beginning of Asr time is disputed within the Hanafi school; the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) follows the Sahibayn: Asr begins when the shadow equals the object's height.

Definition of Shafaq and the End of Maghrib Time
States Maghrib time with dispute on shafaq definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi positions on shafaq and state the mufta bihi definition with its evidence.

Core Idea
The end of Maghrib time depends on shafaq; the Hanafi fatwa now defines shafaq as redness, contrary to Abu Hanifa's earlier view.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the agreed-upon beginning of Maghrib time and the disputed end. While the schools agree that Maghrib enters at sunset, they differ on when it exits. The point of contention is the definition of 'shafaq' (twilight). Understanding this dispute is crucial for accurate prayer timing and highlights how a madhhab can refine its position over time based on stronger evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed and disputed elements of Maghrib time
The passage states that the start of Maghrib time (sunset) is without disagreement. The end time is at the disappearance of shafaq, but the definition of shafaq is disputed. Recognize this as the central issue.
2
State Abu Hanifa's original definition of shafaq
According to Abu Hanifa, shafaq is the whiteness (al-bayad) in the horizon after the redness disappears. This means Maghrib time extends until the white twilight fades.
This view relies on a hadith interpreted as the white twilight.
3
State the Sahibayn's definition and their evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) held that shafaq is the redness (al-humrah) itself. They cite the hadith 'al-shafaq huwa al-humrah' (shafaq is the redness) and the linguistic consensus.
Al-Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the shift to the mufta bihi
The passage from Fath al-Mu'in states the fatwa is that shafaq is redness, due to agreement of the people of language and the general body of Companions interpreting shafaq as redness. Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have retracted to this view.
This illustrates the concept of tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf)
If shafaq is whiteness, Maghrib time ends later; if redness, it ends earlier. The mufta bihi (redness) means Maghrib time is shorter, and delaying prayer beyond the red twilight is not permissible.
This directly affects daily prayer scheduling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمغرب منه : بالجر عطف على العصر، أي أول وقت المغرب من الغروب بلا خلاف، وآخر الوقت عند غروب الشفق خلافاً للشافعي، له قوله عليه: 'وقت المغرب إذا اسود الأفق'، ولنا قوله عليه: 'أول وقت المغرب إذا غربت الشمس، وآخر وقتها حين تغيب الشفق'، وما رواه موقوف على ابن عمر، ثم الشفق هو البياض الذي في الأفق بعد الحمرة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا هو الحمرة، وهو قول الشافعي؛ لقوله عليه: 'الشفق هو الحمرة'. (عيني، مستخلص) وقال في 'فتح المعين': المفتى به أن الشفق هو الحمرة؛ لاتفاق أهل اللسان عليه حتى نقل أن الإمام رجع إليه لما ثبت عنده من حمل عامة الصحابة الشفق على الحمرة. غروب الشفق وقال الشافعي وقتها مقدر بقدر الوضوء والأذان والإقامة وخمس ركعات، وقيل: مقدر بثلاث ركعات عنده وهو البياض الذي بعد الحمرة، وقالا وهو قول الشافعي ورواية عن أبي حنيفة: هو الحمرة، وبه يفتى. (مسكين)
And Maghrib from it (i.e., from sunset): in the genitive case as an apposition to Asr, meaning the beginning of Maghrib time is from sunset without disagreement. The end of the time is at the disappearance of shafaq, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His proof: his saying: 'The time of Maghrib is when the horizon becomes black.' Our proof: his saying: 'The beginning of Maghrib time is when the sun sets, and its end is when the shafaq disappears.' And what he narrated is stopped at Ibn Umar. Then shafaq is the whiteness in the horizon after the redness according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said it is the redness, and that is the saying of al-Shafi'i because of his saying: 'Al-shafaq is the redness.' (Ayni, summarized) And it is said in Fath al-Mu'in: The fatwa is that shafaq is the redness, due to the agreement of the people of language, and it has been transmitted that the Imam (Abu Hanifa) retracted to it when it became established to him that the general body of the Companions interpreted shafaq as redness. The disappearance of shafaq: Al-Shafi'i said its time is estimated to the extent of performing wudu, adhan, iqama, and five rak'ahs, and it is said: it is estimated at three rak'ahs according to him. And whiteness after the redness: The two said it is redness, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Hanifa: it is redness, and fatwa is given accordingly. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses the time of Maghrib prayer. The beginning is agreed upon: at sunset. The end is at the disappearance of shafaq, but the definition of shafaq is disputed. According to Abu Hanifa, shafaq is the whiteness (bayad) that remains in the horizon after the redness (humrah) disappears. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) and al-Shafi'i, shafaq is the redness itself. The Sahibayn rely on a hadith that 'shafaq is the redness.' Abu Hanifa's proof is a hadith that the time ends when shafaq disappears, which he interprets as the white twilight. The text mentions that the fatwa is now that shafaq is the redness, as it is the agreed-upon linguistic meaning and many Companions interpreted it that way. Also, there is an additional discussion: Shafi'i estimates the Maghrib time as a short period (enough for wudu, adhan, iqama, and five rak'ahs), but the Hanafi position is that it continues until the shafaq disappears.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset. Disputed whether it is the red or white light.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) mentioned in this passage, what is shafaq?
A) The whiteness after the redness
B) The redness
C) The blackness of the horizon
D) The first light of dawn

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on shafaq is redness, ending Maghrib time earlier than Abu Hanifa's original view.

Times of the Five Daily Prayers
States the prescribed times for each prayer concisely using abbreviations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed times for each of the five daily prayers according to the Hanafi school and explain the abbreviations used in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Core Idea
Each prayer has a specific time window; performing it outside its time invalidates the prayer.

The times for the five daily prayers are foundational to the validity of Salah. This lesson unpacks the concise matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which uses shorthand abbreviations. You will learn to interpret these abbreviations and memorise the Hanafi prayer times with precision.

Guided Path
1
Decode the abbreviations
Identify the letters س (shay'), م (mithl), ز (zawal), ف (fay'), دك (dhak?) – they stand for key terms: object, like, declination, shade, and 'dhak' possibly refers to 'that is' or a marker. The matn uses them to define time endpoints.
The exact expansion of 'دك' is debated but interpreted as part of the phrase 'مثليه سوى الفيء'.
2
Determine Zuhr time
Zuhr begins at zawal (sun's zenith) and ends when the shadow of an object becomes twice its height, excluding the original shadow present at zawal (al-fay').
The matn says 'س م ز ف دك مثليه سوى الفيء' meaning the shadow becomes like two times except the shade.
3
Determine Asr time
Asr begins at that moment (when shadow is twice object height) and ends at sunset.
This is the beginning of Asr according to Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it begins when shadow equals object height (the earlier view, but the matn follows Abu Hanifa).
4
Determine Maghrib time
Maghrib begins immediately after sunset and ends when the twilight (al-shafaq) disappears. The matn defines twilight as al-bayad (the whiteness).
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says shafaq is whiteness; Sahibayn say it is redness. Later fatwa prefers Sahibayn.
5
Determine Isha and Witr time
Isha begins after Maghrib time ends (i.e., after disappearance of twilight) and continues until dawn (al-subh al-sadiq). Witr shares the same time but must be prayed after Isha due to tartib (order).
The matn emphasizes that Witr cannot precede Isha; order is a condition for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
مواقيت الصلاة
س م ز ف دك مثليه سوى الفيء، والعصر منه إلى الغروب، والمغرب منه إلى غروب الشفق، وهو البياض، والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح ولا يقدم على العشاء للترتيب.
Book of Prayer. Times of Prayer. S M Z F dk two times except the shade, and Asr from that to sunset, and Maghrib from that to disappearance of twilight, which is the whiteness, and Isha and Witr from that to dawn, and one does not advance Witr before Isha due to order.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This is the matn (core text) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on prayer times. The abbreviations are interpreted as follows: S = shay' (the shadow of an object), M = mithl (like), Z = zawal (declination), F = fay' (the shade remaining after zawal). The phrase 'س م ز ف دك مثليه سوى الفيء' means that Zuhr time begins from zawal until the shadow of every object becomes twice its length, excluding the shade at zawal. The time for Asr starts at that point and ends at sunset. Maghrib begins at sunset and ends when the twilight (shafaq) disappears, which the matn defines as whiteness (al-bayad) – this is the white glow that appears in the sky after the redness. Isha and Witr share the same time from the disappearance of twilight until true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq). However, Witr must not be performed before Isha due to the prescribed order (tartib). This lesson is a memorization anchor for the basic prayer times according to the Hanafi school as stated in the original text.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): Twilight; defined in the matn as the whiteness (al-bayad) after redness.
الفيء (al-fay'): The shade that appears after the sun passes its zenith (zawal).
الترتيب (al-tartib): The prescribed order of prayers; Witr must follow Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, when does the time for Asr begin?
A) At zawal
B) When the shadow of every object becomes equal to its height
C) When the shadow of every object becomes twice its height (excluding the shade at zawal)
D) At sunset

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines prayer times by observable natural phenomena: the sun's zenith, shadow lengths, sunset, twilight (disputed), and dawn; the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq provides a concise anchor for these definitions.

End of Asr Time: Proof from Hadith
Establishes the end of Asr time with a Prophetic hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the end of Asr time and explain the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Asr time lasts until sunset; the hadith proves this.

When does Asr time end? A simple question, but one with a subtle intra-Hanafi difference. This passage clarifies the authoritative position by citing the well-known Prophetic hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset, and it addresses a minority view that would shorten the time. Let's trace the proof and see why the majority opinion is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the timing of Asr prayer. The ruling is that its end time is at sunset. What does the matn say? 'To sunset'.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught it.' This is the primary proof.
The hadith is attributed to 'Ali but is well-known from Abu Huraira; the meaning is sound.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'before the sun sets' (قبل أن تغرب الشمس) indicates that the time continues until sunset. Catching a rak'ah before that point means the prayer is on time.
Hanafi usul: the clear implication (dalala qati) from a sahih hadith establishes the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Hasan ibn Ziyad held that Asr ends when the sun turns yellow, i.e., earlier. This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
His reasoning may be based on avoiding delay, but it is not from a strong proof.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The hadith is explicit and taken from the Mustakhlas; the reliance position (mufta bihi) is sunset. The yellowing view is not followed.
The text signals tarjih by saying 'and it is known from this that the end of Asr time is as long as the sun has not set.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى الغروب: أي زمان قبيل غروب الشمس؛ لقوله علي: "من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدركها، فعلم منه أن آخر وقت العصر ما لم تغرب الشمس. (مستخلص) وقال الحسن بن زياد: آخر وقت العصر حين تصفر الشمس. (ط)
'To sunset': meaning a time just before sunset, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught it.' So it is known from this that the end of Asr time is as long as the sun has not set. (Mustakhlas) And Hasan ibn Ziyad said: The end of Asr time is when the sun turns yellow. (Tahawi)
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage explains the matn's phrase 'إلى الغروب' (to sunset) for Asr. The proof is a hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught it.' This indicates that Asr time continues until sunset. However, there is a separate opinion from Hasan ibn Ziyad that the last time is when the sun turns yellow (a time before sunset when the sun's light weakens). This is a notable minority view within the Hanafi school. The hadith used is attributed to 'Ali but is commonly known from Abu Huraira. The text clarifies the authoritative end of Asr and guards against the misconception that Asr ends at yellowing.

Key Terms
الركعة (al-rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the end of Asr time according to the hadith cited in this passage?
A) When the sun turns yellow
B) At sunset
C) When the shadow becomes twice
D) At the disappearance of twilight

Key Takeaway
Asr time ends at sunset; the hadith of catching a rak'ah before sunset is the primary proof.

Isha and Witr Time: Hanafi Position and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Establishes Isha/Witr time and addresses differing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the time of Isha and Witr, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the beginning of Witr time, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument on Isha time.

Core Idea
Isha and Witr share the same window from twilight to dawn; Witr's time hinges on its wajib or sunna nature.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the foundational ruling for Isha and Witr times. It clarifies that both prayers extend from the disappearance of twilight until true dawn, a position supported by a clear hadith. The text then addresses an important intra-Hanafi dispute—whether Witr may be performed before Isha—and ties this to the differing views on the nature of Witr (wajib vs sunna). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground and the Shafi'i objection
First, note that all Hanafis agree that Isha time extends until dawn. The text cites a hadith to refute Imam al-Shafi'i, who limits Isha to one-third of the night. Recognize this inter-madhhab disagreement.
The Shafi'i view is based on a different interpretation of ahadith, but the Hanafi proof is considered stronger.
2
State the Hanafi position on Isha time
The matn states: 'the beginning of the time of Isha and Witr is from the disappearance of twilight until true dawn.' This is the relied-upon Hanafi view. Understand the dalil: the Prophet said 'the last time of Isha is when dawn appears.'
Twilight (shafaq) is the red glow after sunset; true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) is the horizontal light.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr time
Abu Hanifa holds that Witr time begins with Isha (from twilight), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it begins after Isha. The text attributes the companion's view to al-Mukhtasar and Abu Hanifa's view to the matn.
This difference is not about the end time (both say until dawn) but the start.
4
Understand the connection between Witr's nature and its time
Abu Hanifa considers Witr wajib, so when two wajib prayers share a time frame, both can be offered in that window—even if one is ordered to be first. The companions consider Witr sunna, prescribed after Isha, so its time begins after Isha, like the sunna of Zuhr.
The hadith 'Allah has added a prayer for you, and it is Witr' supports the wajib view for Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
According to Abu Hanifa, one may pray Witr before Isha (though order/tartib may require Isha first). According to the companions, Witr must be after Isha. The mufta bihi for fatwa is the companions' view, making Witr sunna and its time after Isha.
The condition of tartib (order) means even Abu Hanifa would require Isha first in practice, so the difference is mostly theoretical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مسكين، مستخلص) للترتيب : [كما لا تقدم الوقتية على الفائتة (ط) اعلم أن وقت الوتر وقت العشاء عند أ . أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: وقته بعد العشاء، وهذا بناء على الاختلاف في صفته، فعنده الوتر واجب والوقت متى جمع بين الصلاتين الواجبتين فهو وقتهما، وإن أمر بتقديم أحدهما كصلاة الوقت والفائتة، وصلاتي الجمع بعرفة، ولأن الوتر مزيد؛ لقوله علي زاد" عليكم صلاة وهي الوتر والعشاء مزيد عليه، وتقديم المزيد عليه فرض على المزيد، وعندهما: الوتر سنة شرعت بعد العشاء، فيدخل وقته بعد العشاء كركعتي الظهر، فلا يجوز أداء الوتر قبل العشاء عنده؛ للترتيب، وعندهما؛ لأنه تبع للعشاء. (مستخلص)
And 'Isha and Witr' meaning the beginning of the time of Isha and Witr is from the disappearance of twilight until true dawn, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'And the last time of Isha is when dawn appears.' And this is a proof against al-Shafi'i who estimates it at the passing of one-third of the night. And the two companions said: The beginning of Witr time is after Isha until the appearance of dawn, due to his saying (peace be upon him) concerning Witr: 'Pray it after Isha until the appearance of dawn.' And what is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar: The beginning of Witr time is after Isha, that is their saying. And what is mentioned in the matn is the saying of Abu Hanifa. (Miskin, Mustakhlas) For the order: [Just as one does not offer a current prayer before a missed one (Tahawi). Know that the time of Witr is the time of Isha according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them its time is after Isha. This is built on the difference regarding its nature. According to him (Abu Hanifa), Witr is obligatory (wajib), and the time when two obligatory prayers are combined is the time of both, even if one is ordered to be offered first, like the current prayer and the missed prayer, and the two prayers combined at 'Arafa. And because Witr is additional; he (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah has added a prayer for you, and it is Witr,' and Isha is added upon it, and advancing what is added over what it is added to is obligatory. According to them (the two companions), Witr is sunna that was prescribed after Isha, so its time begins after Isha like the two rak'ahs of Zuhr. So it is not permissible to perform Witr before Isha according to him (Abu Hanifa) due to order, and according to them because it is a follower of Isha. (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses the time for Isha and Witr. The base ruling: both Isha and Witr begin from the disappearance of twilight (shafaq) and continue until true dawn (al-suhb al-sadiq). This is supported by a hadith stating that the last time for Isha is at dawn. This refutes al-Shafi'i who restricts Isha to one-third of the night. An important intra-Hanafi dispute concerns Witr: according to Abu Hanifa, the time for Witr is the same as Isha (from shafaq to dawn), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say Witr begins after Isha and lasts until dawn. The reason for this difference is the nature of Witr: Abu Hanifa considers it wajib (obligatory) and thus its time aligns with the other wajib prayer (Isha). The companions consider it sunna, established after Isha, thus its time follows Isha. This affects whether Witr can be performed before Isha: according to Abu Hanifa it is permissible (due to the shared time), but according to the companions it is not permissible (since Witr is subordinate to Isha). The text notes that al-Mukhtasar (by Imam Muhammad) states the companions' view, while the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually 1 or 3 rak'ahs) performed after Isha.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order of prayers; Witr should not be performed before Isha.
الشفق (al-shafaq): The redness in the sky after sunset; the disappearance of shafaq marks the beginning of Isha time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does the time of Witr begin?
A) From sunset
B) From the disappearance of twilight
C) After Isha prayer
D) At dawn

Key Takeaway
The time of Isha is from twilight to dawn, and Witr's time depends on whether it is wajib (same time as Isha) or sunna (after Isha); the operative view is that Witr is sunna and must be prayed after Isha.

Obligation of Prayers When Time Is Absent
Discusses whether Isha/Witr are obligatory when time is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Isha and Witr are not obligatory when their prescribed times are completely absent, and explain the qiyas used to derive this ruling.

Core Idea
No time, no obligation – the cause of prayer's obligation is its time.

In high-latitude regions like Bulghar (Volga Bulgaria), the night during summer can be so short that the time for Isha (and Witr) does not occur. Does the obligation for these prayers remain? The Hanafi school addressed this through the principle that the existence of the prescribed time is the cause (sabab) of the obligation of prayer. If the cause is absent, the obligation is lifted. This lesson explores the ruling and the qiyas (analogy) used to support it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the exceptional scenario
The act in question is the Isha prayer and its associated Witr. The scenario is a location (like Bulghar) where the sun sets and Fajr begins before the twilight of Isha has disappeared – effectively, the time for Isha is absent.
The passage specifically mentions 'when one does not find both times' (i.e., the time windows for Isha and Witr).
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling derived from the principle 'no time, no obligation': Isha and Witr are not obligatory when their prescribed times are completely absent. This is based on the absence of the cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub).
The fatwa of non-obligation became the mufta bihi after the exchange between al-Hulwani and al-Bakali.
3
Trace the proof: the qiyas (analogy)
The proof is a logical analogy presented by Sayf al-Din al-Bakali. He analogized the missing prayer time to a person with amputated limbs whose wudu obligations are reduced because the limb is absent. Just as the obligation to wash an amputated limb falls away, the obligation of a prayer falls away when its time is absent.
The common illa (effective cause) is the absence of the cause of obligation – the limb for wudu, the time for prayer.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and its resolution
Initially, Shams al-A'immah al-Hulwani ruled that qada (making up) of Isha is required. However, al-Bakali's qiyas convinced him, and he adopted the view of non-obligation after a respectful exchange.
This shows the dynamic process of ijtihad within the Hanafi school, where a later and stronger dalil can override an earlier opinion.
5
Evaluate the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under al-Hulwani's initial view, Muslims in high-latitude areas would have to make up Isha prayers later (e.g., during winter when normal times return). Under the mufta bihi view, they are not obligated at all, removing hardship.
The ruling applies only when the time is completely absent; if any portion of the time exists, the prayer remains obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يجد وقتيهما لم يجبا. أي العشاء والوتر
الأوقات المندوبة للصلاة]
وقتيهما: أي العشاء ،والوتر، بأن كان ببلدة إذا غربت الشمس طلع الفجر كبلغار. (ط)
وقته رضوان الله،
لم يجبا لعدم سبب الوجوب والوقت، وفي فتاوى الظهيرية : أنه ورد فتوى من بلغار على شمس الأئمة الحلواني بأن الفجر فيها يطلع قبل غيبوبة الشفق في أقصر ليالي السنة، فكتب: "عليكم بوجوب قضاء العشاء"، ثم ورد بخوارزم على الشيخ الكبير سيف الدين البقالي فأفتى بعدم الوجوب، وبلغ جوابه شمس الأئمة فأرسل يسأله من في عامة بجامع خوارزم ما تقول فيمن أسقط من الصلوات الخمس واحدة هل يكفر؟ فأحسن به الشيخ فقال: ما تقول فيمن قطعت يداه من المرفقين أو رجلاه من الكعبين، فكم فرائض وضوئه؟ فقال: ثلاث لفوات محل الرابع، فقال: كذلك الصلاة الخامسة، فبلغ الحلواني جوابه فاستحسنه ووافقه فيه. (مسكين، مستخلص)
And whoever does not find both times (of Isha and Witr), they are not obligatory. (Meaning: Isha and Witr). [The recommended times for prayer]. Their two times: meaning Isha and Witr. That is, if one is in a town where when the sun sets, dawn appears (like Bulghar). (Tahawi) Its time, may Allah be pleased with him. They are not obligatory due to the absence of the cause of obligation and the time. And in Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: a fatwa came from Bulghar to Shams al-A'immah al-Hulwani that Fajr appears there before the disappearance of twilight in the shortest nights of the year, so he wrote: 'You must make up the missed Isha (qada).' Then the matter came to Khwarazm to the great shaykh Sayf al-Din al-Bakali, and he gave a fatwa of non-obligation. His answer reached Shams al-A'immah, so he sent someone to ask him in the public gathering in the mosque of Khwarazm: 'What do you say about someone who drops one of the five prayers, does he become a disbeliever?' He (the shaykh) answered well: 'What do you say about someone whose hands are cut off from the elbows or his feet from the ankles, how many obligatory acts of wudu remain?' He replied: 'Three, due to the loss of the place of the fourth.' He said: 'Likewise the fifth prayer.' So the answer reached al-Hulwani and he approved and agreed with it. (Miskin, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage addresses a unique practical problem: in high-latitude regions like Bulghar (Volga Bulgaria), during the shortest nights of the year, the sun sets and then dawn (Fajr) begins before the twilight (shafaq) for Isha has fully disappeared. In such a case, the time for Isha (and Witr) is effectively absent. The ruling: if the prescribed time does not exist, the prayer is not obligatory. However, there was a difference of opinion among Hanafi jurists. Shams al-A'immah al-Hulwani initially said qada (making up) is required. Sayf al-Din al-Bakali held that it is not obligatory at all, analogizing to the case of a person with amputated limbs whose wudu obligations are reduced. He argued that just as a missing limb removes the obligation of washing that part, the absence of time removes the obligation of that prayer. Al-Hulwani accepted this reasoning. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of using qiyas (analogy) and consideration of 'illa (cause) in deriving rulings for unprecedented situations. The final relied-upon view: if the time for a prayer is completely absent (not just shortened), the prayer is not obligatory.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has passed.
سبب الوجوب (sabab al-wujub): The cause that makes an act obligatory; for prayer, it is the existence of its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the final agreed-upon ruling for Isha prayer in Bulghar where Fajr appears before twilight disappears?
A) Isha must be made up (qada')
B) Isha is not obligatory at all
C) Isha must be performed in combination with Maghrib
D) One should follow the nearest normal region's time

Key Takeaway
When the prescribed time for a prayer is completely absent, the prayer is not obligatory due to the absence of the cause of obligation.

Delaying Fajr: The Hanafi Recommendation and the Shafi'i Objection
Hanafi ruling on Fajr delay with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on delaying Fajr, cite the hadith proof, and explain why the Shafi'i counter-argument is rejected.

Core Idea
Delay Fajr until light — the Prophet ﷺ commanded it for greater reward.

This lesson unpacks the first ruling in the passage: the recommendation to delay Fajr until the sky is bright (isfar). We will examine the Hanafi proof, the Shafi'i objection, and the Hanafi response based on authentic transmission and practical wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Hanafi ruling
The act is performing Fajr. The Hanafi ruling: it is recommended (mandub) to delay it until the time of isfar (light) in all seasons. Note that this is not wajib.
The text explicitly says 'فإنه أعظم للأجر' indicating recommendation.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' (Make Fajr light [delay it], for it is greater in reward). This is a command (amr) which in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation (nadb) when accompanied by a promise of greater reward.
Also cited: the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hastening Fajr is always better. His proof: a hadith (with a weak chain according to Hanafis) that the beginning and middle of time are mercy and the end is forgiveness.
The text identifies the narrator Ibrahim ibn Zakariyya as weak.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi scholars dismiss the Shafi'i hadith as unauthentic (munkar). They also present practical benefits: delay increases congregation size, helps the weak and sleepy ones to attend, and is more convenient.
This shows that the Hanafi position considers both textual evidence and maslahah.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi practice, Fajr is delayed until light is clear; in Shafi'i, it is prayed early in the dark. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
Exception: for pilgrims at Muzdalifah, early prayer is better.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب تأخير الفجر وظهر الصيف والعصر ما لم تتغير والعشاء إلى الثلث
،
(ط) وندب تأخير الفجر: أي في الأزمنة كلها، وقال الشافعي: يستحب التعجيل في كل صلاة؛ لقوله علي: "أول ووسطه رحمة الله، وآخره ره عفو الله"، ولنا: قوله عليه: "أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر"، وعن داود بن يزيد عن أبيه قال: كان علي بن أبي طالب يصلي بنا الفجر ونحن نتراأى الشمس مخافة أن تكون قد طلعت، ولأن في الإسفار تكثير الجماعة، وتوسيع الحال على النائم أو الضعيف في إدراك فضل الجماعة، وما استدل به غير صحيح؛ لأن فيه إبراهيم بن زكريا، وهو منكر الحديث عند أهل النقل. (فتح) تأخير الفجر: أي تأخير صلاة في الأزمنة كلها بحيث يرتل أربعين آية ثم يعيده بطهارة لو فسد، إلا للحاج بمزدلفة فالتغليس أفضل. (ط)] والعبرة لتغير القرص عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بأن لا تحار العين في القرص، يعني يذهب ضوءه، فلا يحصل للبصر حيرة وهو الأصح، ولا عبرة لتغير الضوء الذي يقع على الجدار، والتأخير إلى تغير الشمس يكره، أما الأداء فغير مكروه، وقيل: الأداء مكروه أيضاً. (مسكين) إلى الثلث: [ أي ثلث الليل والتأخير إلى النصف مباح، وإلى النصف الأخير بلا عذر مكروه تحريما. (ط)] لتقليل الجماعة. كذا في "الهداية": ويكره النوم قبل الأداء لمن يخشى فوت الجماعة، والحديث بعدها بغير حاجة، وإلا فلا، كقراءة القرآن والذكر وحكايات الصالحين ومذاكرة الفقه والحديث مع الضيف والعرس، ويكره الكلام بعد انفجار الصبح، وإذا صلى الفجر جاز له الكلام. وتأخير العشاء إلى ما زاد إلى نصف الليل، والعصر إلى وقت اصفرار الشمس، والمغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم يكره تحريما. (فتح)
And it is recommended to delay Fajr, the Zuhr of summer, Asr as long as it (the sun) has not changed, and Isha until the third (of the night). (Tahawi) And it is recommended to delay Fajr: meaning in all seasons. And al-Shafi'i said: it is recommended to hasten every prayer, due to his saying (A?): 'The beginning and middle of it (time) are mercy of Allah, and its end is forgiveness of Allah.' And our evidence is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Delay Fajr until it is light (asfiru), for that is greater in reward.' And from Dawud ibn Yazid from his father that Ali ibn Abi Talib used to pray Fajr with us while we were trying to see the sun, fearing that it had already risen. And because in making it light (isfar) there is an increase in the congregation and facilitation for the sleeper or the weak to attain the virtue of congregation. And what he (Shafi'i) used as evidence is not authentic because it contains Ibrahim ibn Zakariyya, who is a rejectable narrator. (Fath) Delaying Fajr: meaning delaying the prayer in all seasons to the extent that one can recite forty verses and then repeat it with wudu if it becomes invalid, except for the pilgrim at Muzdalifah where early (taghlis) is better. (Tahawi) And (delaying) Zuhr of summer due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Cool down the Zuhr in summer, for the severity of heat is from the blaze of Hell.' And because Anas ibn Malik reported that he (peace be upon him) used to hasten Zuhr in winter and cool it in summer. And the limit of delay is that it is prayed before the shadow becomes equal to the object. (Fath, Mustakhlas) As long as it (the sun) has not changed: meaning that the eye is not dazzled in seeing the sun's disc; delaying to the change is makruh tahriman. (Tahawi) And the consideration is the change of the disc according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: that the eye is not dazzled by the disc, meaning its light goes away, so the eye does not become confused, and this is the most correct view. And there is no consideration of the change of light that falls on the wall. And delaying until the sun changes is makruh, while performing (at that time) is not makruh, but some said it is also makruh. (Miskin) Until the third: meaning one-third of the night; delaying until half is permissible, and delaying to the last half without excuse is makruh tahriman. (Tahawi) Because it reduces the congregation. So it is in al-Hidayah: It is makruh to sleep before performing (Isha) for one who fears missing the congregation, and to talk after it without need; otherwise it is not, like reciting Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest or at a wedding. And it is makruh to talk after Fajr appears, and when one has prayed Fajr, it is permissible to talk. And delaying Isha beyond half the night, and Asr until the sun turns yellow, and Maghrib until the stars are thick (i.e., become plenty) is makruh tahriman. (Fath)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage outlines recommended (mandub) times for delaying certain prayers and the prohibitions of delaying them too much. For Fajr, it is recommended to delay it until there is enough light (isfar), contrary to the Shafi'i view that hastening is always better. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' and the practice of Ali. Regarding Zuhr in summer, it is recommended to delay it until the intense heat subsides, based on the hadith 'أبردوا بالظهر في الصيف'. The limit of delay is before the shadow equals the object. For Asr, it is recommended to perform it while the sun is still high and its disc is not yet dazzling; delaying until the sun changes (turns yellow) is makruh tahriman. For Isha, it is recommended to delay it until one-third of the night, and it is permissible to delay until midnight; delaying beyond midnight without excuse is makruh tahriman. The passage also mentions that sleeping before Isha or talking after it without need is makruh for those who fear missing the congregation. Additionally, it states that performing Maghrib when the stars are thick is makruh tahriman. This passage provides a comprehensive guide to the preferred times and prohibited delays.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isfar): The time when the sky becomes bright enough to distinguish things clearly; delaying Fajr to this time is recommended.
التغليس (al-taghlis): Performing Fajr in darkness; for pilgrims at Muzdalifah, this is better.

D) 'أول الوقت رحمة الله'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Fajr until the sky is bright, based on an authentic hadith and practical wisdom, in contrast to the Shafi'i position of hastening.

Delaying Zuhr in Summer: The Command to Cool Down
Hanafi ruling on Zuhr delay in summer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Zuhr in summer, cite the hadith proof, and define the limit of delay.

Core Idea
Cool down Zuhr in summer — intense heat is from the blaze of Hell.

This lesson covers the second recommendation: delaying Zuhr in summer until the heat subsides. We will examine the hadith 'أبردوا بالظهر' and the limit of delay before the shadow equals the object.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is Zuhr prayer in summer. Ruling: it is recommended (mandub) to delay it until the intense heat lessens.
This does not apply in winter; then hastening is recommended.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'أبردوا بالظهر في الصيف، فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم' (Cool down the Zuhr in summer, for the severity of heat is from the blaze of Hell). Also the practice of the Prophet as reported by Anas.
This hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Determine the limit of delay
The delay should be such that the prayer is performed before the shadow of an object becomes equal to its height (before the time of 'misal' or 'zawal' ends). The limit is before 'al-mithl'.
After that, the time enters for 'fard' but delay would be makruh.
4
Note the exception
In winter, recommendation is to hasten Zuhr, based on the practice of the Prophet who used to hasten it in winter.
5
Summarize the rule
Summer: delay until heat subsides but before shadows equal objects. Winter: hasten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب تأخير الفجر وظهر الصيف والعصر ما لم تتغير والعشاء إلى الثلث
،
(ط) وندب تأخير الفجر: أي في الأزمنة كلها، وقال الشافعي: يستحب التعجيل في كل صلاة؛ لقوله علي: "أول ووسطه رحمة الله، وآخره ره عفو الله"، ولنا: قوله عليه: "أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر"، وعن داود بن يزيد عن أبيه قال: كان علي بن أبي طالب يصلي بنا الفجر ونحن نتراأى الشمس مخافة أن تكون قد طلعت، ولأن في الإسفار تكثير الجماعة، وتوسيع الحال على النائم أو الضعيف في إدراك فضل الجماعة، وما استدل به غير صحيح؛ لأن فيه إبراهيم بن زكريا، وهو منكر الحديث عند أهل النقل. (فتح) تأخير الفجر: أي تأخير صلاة في الأزمنة كلها بحيث يرتل أربعين آية ثم يعيده بطهارة لو فسد، إلا للحاج بمزدلفة فالتغليس أفضل. (ط) وظهر الصيف لقوله عليه: "أبردوا بالظهر في الصيف، فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم"، ولما روى أنس بن مالك: أنه عليه كان يبكر الظهر - أي يعجلها - في الشتاء ويبردها في الصيف، وحد التأخير أن يصلى قبل المثل. (فتح، مستخلص ما لم تتغير [ أي الشمس بأن لا تحار العين في رؤية قرصها، والتأخير إلى التغير يكره تحريماً. (ط)] والعبرة لتغير القرص عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بأن لا تحار العين في القرص، يعني يذهب ضوءه، فلا يحصل للبصر حيرة وهو الأصح، ولا عبرة لتغير الضوء الذي يقع على الجدار، والتأخير إلى تغير الشمس يكره، أما الأداء فغير مكروه، وقيل: الأداء مكروه أيضاً. (مسكين) إلى الثلث: [ أي ثلث الليل والتأخير إلى النصف مباح، وإلى النصف الأخير بلا عذر مكروه تحريما. (ط)] لتقليل الجماعة. كذا في "الهداية": ويكره النوم قبل الأداء لمن يخشى فوت الجماعة، والحديث بعدها بغير حاجة، وإلا فلا، كقراءة القرآن والذكر وحكايات الصالحين ومذاكرة الفقه والحديث مع الضيف والعرس، ويكره الكلام بعد انفجار الصبح، وإذا صلى الفجر جاز له الكلام. وتأخير العشاء إلى ما زاد إلى نصف الليل، والعصر إلى وقت اصفرار الشمس، والمغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم يكره تحريما. (فتح)
And it is recommended to delay Fajr, the Zuhr of summer, Asr as long as it (the sun) has not changed, and Isha until the third (of the night). (Tahawi) And it is recommended to delay Fajr: meaning in all seasons. And al-Shafi'i said: it is recommended to hasten every prayer, due to his saying (A?): 'The beginning and middle of it (time) are mercy of Allah, and its end is forgiveness of Allah.' And our evidence is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Delay Fajr until it is light (asfiru), for that is greater in reward.' And from Dawud ibn Yazid from his father that Ali ibn Abi Talib used to pray Fajr with us while we were trying to see the sun, fearing that it had already risen. And because in making it light (isfar) there is an increase in the congregation and facilitation for the sleeper or the weak to attain the virtue of congregation. And what he (Shafi'i) used as evidence is not authentic because it contains Ibrahim ibn Zakariyya, who is a rejectable narrator. (Fath) Delaying Fajr: meaning delaying the prayer in all seasons to the extent that one can recite forty verses and then repeat it with wudu if it becomes invalid, except for the pilgrim at Muzdalifah where early (taghlis) is better. (Tahawi) And (delaying) Zuhr of summer due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Cool down the Zuhr in summer, for the severity of heat is from the blaze of Hell.' And because Anas ibn Malik reported that he (peace be upon him) used to hasten Zuhr in winter and cool it in summer. And the limit of delay is that it is prayed before the shadow becomes equal to the object. (Fath, Mustakhlas) As long as it (the sun) has not changed: meaning that the eye is not dazzled in seeing the sun's disc; delaying to the change is makruh tahriman. (Tahawi) And the consideration is the change of the disc according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: that the eye is not dazzled by the disc, meaning its light goes away, so the eye does not become confused, and this is the most correct view. And there is no consideration of the change of light that falls on the wall. And delaying until the sun changes is makruh, while performing (at that time) is not makruh, but some said it is also makruh. (Miskin) Until the third: meaning one-third of the night; delaying until half is permissible, and delaying to the last half without excuse is makruh tahriman. (Tahawi) Because it reduces the congregation. So it is in al-Hidayah: It is makruh to sleep before performing (Isha) for one who fears missing the congregation, and to talk after it without need; otherwise it is not, like reciting Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest or at a wedding. And it is makruh to talk after Fajr appears, and when one has prayed Fajr, it is permissible to talk. And delaying Isha beyond half the night, and Asr until the sun turns yellow, and Maghrib until the stars are thick (i.e., become plenty) is makruh tahriman. (Fath)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage outlines recommended (mandub) times for delaying certain prayers and the prohibitions of delaying them too much. For Fajr, it is recommended to delay it until there is enough light (isfar), contrary to the Shafi'i view that hastening is always better. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' and the practice of Ali. Regarding Zuhr in summer, it is recommended to delay it until the intense heat subsides, based on the hadith 'أبردوا بالظهر في الصيف'. The limit of delay is before the shadow equals the object. For Asr, it is recommended to perform it while the sun is still high and its disc is not yet dazzling; delaying until the sun changes (turns yellow) is makruh tahriman. For Isha, it is recommended to delay it until one-third of the night, and it is permissible to delay until midnight; delaying beyond midnight without excuse is makruh tahriman. The passage also mentions that sleeping before Isha or talking after it without need is makruh for those who fear missing the congregation. Additionally, it states that performing Maghrib when the stars are thick is makruh tahriman. This passage provides a comprehensive guide to the preferred times and prohibited delays.

Key Terms
الإبراد (al-ibrad): Delaying Zuhr until the heat cools down; the recommended practice in summer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the limit of delay for Zuhr in summer?
A) Until the sun begins to decline
B) Before the shadow of an object becomes equal to its height
C) Until the time for Asr enters
D) There is no limit

Key Takeaway
Zuhr in summer should be delayed until the heat lessens but before the shadow equals the object, based on the authentic hadith.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Delaying Asr: Before the Sun Changes
Hanafi ruling on Asr timing with definition of change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Asr early and explain when delay becomes makruh tahriman.

Core Idea
Perform Asr while the sun is bright; delaying until it turns yellow is prohibitively disliked.

This lesson explains the recommendation to perform Asr early while the sun is still high, and the limit of change into yellow. The passage clarifies the criterion for change according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Act: Asr prayer. Ruling: It is recommended (mandub) to perform it early, before the sun changes (turns yellow).
2
Define 'change' (taghayyur)
The change is when the sun's disc becomes such that the eye is not dazzled by it; its brightness fades. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The change of light on walls is not considered.
There is a difference of opinion: some say the criterion is light on walls, but the most correct view is the disc.
3
State the limit
Performing Asr before the change is recommended. Delaying until the change is makruh tahriman. Some scholars also consider performing at the change as makruh.
The text says: 'الأداء فغير مكروه، وقيل: مكروه أيضاً' meaning performance at change is not makruh according to one view, but some say it is.
4
Note the practical implication
To get the full reward, Asr should be prayed early. However, if delayed beyond the change, the prayer is still valid but sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

التغير (al-taghayyur): The change of the sun's disc to a dull yellow when the eye is not dazzled.

According to the most correct view (al-asahh), what is the criterion for the sun's change?
A) The light on the wall changes

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Delaying Isha: Recommended Time and Prohibited Delay
Hanafi ruling on Isha timing with levels of recommendation and prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommended time for Isha, the permissible delay, and when it becomes makruh tahriman.

Core Idea
Delay Isha until one-third of the night; delaying past half is prohibitively disliked.

This lesson covers the recommendation to delay Isha until one-third of the night has passed, the permissibility of delaying to half, and the prohibition of delaying to the last half without excuse. It also touches on related etiquette: sleeping before Isha and talking after it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Act: Isha prayer. Ruling: It is recommended (mandub) to delay it until one-third of the night has passed.
The night begins after Maghrib.
2
Distinguish permissible and prohibited delays
Delaying until half the night is permissible (mubah). Delaying beyond half without a valid excuse is makruh tahriman.
The text says: 'والتأخير إلى النصف مباح، وإلى النصف الأخير بلا عذر مكروه تحريما'.
3
Identify the reason for the prohibition
Delaying beyond half reduces the attendance in congregation ('لتقليل الجماعة').
4
Note related rulings
Sleeping before performing Isha is makruh if one fears missing the congregation. Talking after Isha without need is also makruh, but permissible if it is beneficial (e.g., reciting Quran, studying fiqh).
5
Summarize the complete time hierarchy for Isha
Best: first third. Permissible: up to half. Makruh tahriman: beyond half without excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
