This passage outlines recommended (mandub) times for delaying certain prayers and the prohibitions of delaying them too much. For Fajr, it is recommended to delay it until there is enough light (isfar), contrary to the Shafi'i view that hastening is always better. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' and the practice of Ali. Regarding Zuhr in summer, it is recommended to delay it until the intense heat subsides, based on the hadith 'أبردوا بالظهر في الصيف'. The limit of delay is before the shadow equals the object. For Asr, it is recommended to perform it while the sun is still high and its disc is not yet dazzling; delaying until the sun changes (turns yellow) is makruh tahriman. For Isha, it is recommended to delay it until one-third of the night, and it is permissible to delay until midnight; delaying beyond midnight without excuse is makruh tahriman. The passage also mentions that sleeping before Isha or talking after it without need is makruh for those who fear missing the congregation. Additionally, it states that performing Maghrib when the stars are thick is makruh tahriman. This passage provides a comprehensive guide to the preferred times and prohibited delays.

Key Terms
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): When stars become plentiful; delaying Maghrib to that point is makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on delaying Isha beyond half the night without an excuse?
A) Recommended
B) Permissible
C) Makruh tahriman
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Isha is best prayed in the first third of the night; delaying to half is permissible, but beyond half without excuse is makruh tahriman.

When Isha and Witr Are Not Obligatory: The Time Condition
Ruling on Isha/Witr obligation in extreme northern latitudes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Isha and Witr prayer in extreme northern latitudes and explain the qiyas (analogy) used by Hanafi scholars to derive this ruling.

Core Idea
When the time for Isha does not appear, the obligation is lifted — the condition of time is as crucial as the condition of limbs for wudu.

This lesson examines a unique fiqh issue: what happens to the obligation of Isha and Witr prayers in regions where the night is so short that no time between sunset and dawn actually appears? The Hanafi school, through a powerful analogy from wudu, resolves that the obligation is removed entirely—not just delayed. You will follow the reasoning of two great Hanafi jurists and their eventual agreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Understand the scenario: a town where the sun sets and dawn rises immediately, so the time for Isha (between sunset and disappearance of twilight) does not occur. The text cites Bulghar as an example.
This is not a hypothetical—it occurs in high latitudes.
2
State the Condition for Obligation
Recognize that time (waqt) is a necessary condition (shart) for the obligation of prayer. If the time is absent, the obligation falls away. The text says 'lam yajiba' (they are not obligatory) due to the absence of the cause (sabab) and the time.
Hanafi usul: 'al-waqt shart al-wujub' — time is a condition of obligation.
3
Follow the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Learn about the initial disagreement: Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani ruled qada (make-up) is obligatory; Saif al-Din al-Bukhari ruled no obligation. Al-Halwani later tested al-Bukhari's reasoning publicly.
This shows how ijtihad is tested and refined among Hanafi scholars.
4
Analyze the Qiyas (Analogy)
Work through al-Bukhari's analogy: a person with amputated hands and feet has only three limbs for wudu; similarly, a person whose Isha time never appears has only four prayers obligatory. The illa (effective cause) is the absence of the condition (limb/time).
The wudu limbs are obligatory only if present; similarly, prayer is obligatory only if time is present.
5
Conclude the Mufta Bihi Ruling
Confirm that al-Halwani accepted the qiyas and agreed with al-Bukhari. The relied-upon position is non-obligation, and this ruling applies to any similar locality (e.g., regions with continuous daylight).
This ruling is from later fatwa collections (Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah), but it is now settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يجد وقتيهما لم يجبا. أي العشاء والوتر وقتيهما: أي العشاء ،والوتر، بأن كان ببلدة إذا غربت الشمس طلع الفجر كبلغار. (ط) لم يجبا لعدم سبب الوجوب والوقت، وفي فتاوى الظهيرية : أنه ورد فتوى من بلغار على شمس الأئمة الحلواني بأن الفجر فيها يطلع قبل غيبوبة الشفق في أقصر ليالي السنة، فكتب: "عليكم بوجوب قضاء العشاء"، ثم ورد بخوارزم على الشيخ الكبير سيف الدين البقالي فأفتى بعدم الوجوب، وبلغ جوابه شمس الأئمة فأرسل يسأله من في عامة بجامع خوارزم ما تقول فيمن أسقط من الصلوات الخمس واحدة هل يكفر؟ فأحسن به الشيخ فقال: ما تقول فيمن قطعت يداه من المرفقين أو رجلاه من الكعبين، فكم فرائض وضوئه؟ فقال: ثلاث لفوات محل الرابع، فقال: كذلك الصلاة الخامسة، فبلغ الحلواني جوابه فاستحسنه ووافقه فيه. (مسكين، مستخلص)
And whoever does not find their two times, they are not obligatory. Meaning Isha and Witr. Their two times: meaning Isha and Witr, as in a town where when the sun sets, dawn rises, like Bulghar. (T) They are not obligatory due to the absence of the cause of obligation and the time. In Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: that a fatwa request came from Bulghar to Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani that dawn there rises before the disappearance of the twilight in the shortest nights of the year, so he wrote: "Upon you is the obligation of making up Isha." Then [a request] came to Khwarazm to the great scholar Saif al-Din al-Bukhari, and he gave a fatwa of non-obligation. His answer reached Shams al-A'immah, so he sent someone to ask him publicly in the congregational mosque of Khwarazm: "What do you say about one who drops one of the five prayers—does he become an unbeliever?" The teacher responded well: "What do you say about one whose hands are cut off from the elbows or his feet from the ankles—how many obligatory parts of his wudu are there?" He said: "Three, due to the loss of the fourth place." He said: "Similarly, the fifth prayer." So al-Halwani's answer reached him, and he approved it and agreed with him. (Miskeen, Mustakhlis)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the obligation of Isha and Witr prayers in regions with extremely short nights, such as Bulghar (modern-day Bulgaria/Tatar region). The text explains that if a person does not find the time for these prayers—meaning the period between sunset and dawn is so brief that the time for Isha (from sunset to disappearance of twilight) does not occur before dawn—then these prayers are not obligatory. The reason given is that the time (waqt) is a necessary cause for obligation, and in its absence, the obligation is removed. The commentary then relates a historical debate among Hanafi scholars. Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani initially ruled that qada (make-up) of Isha was obligatory, but Saif al-Din al-Bukhari ruled that it was not obligatory. To resolve the dispute, al-Halwani sent a questioner to al-Bukhari to ask publicly whether dropping one of the five prayers constitutes disbelief. Al-Bukhari responded with an analogy (qiyas): a person with amputated hands and feet only has three obligatory parts of wudu due to the loss of the limbs; similarly, a person in such a location has only four daily prayers obligatory, as the fifth prayer's time is missing. Al-Halwani accepted this reasoning and agreed. This ruling is from later fatwa collections (Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah) and is considered the mufta bihi (operative) position for such regions.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The specified time period for an obligatory prayer; absence of waqt removes the obligation.
وقتيهما (waqtayhima): The two times for Isha and Witr prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani change his initial fatwa to agree with Saif al-Din al-Bukhari?
A) He received a direct revelation from Allah.
B) He was convinced by the qiyas (analogy) from wudu.
C) He feared the ruler's authority.
D) He realized his initial fatwa was based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Isha and Witr are not obligatory in locations where their prescribed time does not occur, using a qiyas from the obligation of wudu limbs when those limbs are missing.

Recommended Delay of Fajr: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on Fajr timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the timing of Fajr prayer, cite the primary proof for each, and apply the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
Delaying Fajr to brightness (isfar) is recommended in the Hanafi school for greater congregation and reward.

The timing of Fajr prayer is a point of valid scholarly difference. While many assume that praying at the earliest moment is always best, the Hanafi school holds a nuanced view: for Fajr, delaying until the sky is bright (isfar) is recommended (mandub). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proofs and the response to the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: it is recommended (mandub) to delay Fajr prayer until isfar (brightness) in all seasons. This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hastening (ta'jil) is recommended for all prayers, including Fajr, citing a hadith about mercy and forgiveness.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof: a hadith that the beginning and middle of time are mercy, and the end is forgiveness. This implies that earlier prayer is more merciful.
The Hanafi response critiques this hadith's chain.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis provide three proofs: (1) the hadith 'Asfiru bi-l-fajr' commanding brightness, (2) the practice of 'Ali praying when the sun was visible, and (3) the rational benefit of a larger congregation. Then they critique the Shafi'i hadith as weak due to a rejected narrator.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis in congregation delay Fajr until brightness; Shafi'is pray at early dawn. This affects mosque timings and individual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب تأخير الفجر: أي في الأزمنة كلها، وقال الشافعي: يستحب التعجيل في كل صلاة؛ لقوله عليه: "أول ووسطه رحمة الله، وآخره ره عفو الله"، ولنا: قوله عليه: "أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر"، وعن داود بن يزيد عن أبيه قال: كان علي بن أبي طالب يصلي بنا الفجر ونحن نتراأى الشمس مخافة أن تكون قد طلعت، ولأن في الإسفار تكثير الجماعة، وتوسيع الحال على النائم أو الضعيف في إدراك فضل الجماعة، وما استدل به غير صحيح؛ لأن فيه إبراهيم بن زكريا، وهو منكر الحديث عند أهل النقل. (فتح)
And it is recommended to delay Fajr: meaning in all times. Al-Shafi'i said: It is recommended to hasten in every prayer; due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Its beginning and middle are the mercy of Allah, and its end is the forgiveness of Allah.' And for us (the Hanafis): his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Make Fajr bright (isfiru), for it is greater in reward.' And from Dawud ibn Yazid from his father: He said: 'Ali ibn Abi Talib prayed Fajr with us while we could clearly see the sun, fearing that it had risen.' And because in making it bright there is an increase of the congregation and making it easier for the sleeping or weak person to attain the virtue of the congregation. And what he (al-Shafi'i) adduced is not authentic; because in it is Ibrahim ibn Zakariyya, and he is a rejected narrator according to the people of transmission. (Fath)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended time for Fajr prayer. The Hanafi school holds that it is recommended (mandub) to delay Fajr—specifically, to perform it when the sky is bright (isfar) rather than immediately at dawn (taghlis). This applies in all seasons. The Shafi'i school, however, prefers hastening (ta'jil) in all prayers, citing a hadith that the beginning and middle of prayer time are mercy and the end is forgiveness, implying earliness is better. The Hanafi response provides three proofs: (1) The hadith 'Asfiru bi-l-fajr fa innahu a'zam li-l-ajr'—a direct command to brighten Fajr. (2) The practice of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib who prayed Fajr with the congregation so late that they could see the sun, fearing it had risen. (3) A rational argument: delaying increases the congregation size (jama'ah) and allows more people (sleepers, weak) to join, earning greater reward. Finally, the Hanafis critique the Shafi'i hadith, pointing out that its chain includes Ibrahim ibn Zakariyya, who is classified as munkar al-hadith (rejected) by hadith critics. Thus, the Hanafi position is stronger.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isfar): Delaying Fajr until the sky is bright and daylight is clear.
التغليس (al-taghlis): Praying Fajr while it is still dark at early dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary hadith evidence the Hanafi school uses to support delaying Fajr prayer?
A) 'Pray Fajr in the first part of its time'
B) 'Make Fajr bright, for it is greater in reward'
C) 'Delay the prayer until the sun rises'
D) 'The best of deeds is prayer at its earliest time'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Fajr to isfar (brightness) for greater reward and congregation, based on authentic hadith and rational reasoning.

Recommended Times for Zuhr in Summer and Asr
Ruling on recommended prayer times with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time limits for Zuhr in summer and Asr, explain the proof from the hadith, and identify the criterion for the disliked time of Asr according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Delay Zuhr in summer; pray Asr before the sun's disc ceases to dazzle.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed us to 'cool' the Zuhr prayer in summer, delaying it until the heat subsides, and to pray Asr while the sun is still high. This lesson examines these two rulings, their proof from the Sunnah, and the precise limits set by the Hanafi school, including the sounder view on what constitutes the disliked time for Asr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two related rulings: (1) It is sunnah to delay Zuhr in summer until before the shadow equals the object (mithl), and (2) it is sunnah to pray Asr before the sun's disc changes (i.e., before it turns yellow), while delaying beyond that point is makruh tahrimi.
Both rulings are based on the same hadith and practice of the Prophet.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the prophetic hadith: 'Cool the Zuhr prayer in summer, for the intensity of heat is from the raging of Hellfire.' This is supported by the practice of the Prophet as narrated by Anas ibn Malik, who reported that the Prophet used to hasten Zuhr in winter and delay it in summer.
The imperative 'abridu' is understood as recommendation (nadb) due to the stated reason (heat).
3
Determine the limit for Zuhr delay
The text specifies that the delay for Zuhr should be such that it is prayed before the shadow of an object becomes equal to its height (al-mithl). This marks the beginning of Asr time, so Zuhr must be completed before Asr enters.
This limit ensures that Zuhr is not delayed into the time of the next prayer.
4
Determine the limit for Asr
For Asr, the recommended time is before the sun's disc changes (taghayyur al-shams), meaning while the eye can still look at the disc without dazzlement. Delaying until the sun turns yellow is makruh tahrimi.
The criterion is the disc itself, not the yellow light on the wall, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The text mentions a difference: some Hanafi scholars consider the change of light on the wall, but the sounder view (asahh) is to look at the actual disc. This affects the determination of when the disliked time begins.
The mufta bihi is the disc criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظهر الصيف لقوله عليه: "أبردوا بالظهر في الصيف، فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم"، ولما روى أنس بن مالك: أنه عليه كان يبكر الظهر - أي يعجلها - في الشتاء ويبردها في الصيف، وحد التأخير أن يصلى قبل المثل. (فتح، مستخلص ما لم تتغير [ أي الشمس بأن لا تحار العين في رؤية قرصها، والتأخير إلى التغير يكره تحريماً. (ط)] والعبرة لتغير القرص عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بأن لا تحار العين في القرص، يعني يذهب ضوءه، فلا يحصل للبصر حيرة وهو الأصح، ولا عبرة لتغير الضوء الذي يقع على الجدار، والتأخير إلى تغير الشمس يكره، أما الأداء فغير مكروه، وقيل: الأداء مكروه أيضاً. (مسكين)
And Zuhr of summer due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Cool the Zuhr prayer in summer, for the intensity of heat is from the raging of Hellfire.' And because Anas ibn Malik narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to hasten Zuhr—i.e., perform it early—in winter and cool it in summer. The limit of delay is that it be prayed before the shadow becomes like the object. (Fath, Mustakhlis) As long as it has not changed [i.e., the sun such that the eye is not dazzled in seeing its disc, and delaying until the change is makruh tahriman. (T)] And the consideration is for the change of the disc according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: that the eye is not dazzled by the disc, meaning its light goes away, so the vision does not experience dazzlement, and this is the sounder view. And there is no consideration for the change of light that falls on the wall. Delaying until the sun changes is makruh, but performing it (before the change) is not makruh; and it is said that performing it is also makruh. (Miskeen)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings: (1) It is recommended to delay Zuhr prayer in summer until the heat subsides, based on the hadith 'Cool the Zuhr, for intense heat is from Hellfire.' The practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is to hasten Zuhr in winter and delay it in summer. The delay is limited to before the shadow of an object becomes equal to its own height (mithl)—i.e., before the time of 'Asr begins. (2) For 'Asr prayer, it is recommended to perform it while the sun is still high and its disc does not dazzle the eye—i.e., before it starts to change color to yellow. Delaying 'Asr until the sun changes (turns yellow) is makruh tahriman (near-prohibited). There is a difference of opinion on whether performing 'Asr during the yellowing time is makruh or not; the sounder view according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that the criterion is the disc of the sun, not the yellow light on walls. The ruling is based on the hadith and the practice of the early Muslims.

Key Terms
المثل (al-mithl): The time when the shadow of an object equals its height, marking the end of Zuhr time.
تغير الشمس (taghayyur al-shams): The sun's disc turning yellow (beginning of disliked time for 'Asr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's guidance on timing prayers increases reward: delay Zuhr in summer, pray Asr early; the disliked time for Asr begins when the sun's disc changes.

Recommended Timing for Isha and Related Etiquette
Rulings on Isha timing and pre/post prayer etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on delaying Isha prayer and identify when delay becomes makruh tahriman.

Core Idea
Delaying Isha to one-third night is sunnah; beyond half without excuse is makruh tahriman.

This lesson clarifies the recommended and impermissible delays for Isha prayer. You will learn the exact times and the associated etiquette regarding sleep and conversation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended time
The passage states that Isha prayer should be delayed until one third of the night has passed. This is the most virtuous time.
One third of night: e.g., if night starts at 7 PM and ends at 4:30 AM, one third is about 3.5 hours after sunset.
2
Identify the permissible delay
Delaying Isha until half the night is permissible (mubah). Beyond that without excuse is problematic.
Half night is the boundary between permissible and discouraged.
3
Identify the makruh tahriman delay
Delaying Isha into the last half of the night without a valid excuse is makruh tahriman. The reason given is that the congregation decreases.
Makruh tahriman is close to haram; one should avoid it.
4
Note the associated etiquette
It is disliked (makruh) to sleep before Isha if one fears missing the congregation, and to engage in idle talk after Isha without need. Beneficial activities like Quran recitation are exempt.
Talking after Fajr prayer is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعشاء إلى الثلث: [ أي ثلث الليل والتأخير إلى النصف مباح، وإلى النصف الأخير بلا عذر مكروه تحريما. (ط)] لتقليل الجماعة. كذا في "الهداية": ويكره النوم قبل الأداء لمن يخشى فوت الجماعة، والحديث بعدها بغير حاجة، وإلا فلا، كقراءة القرآن والذكر وحكايات الصالحين ومذاكرة الفقه والحديث مع الضيف والعرس، ويكره الكلام بعد انفجار الصبح، وإذا صلى الفجر جاز له الكلام. وتأخير العشاء إلى ما زاد إلى نصف الليل، والعصر إلى وقت اصفرار الشمس، والمغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم يكره تحريما. (فتح) والوتر إلى آخر الليل لمن يثق بالانتباه، وتعجيل ظهر الشتاء والمغرب، وما فيها عين يوم غين، ويؤخر غيره فيه. (ط) أي ندب تأخيره. (ط)
And 'Isha until the third: [i.e., one third of the night, and delaying until half is permissible, and until the last half without an excuse is makruh tahriman. (T)] because the congregation decreases. Thus in al-Hidayah: It is disliked to sleep before performing (Isha) for one who fears missing the congregation, and to speak after it without need; otherwise not, such as reciting Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, and discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest or at a wedding. And it is disliked to speak after the break of dawn. And when he has prayed Fajr, speech is permissible for him. And delaying 'Isha beyond half the night, and 'Asr until the time of yellowing of the sun, and Maghrib until the stars are thickly visible is makruh tahriman. (Fath) And Witr until the last part of the night for one who trusts himself to wake up. And hastening Zuhr in winter and Maghrib. And those prayers which have an 'ayn letter in their names (i.e., 'Asr and 'Isha) on a cloudy day; and others are delayed on such a day. (T) Meaning it is recommended to delay them. (T)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings about the timing of 'Isha, Witr, and other prayers: (1) It is recommended to delay 'Isha until approximately one third of the night has passed. Delaying it until half the night is permissible (mubah), but delaying it into the last half without a valid excuse is makruh tahriman. The reason given is that the congregation may decrease if delayed too much. (2) It is disliked (makruh) to sleep before performing 'Isha if one fears missing the congregation, and to engage in idle talk after 'Isha without a valid need; however, beneficial activities like Quran recitation, dhikr, studying fiqh, and talking with guests are exempt. (3) It is makruh tahriman to delay 'Isha beyond mid-night, to delay 'Asr until the sun turns yellow, and to delay Maghrib until the stars are fully visible. (4) Witr prayer is recommended to be delayed to the last part of the night for anyone who is confident they will wake up. If not sure, it should be prayed before sleeping. (5) In winter, Zuhr should be hastened (prayed early), and Maghrib should also be hastened. (6) On cloudy days, prayers whose name contains the letter 'ayn (i.e., 'Asr and 'Isha) should be hastened, while others (Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib) should be delayed, to increase congregation and avoid missing the correct time.

Key Terms
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): The time when stars become thickly visible, marking the end of the recommended time for Maghrib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Mubah
C) Makruh tahriman
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Delay Isha to one-third night for sunnah; up to half is permissible; beyond half without excuse is makruh tahriman.

Makruh Tahriman Delays for Asr and Maghrib and Hastening in Winter
Rulings on delaying Asr and Maghrib and hastening in winter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why delaying Asr to yellowing and Maghrib to star visibility is makruh tahriman and state when to hasten these prayers.

Core Idea
Delaying Asr to yellowing and Maghrib to star visibility is makruh tahriman; hasten Zuhr in winter and Maghrib.

This lesson covers the impermissible delays for Asr and Maghrib prayers. It also addresses the opposite scenario: hastening Zuhr in winter and Maghrib (always) to avoid missing the best time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forbidden delays
The passage states that delaying Asr until the sun turns yellow (sufra) and Maghrib until the stars are thickly visible (ishtibak al-nujum) is makruh tahriman.
Sufra: sun becomes pale yellow before sunset. Ishtibak: stars appear thickly.
2
Understand the reason
These delays risk missing the prayer within its valid time or at least the most virtuous time.
3
Identify the hastening commands
The passage says to hasten Zuhr in winter and Maghrib. For Zuhr, hastening means praying at the beginning of its time in winter when days are short.
4
Note the connection
Hastening Maghrib is the opposite of delaying it to star visibility. The ruling encourages early Maghrib to avoid makruh delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعشاء إلى الثلث: [ أي ثلث الليل والتأخير إلى النصف مباح، وإلى النصف الأخير بلا عذر مكروه تحريما. (ط)] لتقليل الجماعة. كذا في "الهداية": ويكره النوم قبل الأداء لمن يخشى فوت الجماعة، والحديث بعدها بغير حاجة، وإلا فلا، كقراءة القرآن والذكر وحكايات الصالحين ومذاكرة الفقه والحديث مع الضيف والعرس، ويكره الكلام بعد انفجار الصبح، وإذا صلى الفجر جاز له الكلام. وتأخير العشاء إلى ما زاد إلى نصف الليل، والعصر إلى وقت اصفرار الشمس، والمغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم يكره تحريما. (فتح) والوتر إلى آخر الليل لمن يثق بالانتباه، وتعجيل ظهر الشتاء والمغرب، وما فيها عين يوم غين، ويؤخر غيره فيه. (ط) أي ندب تأخيره. (ط)
And 'Isha until the third: [i.e., one third of the night, and delaying until half is permissible, and until the last half without an excuse is makruh tahriman. (T)] because the congregation decreases. Thus in al-Hidayah: It is disliked to sleep before performing (Isha) for one who fears missing the congregation, and to speak after it without need; otherwise not, such as reciting Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, and discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest or at a wedding. And it is disliked to speak after the break of dawn. And when he has prayed Fajr, speech is permissible for him. And delaying 'Isha beyond half the night, and 'Asr until the time of yellowing of the sun, and Maghrib until the stars are thickly visible is makruh tahriman. (Fath) And Witr until the last part of the night for one who trusts himself to wake up. And hastening Zuhr in winter and Maghrib. And those prayers which have an 'ayn letter in their names (i.e., 'Asr and 'Isha) on a cloudy day; and others are delayed on such a day. (T) Meaning it is recommended to delay them. (T)
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings about the timing of 'Isha, Witr, and other prayers: (1) It is recommended to delay 'Isha until approximately one third of the night has passed. Delaying it until half the night is permissible (mubah), but delaying it into the last half without a valid excuse is makruh tahriman. The reason given is that the congregation may decrease if delayed too much. (2) It is disliked (makruh) to sleep before performing 'Isha if one fears missing the congregation, and to engage in idle talk after 'Isha without a valid need; however, beneficial activities like Quran recitation, dhikr, studying fiqh, and talking with guests are exempt. (3) It is makruh tahriman to delay 'Isha beyond mid-night, to delay 'Asr until the sun turns yellow, and to delay Maghrib until the stars are fully visible. (4) Witr prayer is recommended to be delayed to the last part of the night for anyone who is confident they will wake up. If not sure, it should be prayed before sleeping. (5) In winter, Zuhr should be hastened (prayed early), and Maghrib should also be hastened. (6) On cloudy days, prayers whose name contains the letter 'ayn (i.e., 'Asr and 'Isha) should be hastened, while others (Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib) should be delayed, to increase congregation and avoid missing the correct time.

Key Terms
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): The time when stars become thickly visible, marking the end of the recommended time for Maghrib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Delaying Asr prayer until the sun turns yellow is considered:
A) Sunnah
B) Mubah
C) Makruh tahriman
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Delaying Asr to yellowing and Maghrib to stars is makruh tahriman; hasten Zuhr in winter and Maghrib.

Witr Timing and Cloudy Day Prayer Scheduling
Rulings on Witr timing and cloudy day adjustments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended time for Witr and apply the rule of hastening 'Asr and 'Isha on cloudy days.

Core Idea
Witr is best delayed to last part of night if one trusts waking; on cloudy days, hasten 'Asr and 'Isha, delay others.

This lesson explains two separate but connected rulings: the timing of Witr prayer and how to adjust prayer times on cloudy days to avoid missing the correct time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Witr ruling
Witr prayer is recommended to be delayed to the last part of the night for one who is confident they will wake up. Otherwise, pray it before sleep.
Last part of night: e.g., before Fajr time.
2
Identify the cloudy day rule
On a cloudy day, prayers whose name contains the letter 'ayn ('Asr and 'Isha) should be hastened (prayed early in their time). Other prayers (Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib) should be delayed slightly.
'Ayn: عسير (Asr) and عشاء (Isha) contain ع.
3
Understand the reason
Hastening 'Asr and 'Isha on cloudy days reduces the risk of missing their exact times due to uncertainty. Delaying others increases congregation.
4
Apply the rule
In practice, an imam on a cloudy day would call 'Asr earlier than usual and 'Isha earlier than usual, but delay Fajr and Zuhr slightly if needed.

Delaying it until half the night is permissible (mubah), but delaying it into the last half without a valid excuse is makruh tahriman. The reason given is that the congregation may decrease if delayed too much. (2) It is disliked (makruh) to sleep before performing 'Isha if one fears missing the congregation, and to engage in idle talk after 'Isha without a valid need; however, beneficial activities like Quran recitation, dhikr, studying fiqh, and talking with guests are exempt. Disliked Times for Prayer: Sunrise and Zenith
Ruling on disliked times for prayer: sunrise and zenith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two disliked times for prayer mentioned in the passage (sunrise and zenith), identify which types of prayers are included, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Fajr prayer interrupted by sunrise.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise until one spear-height and at zenith from mid-day until decline is makruh tahrimi, including all prayers.

The Hanafi school identifies specific times when performing prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to explicit prophetic prohibitions. This passage focuses on two such times: sunrise (until the sun rises approximately one or two spear lengths) and zenith (the time when the sun is at its meridian, from mid-day until it begins to decline). The prohibition applies to all types of prayers—obligatory (ada and qada), supererogatory, funeral prayers, and prostrations of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah)—with some exceptions like sajdah al-shukr. Understanding these times and their nuances is essential for ensuring the validity of one's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disliked times
Locate the terms 'عند الطلوع' (at sunrise) and 'عند الاستواء' (at zenith) in the text. Note that sunrise here means from the moment the sun begins to rise until it rises one or two spear heights; zenith means the period from mid-day until the sun begins its decline (zawal).
The exact moment of zawal (decline) is not disliked by consensus.
2
Determine which prayers are included
The text explicitly includes all prayers (أداء وقضاء أي صلاة كانت), sajdah al-tilawah, sajdah al-sahw, and funeral prayer. It excludes sajdah al-shukr except when performed in a time when nafl is disliked.
Sajdah al-shukr is only disliked if done after a prayer in a disliked time; otherwise it is not disliked.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on Fajr interrupted by sunrise
The text states: 'فلو طلعت الشمس، وهو في صلاة الفجر فسدت' (if the sun rises while he is in Fajr prayer, it becomes invalid). This is Abu Hanifa's view. Then it mentions Abu Yusuf's view: the prayer does not become invalid; one waits and completes after sunrise.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's view that the prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنع عن الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة عند الطلوع والاستواء. أي منع تحريم للنهي. (ط) عن الصلاة: أداء وقضاء أي صلاة كانت. (ع) وسجدة التلاوة وكذا سجدة السهو بخلاف سجدة الشكر ، لكن في النهر الفائق [١١٥/١]: يكره أن يسجد شكراً بعد الصلاة في الوقت الذي يكره النفل فيه، ولا يكره في غيره، وفي "المعراج": وأما ما يفعل عقب الصلوات من السجدة فمكروه إجماعاً؛ لأن العوام يعتقدون أنها واجبة أو سنة. (فتح) وصلاة الجنازة: التي حضرت في الوقت الصحيح. (رمز الحقائق: ٤٥/١) عند الطلوع: بأن لم ترتفع قدر رمح أو رمحين، فلو طلعت الشمس، وهو في صلاة الفجر فسدت، وعن أبي يوسف أنها لا تفسد ، ولكن يصبر حتى إذا ارتفعت الشمس أتم صلاته. والاستواء قالوا: الوقت المكروه عند انتصاف النهار إلى أن تزول الشمس، ولا يخفى أن زوال الشمس إنما هو عقب انتصاف النهار، وفي هذا القدر من الزمان لا يمكن أداء الصلاة، فلعل المراد أنه لا تجوز الصلاة بحيث تقع تحريمتها في هذا الزمان، والتعبير بالاستواء أولى من التعبير بوقت الزوال؛ لعدم كراهة الصلاة وقت الزوال إجماعا. (فتح)
And he forbade (the prohibition is tahrimi due to the prohibition) prayer, recital of sajdah (tilawah), and funeral prayer at sunrise and at zenith. (T) Concerning prayer: both performance and make-up, any prayer it may be. (Ayn) And sajdah al-tilawah, and likewise sajdah al-sahw, unlike sajdah al-shukr. However, in al-Nahr al-Faiq [1/115]: It is disliked to perform sajdah shukr after prayer during a time when supererogatory prayer is disliked, and it is not disliked at other times. In al-Mi'raj: As for what is done after prayers of sajdah, it is disliked by consensus; because the common people believe it is obligatory or sunnah. (Fath) And funeral prayer that is attended at the correct time. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 45/1) At sunrise: meaning the sun has not risen the height of a spear or two spears. If the sun rises while he is in Fajr prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. From Abu Yusuf: it does not become invalid, but he waits until the sun has risen and then completes his prayer. And at zenith: they said: the disliked time is at mid-day until the sun declines. It is not hidden that the declining of the sun occurs right after mid-day, and in this amount of time it is not possible to perform prayer. Perhaps the intent is that prayer is not permissible such that its takbirat al-ihram falls in this time. And the expression 'istiwai' (zenith) is better than the expression 'time of zawal' (decline); because there is no dislike for prayer at the time of zawal by consensus. (Fath)
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage discusses the times when prayer is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). These are: (1) At sunrise, specifically from when the sun begins to rise until it has risen approximately one or two spear lengths above the horizon. (2) At zenith (istiwai), when the sun is at its meridian, from mid-day until it begins to decline (zawal). The prohibition applies to all prayers, including obligatory (ada and qada), supererogatory, sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation), and funeral prayer (janazah), except that sajdah al-shukr is exempted under certain conditions (disliked only if done in a time when nafl is disliked). There is an intra-Hanafi difference: if the sun rises during Fajr prayer, Abu Hanifa rules the prayer is invalid, while Abu Yusuf says it is not invalid; the person waits and completes after the sun rises. For funeral prayer, it is disliked only if the body is present during the hated time; if not, it can be performed later. The rationale is that the prohibition is based on clear prohibitions (nahy) from the Prophet, thus the ruling is tahrimi.

Key Terms
الطلوع (al-tulu'): The time of sunrise until the sun rises one or two spear heights.
الاستواء (al-istiwai): The time when the sun is at its zenith, from mid-day until decline (zawal).
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation upon reciting a verse of sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the Fajr prayer if the sun rises while one is still in the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated after sunrise
B) The prayer is valid and one should continue
C) The prayer becomes invalid only if one intentionally delays
D) One stops and completes after the sun rises (according to Abu Yusuf)

Key Takeaway
Prayer is prohibitively disliked at sunrise and zenith; if sunrise occurs during Fajr, the prayer is invalid (Abu Hanifa).

The Three Prohibited Times for Prayer: Hanafi Ruling and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on three prohibited times for prayer with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times, apply the Hanafi ruling on qada and nafl in those times, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Prayer is prohibited at sunrise, zenith, and sunset; missed obligations cannot be made up, but voluntary prayers are merely disliked.

The passage before us is a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the three times when prayer is prohibited. The Hanafi school, based on a hadith from Uqba ibn Amir, holds that no prayer should be initiated in these times, with specific exceptions for funeral prayers and sajda tilawa (which are valid but disliked). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, permitting qada of missed prayers and voluntary prayers in Mecca. Understanding this dispute sharpens our appreciation of how different schools weigh conflicting hadiths and the concept of deficiency (nuqsan) in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three times and primary evidence
The times are sunrise, zenith (solar noon), and sunset. The primary proof is the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir (Muslim) which prohibits prayer and burying the dead (meaning funeral prayer) in these times.
The hadith uses the phrase 'nahana' (prohibited us), which in Hanafi usul indicates prohibition (tahrim).
2
Understand the Hanafi ruling: hierarchy of prohibitions
The prohibition applies differently: qada of missed fard/wajib is absolutely impermissible (haram); voluntary (nafl) prayers are permissible but disliked (makruh tanzihi); funeral prayer and sajda tilawa are valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi) because they become obligated in a deficient state when commenced.
Key distinction: complete obligations cannot be performed deficiently; incomplete obligations can.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counter-evidence
Al-Shafi'i cites two hadiths: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer... let him pray it when he remembers' (for qada) and 'O Banu Abd Manaf! Do not prevent anyone from circumambulating and praying at any hour' (for nafl in Mecca).
These seem to permit prayer at any time, conflicting with the general prohibition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the general prohibition is not overridden by these specific hadiths. The Banu Abd Manaf hadith is an exception for them alone, and the 'sleeping' hadith applies only to the individual who missed a prayer, but does not lift the prohibition for others in general.
The principle: 'al-amm yurid bi-'umumihi' (the general remains general) unless a clear specification (takhsis) is proven.
5
Identify the exception for Asr of the same day
Asr of the same day is valid just before sunset because its time is deficient (end of day), so it is performed as it became obligatory. Fajr of the same day is invalidated by sunrise because Fajr time is complete.
This is based on the concept of 'kamaal' (completeness) vs 'nuqsan' (deficiency) of the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة والغروب إلا عصر يومه. والغروب: أي لا يجوز الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة في هذه الأوقات الثلاثة؛ لحديث عقبة بن عامر أنه قال: ثلاثة أوقات نهانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نصلي فيها، وأن نقبر فيها موتانا عند طلوع الشمس حتى ترتفع، وعند زوالها حتى تزول، وحين تضيف للغروب حتى تغرب رواه مسلم والمراد من قوله: "أن نقبر" صلاة الجنازة؛ إذ الدفن غير مكروه، وقال الشافعي: لا يكره قضاء الفوائت في هذه الأوقات؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها فإن ذلك وقتها"، وكذا النوافل عنده لا يكره في هذه الساعات بمكة؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "يا بني عبد مناف! لا تمنعوا أحداً طاف بهذا البيت، وصلّى في أي ساعة شاء من ليل أو نهار"، والجواب عنه: أن الشرع نهي عن الصلاة في هذه الأوقات، واستثنى بني عبد مناف وعن أبي يوسف: إباحة النفل يوم الجمعة وقت الاستواء، والحجة عليه ما روينا، وسجدة التلاوة في معنى الصلاة؛ ولذلك نهي عنها، والمراد بالنهي عن صلاة الجنازة أو سجدة التلاوة الكراهة، حتى لو صلاها أو سجدها أجزأته؛ لأنها وجبت ناقصة بالشروع في الوقت المكروه فأديت كذلك، وأما قضاء الفوائت فلا يجوز أصلاً؛ لأنها شرعت كاملة، فلا يؤدى بالنقصان. (مستخلص) واعلم أن التطوع في هذه الأوقات يجوز ويكره، ولا يجوز قضاء الفرض والواجب الفائت فيها كسجدة تلاوة وجبت بتلاوة في وقت غير مكروه وكوتر، فالمنع يتناول الكراهة وعدم الجواز وفي البحر: أن يصلي على الجنازة إذا حضرت في الأوقات الثلاثة، ولا يؤخرها؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "ثلاث لا يؤخرن جنازة أتت" الحديث؛ ولأنها أديت كما وجبت؛ إذ الوجوب بالحضور، وهو أفضل، والتأخير مكروه لما ذكرنا والظاهر أن ما ذكروا من الكراهة محمول على ما إذا حضرت في وقت كامل وصلى عليها في وقت مكروه، وكذا المراد بسجدة التلاوة إذا تلاها قبل هذه الأوقات؛ لأنها وجبت كاملة فلا تتأدى بالنقصان، وأما إذا تلا فيها جاز أداؤها من غير كراهة، لكن الأفضل التأخير إلى الوقت المستحب؛ لأنها لا تفوت بالتأخير. (فتح) إلا عصر يومه: [استثناء من منع، فإن عصر يومه تصح قبيل الغروب؛ ولأنه أداها كما وجبت حتى لا يجوز عصر أمسه؛ لأن الكامل لا يتأدى بالناقص. (ط، ف، ع)] فإنه يجوز، وأما فجر يومه فيبطل بالطلوع، والفرق بينهما أن السبب في العصر آخر الوقت، وهو وقت التغير ناقص، فإذا أداها فيه أداها كما وجبت، ووقت الفجر كله كامل فوجبت كاملة، فتبطل بطرء الطلوع (هدايه)
The times in which prayer is disliked: sunset except the Asr of that day. Commentary on sunset: It is not permissible to pray, perform sajda tilawa, or funeral prayer in these three times; due to the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir that he said: The Messenger of Allah forbade us from praying in three times and from burying our dead in them: at sunrise until it rises high, at zenith until it declines, and when it inclines towards setting until it sets. Narrated by Muslim. The meaning of 'we bury' is funeral prayer, as burial is not disliked. Al-Shafi'i said: Making up missed prayers is not disliked in these times, due to his statement: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers, for that is its time.' Similarly, voluntary prayers in his view are not disliked in these hours in Mecca, due to his statement: 'O Banu Abd Manaf! Do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour he wishes, night or day.' The response: The Shari'a prohibited prayer in these times, and made an exception for Banu Abd Manaf. From Abu Yusuf: permission for voluntary prayer on Friday at the time of (solar) noon; the proof against him is what we narrated. Sajda tilawa is analogous to prayer, so it is prohibited. The intent of the prohibition of funeral prayer or sajda tilawa is dislike (karaha), such that if one performs them, they suffice, because they become obligated incomplete by commencing in a disliked time and were performed accordingly. As for making up missed prayers, it is absolutely impermissible, because they are legislated as complete and cannot be performed deficiently. (Mukhtasar) Know that voluntary prayers in these times are permissible but disliked, and it is not permissible to make up missed obligatory or wajib prayers in them, like sajda tilawa obligated by recitation in a non-disliked time, and witr. So the prohibition encompasses both dislike and impermissibility. In al-Bahr: One should pray the funeral prayer if it occurs in the three times and not delay it, due to his statement: 'Three things are not to be delayed: a funeral that has come...' and because it is performed as it became obligatory, as obligation occurs by presence, and it is better; delaying is disliked as we mentioned. Apparently, what they mentioned of dislike is interpreted as when it occurred in complete time and he prayed in a disliked time. Similarly for sajda tilawa if he recited before these times, because it became obligatory complete so it cannot be performed deficiently. But if he recited in (these times), performing it is permissible without dislike, but it is better to delay to a preferred time because it is not lost by delay. (Fath) Except Asr of that day: [exception from prohibition, for the Asr of that day is valid close to sunset; because he performed it as it became obligatory, so the Asr of the previous day is not valid, because the complete cannot be performed deficiently. (T, F, A)] So it is permissible. As for the Fajr of that day, it is invalidated by sunrise. The difference is that the reason for Asr is the end of its time, which is a time of change that is deficient, so when he performs it in it, he performs it as it became obligatory. But the time of Fajr is entirely complete, so it becomes obligatory complete, thus it is invalidated by the occurrence of sunrise. (Hidaya)
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the three prohibited times for prayer. The text begins by stating the ruling: it is not permissible to pray salah, perform sajda tilawa, or pray janaza in these three times. The primary proof is a hadith from Muslim narrated by Uqba ibn Amir, listing sunrise, zenith, and sunset as times of prohibition. The text clarifies that 'burying our dead' means funeral prayer, not burial itself. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that making up missed prayers is not disliked at these times, citing the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer... let him pray it when he remembers, for that is its time,' and also permits voluntary prayers in Mecca at any hour based on a hadith about Banu Abd Manaf. The Hanafi response is that the Shari'a prohibition overrides these exceptions, and the hadith about Banu Abd Manaf is specific to them. Abu Yusuf's view allowing voluntary prayer on Friday at noon is rejected with the same proof. The text then explains that the prohibition for janaza and sajda tilawa is only karaha (dislike), so if performed, they are valid. However, making up missed obligatory prayers is absolutely impermissible in these times because they are complete obligations and cannot be performed deficiently. Voluntary prayers are permissible but disliked. A further distinction is made: if a janaza occurs in a prohibited time, it should be prayed immediately because presence in itself creates an obligation, but it is still disliked. Similarly, sajda tilawa if recited before the prohibited time must be performed earlier to avoid deficiency; if recited in the prohibited time, it may be performed without dislike but it is better to delay. Finally, the text addresses the exception for Asr of the same day: it is valid if performed just before sunset because it is performed as it became obligatory (the obligation was deficient due to end-of-time). In contrast, Fajr of that day is invalidated by sunrise because Fajr time is complete. The key point is that a complete obligation cannot be performed deficiently.

Key Terms
الوقت المكروه (al-waqt al-makruh): Time in which prayer is disliked or prohibited.
قضاء الفوائت (qada' al-fawa'it): Making up missed obligatory prayers.
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary (supererogatory) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for making up a missed fajr prayer during the time of sunrise?
A) Permissible and not disliked
B) Permissible but disliked
C) Impermissible and invalid
D) Permissible only in Mecca

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits qada of missed prayers in the three prohibited times, while allowing janaza and sajda tilawa with dislike, except the current day's Asr which is valid.

The Absolute Prohibition of Nafl After Fajr and Asr
Ruling on prohibition of voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
No voluntary prayer after Fajr or Asr, even with a cause — the general hadith overrides all exceptions.

The time after Fajr and Asr prayers is sacred and reserved for dhikr, not voluntary worship. While Imam al-Shafi'i permits some nafl prayers if they have a specific cause, the Hanafi school adheres strictly to the general prohibition of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This lesson will walk you through the evidence and the crux of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: all voluntary prayers (nafl) are prohibited after Fajr and Asr, whether or not they have a cause.
The ruling is makruh tahrimi; the prayer itself is invalid if performed.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that voluntary prayers with a specific cause (like tahiyyat al-masjid, tawaf rak'ahs, or vowed prayers) are permissible and not disliked after these times.
Shafi'i makes an exception based on other hadiths.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i relies on hadiths such as the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying two rak'ahs after tawaf at any time, and the general recommendation to pray tahiyyat al-masjid.
These hadiths suggest that a cause legitimizes the prayer.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school insists that the general hadith 'No prayer after Fajr until sunrise, and no prayer after Asr until sunset' (Bukhari, Muslim) is general and specific; it overrides any specific hadith that might permit. The cause does not lift the prohibition.
The only exception is the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah, which are prayed before Fajr, not after.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, a person cannot pray tahiyyat al-masjid or tawaf rak'ahs after Fajr/Asr; in the Shafi'i school, they can.
This affects daily worship in mosques near the Haram or after Fajr congregations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن التنفل: أي مطلقاً سواء كان له سبب أو لا، وقال الشافعي: إن التنقل بعدهما إذا كان له سبب جائز بلا كراهة وأراد به ركعتي الطواف وتحية المسجد والسنن الموقتة والمنذورة، أما ابتداء النفل فإنه أيضاً عنده مكروه. (فتح) بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر أي وبعد صلاته لقوله عليه: "لا صلاة بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس، ولا صلاة بعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وهو حجة على الشافعي في تجويزه النفل الذي له سبب كتحية المسجد وركعتي الطواف. (ع)
And concerning voluntary prayer: meaning absolutely, whether it has a cause or not. Al-Shafi'i said: voluntary prayer after them (Fajr and Asr) if it has a cause is permissible without dislike, and he meant by it the two rak'ahs of tawaf, greeting the mosque, and the timed and vowed sunnahs. As for initiating voluntary prayer, in his view it is also disliked. (Fath) After Fajr and Asr prayers: meaning after performing them, due to his statement: 'No prayer after Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr prayer until the sun sets.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. It is a proof against al-Shafi'i in his allowing voluntary prayer that has a cause, like greeting the mosque and the two rak'ahs of tawaf. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of voluntary prayers after the Fajr and Asr prayers. The text clarifies that the prohibition is absolute—whether the voluntary prayer has a cause (like tawaf or mosque greeting) or not. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that voluntary prayers with a cause are permissible without dislike, citing examples like the two rak'ahs after tawaf and tahiyyat al-masjid. However, the primary Hanafi proof is the hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim: 'No prayer after Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr prayer until the sun sets.' This general prohibition overrides any specific cause. The commentator (Ayni) states that this hadith is a proof against al-Shafi'i. Note that the sunnah of Fajr itself is excluded as it is prayed before Fajr prayer; after Fajr prayer, no voluntary prayer is allowed.

Key Terms
التنفل (al-tanafful): Voluntary prayer (nafl); supererogatory worship beyond the obligatory.
النفل الذي له سبب (al-nafl alladhi lahu sabab): Voluntary prayer that has a specific cause, such as greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid), the two rak'ahs after tawaf, or a vowed prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying tahiyyat al-masjid after the Fajr prayer?
A) Permissible because it has a cause
B) Disliked but valid
C) Prohibited and not valid
D) Permissible only in Mecca

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that no voluntary prayer is valid after Fajr or Asr, based on the general prohibition in the hadith, rejecting the Shafi'i exception for prayers with a cause.

Prohibition of Voluntary Prayer After Fajr
Ruling on prohibiting more than two rak'ahs after Fajr time begins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayer after Fajr time and apply the exceptions (sunnah of Fajr and qada).

Core Idea
After Fajr, no voluntary prayer except the two sunnah rak'ahs and missed obligatory prayers.

The Prophet ﷺ emphatically restricted prayer after dawn: only two rak'ahs are allowed. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the exception for making up missed prayers. We also explore a common boundary case: what if you started a nafl before Fajr?

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing any voluntary prayer (other than the two sunnah rak'ahs) after the time of Fajr enters. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's statement: 'When dawn breaks, there is no prayer except two rak'ahs' (Tabarani). Another hadith adds: 'Let the present inform the absent: indeed, no prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs.'
The hadith is ahad, but strong in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative negation 'لا صلاة' indicates a prohibition of all prayers. The exception 'إلا ركعتين' specifically allows the two sunnah rak'ahs. This proves that only these two rak'ahs are permitted after Fajr.
The Prophet's own practice confirms he never added more.
4
Note the exceptions
The prohibition applies to voluntary prayers (nafl) only. Making up missed obligatory prayers (qada) is not included and is permissible at all times.
Also, the two sunnah rak'ahs are explicitly exempted.
5
Apply to a boundary case
If one started a nafl prayer before Fajr and Fajr entered, the correct view is: he completes that nafl does not stand for the sunnah of Fajr, because the nafl was started unintentionally (before Fajr).
He does not cut the nafl, nor add the sunnah afterwards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بأكثر من سنة الفجر : لقوله علي: "ليبلغ شاهدكم غائبكم، ألا ! لا صلاة بعد الصبح إلا ركعتين"؛ ولأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يزد عليهما مع حرصه على الصلاة، ولو شرع في النفل قبل طلوع الفجر ثم طلع، فالأصح أنه لا يقوم عن سنة الفجر، ولا يقطعه؛ لأن الشروع فيه كان لا . عن قصد. (فتح) سنة الفجر : لقوله علية : "إذا طلع الفجر لا صلاة إلا ركعتين"، رواه الطبراني والمراد من الصلاة النفل، فيجوز قضاء الفوائت. (مسكين)
More than the sunnah of Fajr: due to his statement: 'Let the present inform the absent: indeed, no prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs.' And because the Prophet did not add to them despite his eagerness for prayer. If one commenced a voluntary prayer before Fajr time and then Fajr occurred, the correct view is that he does not stand up for the sunnah of Fajr, nor does he cut it off, because the commencement was not intentional. (Fath) Sunnah of Fajr: due to his statement: 'When dawn breaks, there is no prayer except two rak'ahs' narrated by Tabarani. The intended meaning of 'prayer' is voluntary, so it is permissible to make up missed prayers. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage explains the prohibition of voluntary prayers beyond the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr after the time of Fajr has begun. The proof is a hadith: 'No prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs.' Additionally, the Prophet's practice confirms he never prayed more than two. If someone had started a nafl prayer before Fajr time and then Fajr entered, the correct view is that he does not stand up for the sunnah of Fajr separately nor does he cut the existing nafl; instead he completes it and does not add the sunnah, because the nafl was started unintentionally (i.e., before Fajr time). The text also clarifies that the prohibition applies to voluntary prayers (nafl), not to qada of missed obligatory prayers, as qada is permissible because it is not included in the prohibition.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before Fajr prayer.
قضاء الفوائت (qada' al-fawa'it): Making up missed obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Cut the prayer and pray sunnah of Fajr
B) Complete the voluntary prayer and do not pray sunnah of Fajr
C) Continue the voluntary prayer and then pray sunnah of Fajr
D) Abandon both prayers

Key Takeaway
After Fajr time, only the two sunnah rak'ahs are allowed for nafl; qada of missed prayers is also permissible.

Prohibition of Voluntary Prayer Before Maghrib
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on voluntary prayer before Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits voluntary prayer before Maghrib and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Delaying an obligatory prayer for a voluntary one is prohibited in the Hanafi school.

This short but sharp passage from al-Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a key practical dispute: may one pray voluntary (nafl) rak'ahs after sunset but before the Maghrib fard? The Hanafi ruling is a firm prohibition, rooted in the principle of avoiding delay of an obligation. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, holds it to be an established sunnah. Understanding the basis of each position sharpens our ability to weigh proofs and prioritise obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from the text: voluntary prayer before Maghrib is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The reason given is ta'khir al-maghrib — delaying the obligatory Maghrib.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The text mentions Imam al-Shafi'i directly. Note his position: two rak'ahs before Maghrib are sunnah, i.e., recommended.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Although not quoted in this passage, the Shafi'i proof is based on hadith reports that the Prophet ﷺ prayed two rak'ahs before Maghrib. Consider how such a practice could be classified as sunnah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is implicit: the delay of Maghrib is so serious that it overrides any general recommendation for voluntary prayer. Moreover, the time of Maghrib is very short, and any voluntary act risks missing the fard.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi will not pray any nafl after sunset until after Maghrib; a Shafi'i may pray two rak'ahs. This affects mosque practice and personal observance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل المغرب: أي بعد غروب الشمس؛ لما فيه من تأخير المغرب، وقال الشافعي: يصلى ركعتين قبل المغرب وهي سنة عنده. (ع)
And before Maghrib: meaning after sunset; due to what it entails of delaying Maghrib. Al-Shafi'i said: one prays two rak'ahs before Maghrib, and it is sunnah in his view. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This brief passage addresses the voluntary prayer before Maghrib. The Hanafi ruling is that it is prohibited (makruh) because it delays the performance of the obligatory Maghrib prayer, which should be prayed immediately after sunset. Imam al-Shafi'i considers two rak'ahs before Maghrib to be a sunnah. The Hanafi position is based on the principle of avoiding delay of an obligatory prayer with supererogatory acts.

Key Terms
تأخير المغرب (ta'khir al-maghrib): Delaying the Maghrib prayer past its earliest time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Maghrib is a very short time.
B) Because it delays the obligatory Maghrib prayer.
C) Because it is not mentioned in any hadith.
D) Because it is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits voluntary prayer before Maghrib because delaying an obligation is a more significant consideration than performing a supererogatory act.

Prohibition of Prayer During the Khutbah
Ruling on prohibition of any prayer during the khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which types of khutbah prohibit prayer and explain the rationale that listening is wajib.

Core Idea
No prayer—sunnah or nafl—during any khutbah, because listening is wajib.

This passage expands the prohibition of prayer beyond Friday khutbah to all sermons. It emphasizes that during any khutbah—whether for Friday, Eid, rain, Hajj, Quran completion, or Nikah—performing any prayer is prohibited. The reason is that listening to the khutbah is obligatory (wajib), and engaging in prayer distracts from that obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
The text prohibits any prayer—whether sunnah (e.g., tahiyyat al-masjid) or nafl—during the khutbah.
The Arabic 'سواء كانت سنة أو نفلاً' makes it absolute.
2
List the types of khutbah covered
The passage enumerates: Friday, Eid, rain (istisqa), Hajj, completion of Quran (khatm), and marriage (nikah). It then says 'سائر الخطب' (all other khutbahs) are included.
So it is not limited to Friday.
3
Understand the rationale
Listening to all khutbahs is wajib. Prayer distracts from that wajib act, hence the prohibition.
The prohibition is to prevent distraction from an obligation.
4
Note the hukm level
The Hanafi school classifies this as makruh tahrimi—close to haram, but the prayer itself is still valid.
However, it is sinful to perform it.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Some schools allow sunnah prayers (e.g., tahiyyat al-masjid) during khutbah. Hanafi strictness is based on making listening wajib.
Students should be aware of this ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و وقت الخطبة أي مطلقاً . سواء كانت سنة أو نفلاً، وسواء كانت خطبة جمعة أو عيد أو استسقاء أو حج أو ختم قرآن أو نكاح، والاستماع إلى سائر الخطب واجب، فيشتغل عن الاستماع. (فتح)
And the time of the khutbah: meaning absolutely, whether it is sunnah or voluntary, and whether it is the khutbah of Friday, Eid, rain, Hajj, completion of Quran, or marriage. Listening to all khutbahs is obligatory, and prayer distracts from listening. (Fath)
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that during any khutbah (sermon), it is prohibited to pray any prayer, whether obligatory (sunnah) or voluntary. The prohibition applies to all types of khutbah: Friday, Eid, rain prayer, Hajj, completion of Quran, Nikah, etc. The reason is that listening to the khutbah is obligatory (wajib), and performing a prayer distracts from that obligation. Therefore, one should refrain from praying and focus on the sermon.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): Sermon given by the preacher, on Friday or other occasions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
No prayer—whether sunnah or nafl—during any khutbah, because listening is wajib.

Prohibition of Combining Two Prayers in One Time Without Excuse
Ruling on prohibition of combining two prayers in one time without a valid excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on combining prayers and contrast it with the Shafi'i position, including the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Combining two prayers in one time is prohibited except at Arafa and Muzdalifa; only virtual combining (jam' suri) is allowed for excuses.

Combining obligatory prayers outside their appointed times is a serious matter in Hanafi fiqh. This lesson examines the ruling on jam' (combining) between two prayers within one time, focusing on the inter-madhhab disagreement with the Shafi'i school. You will learn the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and understand why only virtual combining (jam' suri) is permitted for excuses like travel, rain, or illness. We will also explore the practical difference this makes for a traveler or pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: actual combining (jam' haqiqi) of two prayers in one time is prohibited (haram) except at Arafa and Muzdalifa. Virtual combining (jam' suri) — delaying the first to its end and advancing the second to its beginning — is permissible.
The prohibition is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that actual combining is permissible due to travel, rain, or similar excuses. He cites the Prophet's action in Tabuk when he combined Zuhr and Asr.
Malik and Ahmad extend the excuse to mud (mire).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the Prophet (ﷺ) combined Zuhr and Asr during the expedition of Tabuk. This appears to be actual combining.
The Hanafi school must address this apparent contradiction.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the Tabuk incident as virtual combining (jam' suri): the Prophet prayed Zuhr at the very end of its time and Asr at the very beginning, so no time overlap occurred. This preserves the general prohibition.
Also, a narration from Ibn Mas'ud says combining without excuse is a major sin.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a Hanafi traveler cannot pray Zuhr and Asr together in the time of one; he must perform each in its own time through virtual combining. A Shafi'i traveler may combine them actually.
The text allows a Hanafi to follow the Shafi'i school for combining while traveling, provided he follows all Shafi'i requirements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن الجمع بين الصلاتين لما روي عن ابن مسعود: والذي لا إله غيره ما صلى عليها صلاة قط إلا لوقتها إلا صلاتين، جمع بين الظهر والعصر بعرفة، وبين المغرب والعشاء بجمع، فما ورد عنه عليها مما يقتضي جواز الجمع بين صلاتين لعذر مرض ونحوه محمول على الجمع الصوري بأن أخر الأولى وعجل الثانية، وقال الشافعي: يجمع بين الظهر والعصر، وبين المغرب والعشاء بعذر السفر والمطر، له أنه عليها جمع بين الظهر والعصر في سفر تبوك وبين المغرب والعشاء، ولنا: ما روينا، وأيضاً قوله علي: "من جمع بين الصلاتين فقد أتى بابا من الكبائر"، وتأويل ما رواه أنه عليها جمع بين الظهر والعصر فعلاً لا وقتاً بأن أخر الظهر إلى آخر وقتها وأدى العصر في أول وقتها، وقال مالك: يجوز الجمع لوحل أيضاً، وعن أحمد: مثلهما، واحترز بقوله: "في وقت" عن الجمع بينهما فعلا كما ذكرنا، وبقوله: " بعذر" عن الجمع في عرفة ومزدلفة، فإن ذلك يجوز وإن لم يكن فيه عذر ، فإن جمع في غيرهما فسد لو قدم الفرض على وقته وحرم على عكسه، ولا بأس بتقليد الشافعي للمسافر لاسيما للحاج بشرط أن يلتزم جميع ما يوجبه ذلك الإمام؛ لما أن الحكم المختلط من المذهبين باطل بالإجماع. (فتح) بعذر كسفر أو مطر أو وحل أو مرض رمز الحقائق: ٤٦/١]
And concerning combining two prayers: due to what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: By Him besides whom there is no god, he (the Prophet) never prayed any prayer outside its time except two prayers: he combined Zuhr and Asr at Arafa, and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifa. So whatever is reported from him that implies the permissibility of combining two prayers due to an excuse like illness and the like is interpreted as virtual combining (jam' suri): by delaying the first and praying the second earlier. Al-Shafi'i said: one combines Zuhr and Asr, and Maghrib and Isha, due to the excuse of travel and rain. His proof is that he combined Zuhr and Asr in the expedition of Tabuk, and Maghrib and Isha. Our proof is what we narrated, and also his statement: 'Whoever combines two prayers has committed a major sin.' The interpretation of what he narrated is that he combined Zuhr and Asr in action, not in time, by delaying Zuhr to its end and performing Asr at its beginning. Malik said: combining is also permissible due to mud (mire). And from Ahmad: similar to them. He (the author) restricted by saying 'in one time' to exclude combining them in action as we mentioned, and by saying 'with an excuse' to exclude combining at Arafa and Muzdalifa, for that is permissible even without an excuse. So if one combines elsewhere, then if he advanced the prayer before its time, it is invalid, and if he delayed, it is forbidden. And there is no harm in a traveler, especially a pilgrim, making taqlid of al-Shafi'i, on condition that he adheres to all that which that imam requires; because a ruling mixed from two schools is invalid by consensus. (Fath) With an excuse such as travel, rain, mud, or illness. Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 46/1.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of combining two obligatory prayers in one time (jam' fi al-waqt) without a legitimate excuse. The Hanafi school holds that such combining is generally prohibited, except at Arafa and Muzdalifa during Hajj. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet never prayed outside its time except at Arafa and Muzdalifa. Any reports suggesting permissibility for illness etc. are interpreted as 'virtual combining' (jam' suri): delaying the first prayer to the end of its time and bringing the second forward to the beginning of its time, so that both are prayed within their own time windows. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i allows actual combining (jam' haqiqi) for travel and rain, citing the Prophet's action in Tabuk. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's action was jam' suri, not actual. The prohibition is strong; combining without excuse is a major sin. Imam Malik allows combining for mud, and Ahmad similarly. The text also notes that a Hanafi may follow the Shafi'i school for combining when traveling, especially the pilgrim, provided he follows all aspects of the Shafi'i ruling, because mixing parts of different schools is invalid. The allowed excuses are travel, rain, mud, and illness.

Key Terms
الجمع الصوري (al-jam' al-suri): Virtual combining: delaying the first prayer to the end of its time and bringing the second forward to the beginning of its time.
الجمع الفعلي (al-jam' al-fi'li): Actual combining: performing both prayers in one time without regard to their original times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on combining Zuhr and Asr prayers due to heavy rain?
A) Permissible by actual combining
B) Permissible only by virtual combining (jam' suri)
C) Not permissible at all
D) Permissible only if traveling

Key Takeaway
Combining two prayers in one time is prohibited (haram) except at Arafa and Muzdalifa; only virtual combining (jam' suri) is allowed for excuses like travel, rain, or illness.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Times When Prayer is Disliked (Awqat al-Karahah)
States four disliked prayer times with proofs and inter-school disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four times when prayer is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school, cite the hadith proofs for each, and explain the Hanafi position on combining two prayers, including the response to the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Prayer at four times is makruh tahrimi; combining prayers without excuse is impermissible except at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah.

This lesson examines the times when performing prayer is considered disliked (makruh) in the Hanafi school, ranging from after Fajr to during the khutbah. We will explore the textual proofs from the Sunnah and the reasoning behind each ruling. Additionally, we will analyze the significant inter-madhhab dispute on whether two obligatory prayers can be combined due to travel or rain, and how the Hanafi school defends its strict position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four disliked times
Read the passage and list the four situations where prayer is disliked according to the Hanafi school. Note which prayers are affected (obligatory, sunnah, nafl) at each time.
The four times are: (1) after Fajr beyond two rak'ahs, (2) before Maghrib, (3) during the khutbah, (4) combining two prayers without an excuse.
2
Locate the dalil for each
For each disliked time, identify the specific hadith or rational proof cited in the passage. For after Fajr: the hadith 'no prayer after subh except two rak'ahs' and the Prophet's practice. For before Maghrib: it delays Maghrib. For khutbah: listening is obligatory. For combining: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the hadith 'whoever combines has committed a major sin'.
The hadith for after Fajr is explicitly quoted.
3
Note the inter-madhhab disagreements
Al-Shafi'i holds that two rak'ahs before Maghrib are sunnah, and that combining prayers is permitted for travel and rain. Malik adds mud. Identify how the Hanafi school responds to each claim.
The response includes interpreting the Prophet's actions as 'formal combination' (jam' suri) and restricting combination to 'Arafah and Muzdalifah.
4
Analyze the key concept of 'jam' suri'
Understand the Hanafi interpretation of the reports where the Prophet appeared to combine: they explain that he delayed the first prayer to the end of its time and performed the second at the beginning, so that each was in its actual time. This is formal combination, not real combination.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i, who accepts real combination (jam' haqiqi).
5
Determine the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
A Hanafi traveler cannot combine prayers even with hardship, whereas a Shafi'i can. However, the passage permits a Hanafi to follow al-Shafi'i on the condition of adhering to all his rulings. What implications does this have for a Hanafi seeking a concession?
Mixing madhhabs arbitrarily is invalid; one must follow a single madhhab fully when adopting its concession.

Source Text
