(فتح) بعذر كسفر أو مطر أو وحل أو مرض رمز الحقائق: ٤٦/١]
Book of Prayer. Times when prayer is disliked: more than the Sunnah of Fajr, before Maghrib, time of the khutbah, and combining two prayers at a time without excuse. One: more than the Sunnah of Fajr: due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Let the present inform the absent: no prayer after the dawn (subh) except two rak'ahs.' And because the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not add more than them despite his eagerness for prayer. And if one begins a supererogatory prayer before dawn breaks, and then it breaks, the soundest view is that he does not stand for the Sunnah of Fajr, nor does he cut it; because beginning it was without intention. (Fath) The Sunnah of Fajr: due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'When dawn breaks, there is no prayer except two rak'ahs,' narrated by al-Tabarani, and what is meant by prayer is supererogatory; thus it is permissible to make up missed obligatory prayers. (Miskin) And before Maghrib: i.e., after sunset; because it delays Maghrib. Al-Shafi'i said: one prays two rak'ahs before Maghrib, and it is Sunnah in his view. (Ayn) And time of the khutbah: i.e., absolutely; whether it is a legal Sunnah or supererogatory, and whether it is a Friday khutbah, Eid, rain prayer, Hajj, completion of the Quran, or marriage; listening to all sermons is obligatory, so one is occupied from listening. (Fath) And about combining two prayers: due to what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: 'By the One besides Whom there is no god, he (the Prophet) never prayed any prayer except at its proper time except two prayers: he combined Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah, and Maghrib and 'Isha' at Jam'.' So whatever is reported from him, peace be upon him, that suggests the permissibility of combining two prayers due to an excuse like illness, etc., is interpreted as a formal combination (al-jam' al-suri) by delaying the first and advancing the second. Al-Shafi'i said: one may combine Zuhr and 'Asr, and Maghrib and 'Isha', due to the excuse of travel and rain; his evidence is that he, peace be upon him, combined Zuhr and 'Asr on the Tabuk expedition and Maghrib and 'Isha'. Our evidence: what we narrated, and also his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever combines two prayers has committed a major sin.' The interpretation of what he narrated is that he combined Zuhr and 'Asr in action, not in time, by delaying Zuhr to the end of its time and performing 'Asr at the beginning of its time. Malik said: combination is also permitted for mud. Ahmad: similar to them. He qualified with 'in time' to exclude combining them in action as we mentioned, and with 'with an excuse' to exclude combination at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, for that is permitted even without an excuse. If one combines elsewhere, it is invalid if he performed the obligatory prayer before its time, and it is forbidden in the opposite case. There is no harm in a traveler, especially a pilgrim, following al-Shafi'i on the condition that he adheres to all that is required by that imam, because a ruling mixed from two madhhabs is void by consensus. (Fath) With an excuse such as travel, rain, mud, or illness. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/46)
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the times when prayer is disliked. It begins by listing four such times: (1) after Fajr beyond the two Sunnah rak'ahs, (2) before Maghrib, (3) during the khutbah, and (4) combining two prayers into one time without a valid excuse. For each, the author provides proof. For the first, he cites the hadith 'no prayer after subh except two rak'ahs' and notes that the Prophet never exceeded two rak'ahs. If one starts a nafl before dawn and dawn breaks, the soundest view is that he does not abandon the Sunnah of Fajr nor cut the nafl. The second time is before Maghrib because it delays the obligatory prayer; the commentator notes that al-Shafi'i considers two rak'ahs before Maghrib as Sunnah. The third is during any khutbah because listening is obligatory and preoccupies one. The fourth is combining two prayers without excuse, which is prohibited. The author then details the dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i permits combination for travel and rain, citing the Prophet's action in Tabuk. The Hanafi response is to interpret such reports as a formal combination (jam' suri) where each prayer is in its actual time, or as specific to 'Arafah and Muzdalifah. The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is cited to show the Prophet only combined in those two places. Combination elsewhere without excuse is invalid or forbidden. The passage also permits a traveler, especially a pilgrim, to follow al-Shafi'i on this issue, provided he adheres strictly to all rulings of that madhhab, because mixing madhhabs arbitrarily is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
الجمع الصوري (al-jam' al-suri): Formal combination: delaying the first prayer to the end of its time and performing the second at the beginning of its time, so that they are not actually combined in one time.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Disliked; here it means prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), close to haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) After 'Asr until sunset

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains strict adherence to specific prayer times, considering four times as makruh tahrimi, and rejects the permissibility of combining prayers except at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, interpreting any apparent combination as formal (jam' suri).

Adhan Rulings in the Hanafi School
States the sunnah status of adhan, prohibition of tarji' and lahn, and the addition for Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of adhan (sunnah muakkadah) and explain the Hanafi position on tarji' and lahn with proofs.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah muakkadah without tarji' or lahn; tarji' is a bid'ah opposed by the practice of Bilal.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on the adhan, the call to prayer. You will learn that adhan is a confirmed sunnah, not obligatory, and that it must be performed without the repetition of the shahadah (tarji') and without melodic distortion (lahn). We will also see the special addition for Fajr and the evidence that underlies these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on adhan
Read the passage: 'سن للفرائض' indicates adhan is sunnah for the obligatory prayers. Note the discussion that it is sunnah muakkadah, close to wajib in sin for abandonment, but the relied-upon position is sunnah.
Imam Muhammad said he would fight those who abandon it, showing its importance.
2
Understand the prohibition of tarji'
The text states 'بلا ترجيع' – without tarji'. Tarji' is lowering the voice with the shahadah then raising it again. This is not part of the Sunnah according to the Hanafi school.
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider tarji' sunnah; the Hanafi school rejects it.
3
Analyze the proof for the Hanafi position on tarji'
The Hanafi proof (dalil) is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd and the consistent practice of Bilal in the Prophet's presence without tarji'. The hadith of Abu Mahdhurah is interpreted as teaching the wording, not tarji'.
This is a classic example of how a hadith is interpreted differently across madhhabs.
4
Identify the ruling on lahn and the Fajr addition
Lahn (melodic distortion) is makruh tahrimi except in the hay'alah phrases where lengthening is allowed. For Fajr, the phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is added after 'hayya 'ala al-falah', based on the story of Bilal and a hadith from Anas.
Beautifying the voice is desirable, but distorting letters is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأذان سن للفرائض بلا ترجيع ولحن، ويزيد بعد الفلاح سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح المؤذن الأذان: [هو في اللغة: الإعلام، وفي الشرع الإعلام على الوجه المخصوص، ولما كان موقوفاً على تحقق الوقت لما كان في الوقت من معنى السببية والسبب مقدم أخره عنه. (مسكين)] هو في الشرع إعلام غالبا على وجه مخصوص، وإنما قلنا: "غالباً"؛ لئلا يرد الأذان الواقع بين يدي الخطيب يوم الجمعة وللفائتة كما سيأتي، ولم يكن في زمنه وأبي بكر و عمر هما إلا مرة بين يدي المنبر، فلما كان زمن عثمان الله أحدثه على الزوراء أولاً. وفي أحدث المنارة أي محل التأذين في المساجد مسلمة بن خلف الصحابي الذي كان أميرا على مصر من الجمعة أول من جانب معاوية له. (فتح) فلا[؟] سن للفرائض: وقيل : إنه واجب لأمره له به على ما روي من قوله : "فأذنا وأقيما" إلخ، وفي "النهر" [١٧١/١]: القولان متقاربان، فإن السنة المؤكدة في حكم الواجب في لحوق الإثم بالترك، وعن محمد أنه قال: لو تركه أهل بلدة لقاتلتهم عليه، ولو تركه واحد لضربته. (فتح) للفرائض: أي الرواتب الخمس والجمعة دون الوتر وصلاة العيدين والكسوف والخسوف والجنازة والاستسقاء والسنن والنوافل وأراد بالفرائض الوقتيات المؤداة في المساجد، یسن للوقتيات المؤداة في البيوت؛ لأنه لا يكره تركهما لمصل في بيته أو في المسجد بعد صلاة الجماعة. (فتح) بلا ترجيع [وهو أن يخفض بالشهادتين صوته ثم يرجع فيرفع بهما صوته. (ط)] فليس هو من سنة الأذان عندنا خلافاً للمالك والشافعي، لهما حديث أبي محذورة أنه عليه أمر بذلك، ولنا: حديث عبد الله بن زيد من غير ترجيع، وأذان بلال بحضرته عليه في الحضر والسفر من غير ترجيع إلى أن توفي عليه، وأما تلقينه علكة لأبي محذورة فكان تعليماً فظنه ترجيعاً، والاختلاف الثاني بيننا وبينه أن التكبير في الشروع أربع تكبيرات، وعند مالك مرتين، قاسه بكلمة الشهادتين، ولنا حديث أبي محذورة أن الأذان تسع عشر كلمة ولن يكون كذلك إذا كان التكبير فيه مرتين، والاختلاف الثالث أن آخر الأذان "لا إله إلا الله" عندنا، وعلى قول أهل المدينة "لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر"، والاعتماد في مثله على المشهور الذي توارثه الناس إلى يومنا هذا. (فتح) ولحن: اعلم أن كراهة اللحن في الأذان إنما هي دون الحيعلتين، أما فيهما فلا بأس بإدخال المد، والكراهة فيه بمعنى إخراج الحروف عما يجوز له في الأداء تحريمية، أما مجرد تحسين الصوت فلا؛ لأنه أمر مطلوب بلا شك. (فتح) ويزيد إلخ: وأصله أن بلالاً جاء بحجرة عائشة بعد الأذان، فقال: الصلاة يا رسول الله ! فقالت عائشة: إن الرسول نائم، فقال: الصلاة خير من النوم ، فلما انتبه أخبرته فاستحسنه وقال: اجعله في أذانك"، وأخرج النسائي عن أنس: السنة إذا قال المؤذن في أذان الفجر: "حي على الفلاح"، قال: "الصلاة خير من النوم". (فتح) من
Chapter of the Adhan. Adhan is sunnah for the obligatory prayers without tarji' (repetition) or lahn (melodic deviation), and he adds after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the Fajr adhan. [Adhan: linguistically, it is announcement; in sacred law, it is announcement in a specific manner. Since it depends on the verification of time, and because time has a meaning of causation, and the cause precedes, he delayed mentioning it after the time. (Miskin)] In sacred law, it is announcement mostly in a specific manner; we said 'mostly' to exclude the adhan that occurs before the khatib on Friday and for missed prayer as will come. It was not in his time and the time of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, except once before the minbar. Then in the time of 'Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, he instituted it first on al-Zawra'. And the first to build a minaret, i.e., a place for adhan in mosques, was Muslimah ibn Khalaf, the Companion who was amir over Egypt, from the Friday first on the side of Mu'awiyah, may Allah be pleased with him. (Fath) So? Sunnah for the obligatory prayers: It is said that it is obligatory due to his command, as narrated from his saying: 'Give the adhan and the iqamah,' etc. In al-Nahr (1/171): the two statements are close, for the confirmed Sunnah is like the obligatory in incurring sin by leaving it. It is reported from Muhammad that he said: 'If the people of a town left it, I would fight them over it; if an individual left it, I would beat him.' (Fath) For the obligatory prayers: i.e., the five daily prayers and Friday, excluding witr, Eid prayers, eclipse prayers, funeral prayer, rain prayer, and supererogatory and nafl prayers. By 'obligatory' he meant time-bound prayers performed in mosques; it is sunnah for time-bound prayers performed in houses, because leaving it is not disliked for one praying in his house or in the mosque after congregational prayer. (Fath) Without tarji': tarji' is that he lowers his voice with the two testimonies, then repeats and raises his voice with them. (T) So it is not part of the Sunnah of adhan in our school, contrary to the Maliki and Shafi'i. They have the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah that he, peace be upon him, ordered that. Our evidence: the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd without tarji', and the adhan of Bilal in his presence, peace be upon him, in urban and travel without tarji' until he died. As for his teaching to Abu Mahdhurah the wording (lahjah), it was instruction, so he thought it was tarji'. The second difference between us and them is that the takbir at the start is four takbirs, and according to Malik it is two, he analogized it to the word of the testimonies. Our evidence: the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah that the adhan is nineteen words; it would not be so if the takbir was two times. The third difference is that the end of the adhan is 'la ilaha illa Allah' in our school, and according to the people of Madinah it is 'la ilaha illa Allah wa Allahu akbar'. The reliance in such matters is on what is well-known and inherited by the people up to this day. (Fath) And lahn (melodic deviation): Know that the prohibition of lahn in the adhan is only apart from the two phrases of 'hayya'? As for these, there is no harm in introducing lengthening. The prohibition here means taking the letters out of what is permissible in performance (tahrimi). As for merely beautifying the voice, it is not prohibited because it is undoubtedly desirable. (Fath) And he adds, etc.: Its origin is that Bilal came to 'Aishah's room after the adhan and said: 'Prayer, O Messenger of Allah!' 'Aishah said: 'The Messenger is sleeping.' He said: 'Prayer is better than sleep.' When he (the Prophet) woke up, she told him, and he approved it and said: 'Make it in your adhan.' Al-Nasa'i narrated from Anas: The Sunnah is that when the mu'adhdhin says in the Fajr adhan 'hayya 'ala al-falah', he says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm.' (Fath) ... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of adhan from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by stating the core rulings: adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) for the five obligatory prayers and Friday, without tarji' (repeating the shahadah in a low then loud voice) and without lahn (melodic distortion). In the Fajr adhan, the phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is added after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. The commentator first defines adhan linguistically and legally, noting that the definition includes 'mostly' to account for the adhan before the Friday khutbah and for missed prayers, which are not necessarily time-based. He then discusses the historical development: in the Prophet's time and under Abu Bakr and 'Umar, adhan was only given once before the minbar; 'Uthman instituted a second adhan on al-Zawra'. The first minaret was built by Muslimah ibn Khalaf, a companion. The commentator then discusses the ruling that adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah, noting that some scholars consider it wajib, and reports that Imam Muhammad said he would fight a town that abandoned it. The phrase 'for the obligatory prayers' is explained to mean the five daily prayers and Friday, not witr or Eid etc., and it applies to prayers in mosques or at home (though not disliked to leave it at home). Then the commentary addresses the dispute with Maliki and Shafi'i on tarji': Hanafis reject tarji' based on the practice of Bilal and the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd. The hadith of Abu Mahdhurah is interpreted as teaching, not tarji'. Further disputes are noted: the number of takbirs at the start (four in Hanafi, two in Maliki) and the final phrase (Hanafi ends with 'la ilaha illa Allah', Madinans add 'Allahu akbar'). On lahn, the commentator clarifies that lahn is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) in the adhan except in the 'hayya' phrases where lengthening is allowed. Beautifying the voice is desirable. Finally, the addition 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' for Fajr is traced to the story of Bilal and is confirmed as sunnah from the hadith of Anas.

Key Terms
الترجيع (al-tarji'): To lower the voice with the shahadah then raise it again (repetition). Considered not part of Sunnah in Hanafi school.
اللحن (al-lahn): Melodic deviation or distortion of letters; it is makruh tahrimi in adhan except in hay'alah where lengthening is allowed.
الصلاة خير من النوم (al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm): The phrase added in Fajr adhan after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'; it is sunnah based on the story of Bilal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a difference between them and the Shafi'i/Maliki schools regarding adhan?
A) The number of takbirs at the start of adhan (Hanafi: 4, others: 2)
B) The phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is not used in Fajr
C) The adhan is only for congregational prayers, not for individuals
D) The adhan must be given while standing on a high place

Key Takeaway
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah; tarji' is not part of the Sunnah, lahn is makruh tahrimi except in hay'alah, and the Fajr addition is confirmed sunnah.

Ruling of Adhan: Sunnah Muakkadah and Conditions
Ruling of adhan with conditions and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and explain the three points of dispute with the Maliki/Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
Adhan is a confirmed Sunnah, not compulsory, but its abandonment invites punishment — and its form is fixed by the Prophet's unbroken practice.

The adhan is the call to prayer, a defining symbol of Islam. In this passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq with its commentary, we learn its ruling as sunnah muakkadah, the conditions (no tarji', no melody), and the three key differences between the Hanafi school and other schools. Understanding these points protects the mu'adhdhin's practice and clarifies the reliance of the Hanafi school on the consistent practice of Bilal (radiyallahu anhu).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The adhan. What is the hukm? The text states 'سن للفرائض' (it is sunnah for obligatory prayers) and 'سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح' (sunnah muakkadah according to the correct view).
Sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school is close to wajib; leaving it is sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid without tarji', and the practice of Bilal in the Prophet's presence without tarji' until his death. Also the hadith of Abu Mahdhura is used by the opposing school.
The Hanafi proof is based on continuous practice (tawatur) of Bilal's adhan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this dalil prove the ruling? The consistent absence of tarji' in Bilal's adhan, who was the official mu'adhdhin, indicates that tarji' is not part of the sunnah. The command 'Fa'adhdhina' (Surah al-Maidah:58) is understood as recommendation, not obligation, due to the absence of additional qara'in (indications).
The command is general, but the practice of the Prophet clarifies it as sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which schools disagree and on what grounds? Malik and Shafi'i differ on three points: 1) tarji' (repeating shahadah low then loud), 2) number of opening takbirs (Hanafi: four, Maliki: two), 3) final phrase (Hanafi: 'La ilaha illa Allah', others add 'Allahu Akbar').
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the actual wording of the adhan.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The Hanafi position is mu'tamad (relied upon) because it is based on the widespread practice (tawatur) inherited from the Prophet's time. The hadith of Abu Mahdhura is interpreted as instruction for learning, not as tarji' (the Prophet taught him the words, not the repetition).
The word count argument: if takbir were only twice, the adhan would not be 19 words.

سن للفرائض: وقيل : إنه واجب لأمره له به على ما روي من قوله : "فأذنا وأقيما" إلخ، وفي "النهر" [١٧١/١]: القولان متقاربان، فإن السنة المؤكدة في حكم الواجب في لحوق الإثم بالترك، وعن محمد أنه قال: لو تركه أهل بلدة لقاتلتهم عليه، ولو تركه واحد لضربته. (فتح) بلا ترجيع [وهو أن يخفض بالشهادتين صوته ثم يرجع فيرفع بهما صوته. (فتح)

The Book of Prayer. Chapter of the Adhan. It is sunnah for the obligatory prayers without tarji' (repetition in a low voice) and without melody, and he adds after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'... Sunnah muakkadah according to the correct view. The mu'adhdhin. The adhan: linguistically it is announcement, and in sacred law it is an announcement in a specific manner. ...

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on adhan from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, with commentary from Fath and other sources. It first states the ruling: adhan is sunnah muakkadah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, not for witr, Eid, etc. There is a view that it is wajib due to the command 'Fa'adhdhina wa aqima' but the two views are close since sunnah muakkadah entails sin for leaving. Imam Muhammad said he would fight a town that abandons it. The phrase 'bila tarji'' means not to repeat the shahadah in a low voice then loud; Hanafis reject tarji', unlike Malik and Shafi'i who rely on the hadith of Abu Mahdhura. Hanafis adduce the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid without tarji' and the practice of Bilal. A second difference is the number of takbirs: Hanafis say four at the start, Malik says two. A third difference is the final phrase: Hanafis end with 'La ilaha illa Allah', while the people of Madinah add 'Allahu Akbar'. The relied-upon position is the well-known one. Regarding melody (lahn): it is impermissible to distort sounds in adhan except in the hay'alah where prolongation is okay. Mere beautification of voice is not disliked.

Key Terms
الأذان (al-adhan): Announcement in a specific manner for the obligatory prayers
الترجيع (al-tarji'): Lowering the voice with the shahadah and then raising it
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-muakkadah): A confirmed sunnah whose omission is sinful in the view of some Hanafis

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Fard kifayah

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a confirmed Sunnah whose form is fixed by the Prophet's unbroken practice; three key differences with other schools exist, but the Hanafi view is based on tawatur.

The Additional Phrase in Fajr Adhan
Details the origin and ruling of the Fajr adhan phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the additional phrase said in the Fajr adhan, identify its origin from the hadith of Bilal, and apply the ruling that it is said twice.

Core Idea
The phrase 'al-salat khair min al-nawm' is a sunnah addition in Fajr adhan, said twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.

In the Hanafi school, the Fajr adhan includes a unique phrase not found in other prayers. This lesson traces the story of Bilal and the prophetic approval that led to this addition. You will learn when and how it is said, along with the evidence from the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase
Find in the text the Arabic phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' that is added in Fajr adhan. It is only for Fajr.
2
Trace its origin
Read the story of Bilal coming to the Prophet's apartment after the adhan and mentioning the phrase. The Prophet approved and instructed Bilal to include it in his adhan.
This is the basis for the practice.
3
Confirm the number of times
The text states the phrase is said 'مرتين' (twice). Understand that both the adhan and the iqamah for Fajr include this twice.
Some narrations say once, but the relied-upon view is twice.

أي الإقامة
"قد قامت الصلاة" مرتين ويترسل فيه، ويحدر فيها، ويستقبل بهما القبلة، ولا يتكلّم أي بالأذان والإقامة

المؤذن
في أذان الفجر وخص الفجر به؛ لأنه يؤدى في حال نوم الناس وغفلتهم، فخص بزيادة الإعلام كما خص بالتطويل بالقراءة لئلا تفوتهم الجماعة. (مسكين) والإقامة مثله : أي مثل الأذان مثنى مثنى غير التكبير، فإنه أربع في الشروع، وقال الشافعي التكبير مثنى وباقيه فرادى؛ لما روي أن بلالاً أمر أن يشفع الأذان ويوتر الإقامة، ولنا: ما
يؤذن
اشتهر عن بلال أنه كان يثني الإقامة إلى أن توفي والملك النازل أقام كذلك، وكان بلال بعد رسول الله الله . مثنى ويقيم مثنى بتواتر الآثار، ولا حجة للشافعي فيما رواه؛ لأنه لم يذكر الآمر ، فيحتمل أن يكون الأمر غير النبي وليس فيه أن بلالاً امتثل لأمره أيضاً. (فتح) مثله مثل الأذان مثنى مثنى، وقال الشافعي: فرادى فرادى. (ط) ويزيد بعد فلاحها إلخ: لقول عبد الله بن زيد: إني كنت بين النائم واليقظان إذ رأيت شخصا نزل من السماء، وعليه ثوبان أخضران وفي يده شبه الناقوس فقلت: أتبيعني هذا؟ فقال: ما تصنع به؟ قلت: نضرب به عند صلاتنا، هذا؟ فقلت: نعم! فقام على قطع حائط مستقبل القبلة فأذن، ثم مكث هنيئة، ثم
أذانك،
فقال: ألا أدلك على ما هو خير من . قام، فقال مثل مقالته الأولى، وزاد في آخره قد قامت الصلاة. (فتح) ويترسل إلخ [ أي يفصل في الأذان بين كلماته. (ع)] لقوله : "يا بلال! إذا أذنت فترسل في وإذا أقمت فاحدر" على وزن "انصر" أي أسرع، وفي الظهيرية لو جعل الأذان إقامة أعاده، ولو جعل الإقامة أذاناً لا؛ لأن تكرار الأذان مشروع أي بالنظر ليوم الجمعة دون الإقامة. (فتح المعين) ويحدر فيها أي يوصل المؤذن في الإقامة بين كلماتها على سبيل السرعة، وهما مندوبان حتى لو ترسل فيهما أو حدر فيه وترسل فيها جاز الحصول المقصود وهو الإعلام. (ع) ويستقبل بهما : لأن التوارث من فعل بلال، فلو ترك جاز وكره. (فتح) ولا يتكلم: لقوله علية: "من تكلم فيهما خيف عليه من زوال الإيمان"؛ ولأن التكلم فيهما يخل بالمقصود، وهو الإعلام؛ ولأنه ذكر معظم كالخطبة، فلا يجوز في خلاله الاشتغال بالتكلم، وهذا الحكم في حق الكل، فإن سمع الأذان لا يجوز له التكلم غير أن يقول ما يقول المؤذن، ولا يجوز ما سوى ذلك ولو برد سلام أو تشميت عاطس، ومنه التنحنح إلا لتحسين صوته، فإن تكلم استأنف إلا إذا كان يسيراً. (فتح، مستخلص) فيهما: أي في الأذان والإقامة؛ لأن فيه ترك الموالاة، ولا يرد السلام أيضاً خلافاً للثوري. (ع) ويلتفت يميناً وشمالاً [المؤذن في الأذان دون الإقامة مسكين)] لأنه خطاب للقوم فيواجههم بالصلاة والفلاح؛ لأن المواجهة أبلغ في الإعلام (مستخلص) بالصلاة: أي يلتفت يميناً عند "حي على الصلاة"، وشمالاً "عند حي . أسماء الأفعال بمعنى هلم وعجل.
"
الفلاح"، و"حي" من
على
And he adds, etc.: Its origin is that Bilal came to the apartment of Aisha after the adhan and said: 'Prayer, O Messenger of Allah!' Aisha said: 'The Messenger is asleep.' He said: 'Prayer is better than sleep.' When he woke up, he told him and he approved and said: 'Put it in your adhan.' ... In the adhan of Fajr, 'al-salat khair min al-nawm' twice, and the iqamah is like it; he adds after its 'hay'alah [the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salat' twice], and he performs tarassul in it, and hadr in her, and faces the qibla with both, and does not speak during them, and turns right and left with 'al-salah' and 'al-falah'.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on adhan, focusing on the additional phrase in Fajr and the rules of iqamah. The origin of the phrase 'al-salat khair min al-nawm' is from Bilal's narration. In the Hanafi school, this phrase is said twice in Fajr adhan after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. The iqamah is like the adhan in being repeated in pairs, except that the takbir at the start is four. There is a dispute with Shafi'i who says iqamah is individual (one by one). Hanafis cite the continuous practice of Bilal and others. The etiquettes include: tarassul (pausing between phrases) in adhan, hadr (speed) in iqamah, facing qibla, not speaking during adhan or iqamah (speaking invalidates and requires restart unless minor), and turning right at 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and left at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' for adhan only (not iqamah). The reason for these rules is to maximize the announcement.

Key Terms
الصلاة خير من النوم (al-salat khair min al-nawm): The phrase 'prayer is better than sleep' added in Fajr adhan

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, how many times is 'al-salat khair min al-nawm' said in the Fajr adhan?
A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'al-salat khair min al-nawm' is a sunnah addition specific to Fajr adhan, said twice based on prophetic approval.

The Dispute on Iqamah: Pairs vs Singles
Details the dispute over iqamah structure with proofs from both schools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that iqamah is said in pairs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The iqamah is said muthanna (pairs) based on the mutawatir practice of Bilal; the Shafi'i hadith is weak due to unknown commander.

One of the key differences between Hanafis and Shafi'is is the structure of the iqamah. The Hanafi position is that all phrases of iqamah are said twice, except the opening takbir which is four. This lesson examines the proofs from both sides and the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that iqamah said muthanna (pairs) except takbir at start is four. Cite from text: 'والإقامة مثله : أي مثل الأذان مثنى مثنى غير التكبير، فإنه أربع في الشروع'.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i said all phrases are fradan (single) except takbir. Find in text: 'وقال الشافعي التكبير مثنى وباقيه فرادى'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is the continuous practice of Bilal that he said iqamah in pairs until his death, and that the angel also did that. This is considered tawatur. Text: 'ما اشتهر عن بلال أنه كان يثني الإقامة إلى أن توفي والملك النازل أقام كذلك'.
4
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
Shafi'i relies on a hadith: 'أن بلالاً أمر أن يشفع الأذان ويوتر الإقامة'. But the Hanafi response is that the commander is unknown, so it cannot be attributed to the Prophet, and Bilal's actual practice contradicts it.
5
Determine the thamarah
Practical difference: Hanafis say 'qad qamat al-salat' twice; Shafi'is say it once. Also, Hanafis say takbir four times in iqamah start; Shafi'is say takbir twice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويزيد إلخ: وأصله أن بلالاً جاء بحجرة عائشة بعد الأذان، فقال: الصلاة يا رسول الله ! فقالت عائشة: إن الرسول نائم، فقال: الصلاة خير من النوم ، فلما انتبه أخبرته فاستحسنه وقال: اجعله في أذانك"، وأخرج النسائي عن أنس: السنة إذا قال المؤذن في أذان الفجر: "حي على الفلاح"، قال: "الصلاة خير من النوم". (فتح)

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Etiquettes of Adhan and Iqamah: Tarassul, Hadr, and More
Details the etiquettes of adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended etiquettes for adhan (tarassul, facing qibla, silence, turning) and iqamah (hadr), and identify which speaking invalidates them.

Core Idea
Tarassul in adhan, hadr in iqamah, facing qibla, silence, and turning are sunnah; significant speaking invalidates and requires restart.

Beyond the words themselves, the adhan and iqamah have specific etiquettes that enhance the call to prayer. This lesson covers the recommended pace, facing, silence, and turning, and explains the ruling on speaking during the call.

Guided Path
1
List the etiquettes
Identify from the text: tarassul in adhan, hadr in iqamah, facing qibla, not speaking, turning right and left during hay'alah in adhan only.
2
Understand tarassul and hadr
Tarassul means pausing between words slowly; hadr means connecting words quickly. Both are mandub. Text: 'ويترسل فيه، ويحدر فيها'.
3
Explain the ruling on speaking
Speaking invalidates the adhan/iqamah if it is significant; minor speech (like clearing throat) is allowed. If one speaks, he must restart. Text: 'فإن تكلم استأنف إلا إذا كان يسيراً'.
4
Detail the turning
The mu'adhdhin turns right at 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and left at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' during adhan only (not iqamah). Reason: to face the qibla and also address the listeners.

Method of Adhan and Iqama: Tarsil, Hadr, and the Madhhab Dispute on Iqama Structure
States the rulings for Fajr adhan, iqama form, tarsil, hadr, facing qibla, silence, and turning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the performance of adhan and iqama, including tarsil, hadr, facing qibla, turning, and the dispute with al-Shafi'i on the iqama being recited in twos.

Core Idea
The iqama is recited in twos like the adhan, except the initial takbir is four, based on the continuous practice of Bilal.

This lesson unpacks a passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq that lays out the detailed rulings for adhan and iqama. You will learn the recommended manner of recitation, the importance of tarsil and hadr, and the evidence behind the Hanafi position that the iqama is recited in pairs. The passage also addresses a key disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the number of repetitions in the iqama.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
List the specific actions prescribed for adhan and iqama: tarsil (slow recitation), hadr (quick recitation), facing qibla, not speaking, and turning.
The ruling for most actions is sunnah muakkadah; speaking is makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the proofs
The Prophet's command to Bilal 'if you give adhan, be slow; if you give iqama, be quick' and the well-known practice of Bilal.
The hadith is ahad but the practice of Bilal is considered tawatur.
3
Understand the dispute
The iqama structure: Hanafi says mathna (twos) except takbir four; Shafi'i says furada (singles) including takbir twos.
4
Evaluate the evidence
Hanafi cites continuous practice of Bilal; Shafi'i cites a narration ordering adhan in pairs and iqama in singles. Hanafi responds that the orderer is unnamed and Bilal may not have acted on it.
The Hanafi response challenges the authority and application of the opposing narration.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is relied upon due to stronger evidence (tawatur of practice).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
باب الأذان
في أذان الفجر الصلاة خير من النوم" مرتين والإقامة مثله، ويزيد بعد فلاحها المؤذن أي الإقامة "قد قامت الصلاة" مرتين ويترسل فيه، ويحدر فيها، ويستقبل بهما القبلة، ولا يتكلّم أي بالأذان والإقامة فيهما ويلتفت يميناً وشمالاً بالصلاة والفلاح، أي في الأذان والإقامة أي يحول المؤذن في أذان الفجر وخص الفجر به؛ لأنه يؤدى في حال نوم الناس وغفلتهم، فخص بزيادة الإعلام كما خص بالتطويل بالقراءة لئلا تفوتهم الجماعة. (مسكين) والإقامة مثله : أي مثل الأذان مثنى مثنى غير التكبير، فإنه أربع في الشروع، وقال الشافعي التكبير مثنى وباقيه فرادى؛ لما روي أن بلالاً أمر أن يشفع الأذان ويوتر الإقامة، ولنا: ما اشتهر عن بلال أنه كان يثني الإقامة إلى أن توفي والملك النازل أقام كذلك، وكان بلال بعد رسول الله [؟] مثنى ويقيم مثنى بتواتر الآثار، ولا حجة للشافعي فيما رواه؛ لأنه لم يذكر الآمر، فيحتمل أن يكون الأمر غير النبي وليس فيه أن بلالاً امتثل لأمره أيضاً. (فتح) مثله مثل الأذان مثنى مثنى، وقال الشافعي: فرادى فرادى. (ط) ويزيد بعد فلاحها إلخ: لقول عبد الله بن زيد: إني كنت بين النائم واليقظان إذ رأيت شخصا نزل من السماء، وعليه ثوبان أخضران وفي يده شبه الناقوس فقلت: أتبيعني هذا؟ فقال: ما تصنع به؟ قلت: نضرب به عند صلاتنا، هذا؟ فقلت: نعم! فقام على قطع حائط مستقبل القبلة فأذن، ثم مكث هنيئة، ثم قال: ألا أدلك على ما هو خير من [؟] قام، فقال مثل مقالته الأولى، وزاد في آخره قد قامت الصلاة. (فتح) ويترسل إلخ [ أي يفصل في الأذان بين كلماته. (ع)] لقوله : "يا بلال! إذا أذنت فترسل في وإذا أقمت فاحدر" على وزن "انصر" أي أسرع، وفي الظهيرية لو جعل الأذان إقامة أعاده، ولو جعل الإقامة أذاناً لا؛ لأن تكرار الأذان مشروع أي بالنظر ليوم الجمعة دون الإقامة. (فتح المعين) ويحدر فيها أي يوصل المؤذن في الإقامة بين كلماتها على سبيل السرعة، وهما مندوبان حتى لو ترسل فيهما أو حدر فيه وترسل فيها جاز الحصول المقصود وهو الإعلام. (ع) ويستقبل بهما : لأن التوارث من فعل بلال، فلو ترك جاز وكره. (فتح) ولا يتكلم: لقوله عليه: "من تكلم فيهما خيف عليه من زوال الإيمان"؛ ولأن التكلم فيهما يخل بالمقصود، وهو الإعلام؛ ولأنه ذكر معظم كالخطبة، فلا يجوز في خلاله الاشتغال بالتكلم، وهذا الحكم في حق الكل، فإن سمع الأذان لا يجوز له التكلم غير أن يقول ما يقول المؤذن، ولا يجوز ما سوى ذلك ولو برد سلام أو تشميت عاطس، ومنه التنحنح إلا لتحسين صوته، فإن تكلم استأنف إلا إذا كان يسيراً. (فتح، مستخلص) فيهما: أي في الأذان والإقامة؛ لأن فيه ترك الموالاة، ولا يرد السلام أيضاً خلافاً للثوري. (ع) ويلتفت يميناً وشمالاً [المؤذن في الأذان دون الإقامة مسكين)] لأنه خطاب للقوم فيواجههم بالصلاة والفلاح؛ لأن المواجهة أبلغ في الإعلام (مستخلص) بالصلاة: أي يلتفت يميناً عند "حي على الصلاة"، وشمالاً عند "حي على الفلاح"، و"حي" من أسماء الأفعال بمعنى هلم وعجل.
The Book of Prayer. Chapter of the Adhan. In the Fajr adhan, (the phrase) "Prayer is better than sleep" twice, and the iqama is like it, and after its 'flah' (after 'hayya 'ala al-falah') the mu'adhdhin says, i.e. in the iqama, "The prayer has been established" twice. And he should be slow (yatarassal) in it (adhan) and quick (yahdir) in it (iqama). And he should face the qibla with both (adhan and iqama), and not speak, meaning in the adhan and iqama, and he should turn right and left with 'al-salah' and 'al-falah', meaning in the adhan and iqama, i.e. the mu'adhdhin changes direction. In the Fajr adhan, it is specified for Fajr because it is performed while people are sleeping and heedless, so it is specified with extra notification just as it is specified with lengthening the recitation so that they do not miss the congregation. (Miskin) And the iqama is like it, i.e., like the adhan in twos, except for the takbir, for it is four at the beginning. Al-Shafi'i said: The takbir is two and the rest are singles, because it is narrated that Bilal was ordered to say the adhan in twos and the iqama in singles. Our proof: It is well-known from Bilal that he continued to say the iqama in twos until he died, and the descending angel did the iqama likewise, and Bilal after the Messenger of God [؟] used to give adhan in twos and iqama in twos by tawatur of traditions. There is no proof for al-Shafi'i in his narration because he did not mention the one who gave the order, so it is possible that the order was from other than the Prophet, and his narration does not include that Bilal acted upon his order. (Fath) It is like the adhan in twos. Al-Shafi'i said: singles. (T) 'And after its flah' etc.: Because of the statement of Abdullah ibn Zaid: I was between sleep and wakefulness when I saw a person descending from the sky, wearing two green garments, and in his hand something like a bell. I said: Will you sell me this? He said: What will you do with it? I said: We will strike it for our prayer. He said: Shall I not guide you to something better than that? Then he stood on a piece of wall facing the qibla and gave adhan, then paused for a while, then said: Shall I not guide you to something better than [؟] stood and said the same first statement, and added at the end: 'The prayer has been established.' (Fath) 'And he should be slow' etc.: i.e., he should separate (pause) between the words of the adhan. (A) Because of his statement: 'O Bilal! When you give adhan, be slow, and when you give iqama, be quick' (ho) meaning hasten. In al-Zahiriyyah: If one makes the adhan iqama, he should repeat it; if he makes the iqama adhan, he should not, because repeating the adhan is legislated considering Friday, not the iqama. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'And be quick in it' i.e., the mu'adhdhin should connect the words of the iqama quickly. Both are recommended, so if one does them slowly or is quick in one and slow in the other, it is permissible because the intended purpose, which is notification, is achieved. (A) 'And face the qibla with both' because it is inherited from the action of Bilal; if he leaves it, it is permissible but disliked. (Fath) 'And do not speak' because of his statement: 'Whoever speaks during them, it is feared that his faith will depart'; and because speaking in them violates the purpose, which is notification; and because it is a great dhikr like the khutba, so it is not permissible to engage in speaking during it. This ruling applies to everyone: the one who hears the adhan should not speak except to repeat what the mu'adhdhin says. Nothing else is permissible, even returning a greeting or responding to a sneeze, and including clearing the throat except to improve one's voice. If one speaks, he should restart unless it is insignificant. (Fath, Mustakhlas) In both: i.e., in adhan and iqama, because it involves abandoning sequentiality, and he should not return the greeting either, contrary to al-Thawri. (A) 'And turn right and left' (the mu'adhdhin in the adhan, not in the iqama - Miskin) because it is an address to the people, so he faces them with 'al-salah' and 'al-falah' because facing is more effective for notification. (Mustakhlas) For 'al-salah': i.e., he turns right at 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and left at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', and 'Hayya' is among the verbal nouns meaning 'come' and 'hasten'.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq presents a series of rulings concerning the method of the adhan and iqama, specifically highlighting the Fajr adhan. The matn states that in the Fajr adhan, the phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is added twice. The iqama is like the adhan, meaning it is recited in pairs (mathna), except that in the iqama the takbir is four at the beginning according to the Hanafi school. The mu'adhdhin adds 'qad qamati al-salah' twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. Then the author details the actions: tarsil (slowness) in the adhan, hadr (swiftness) in the iqama, facing the qibla during both, refraining from speaking, and turning to the right at 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and to the left at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. The commentator clarifies each point with proofs. The Hanafi position on the iqama being in twos is defended against al-Shafi'i, who holds it should be singles. The proof from the practice of Bilal and the descending angel is cited, and al-Marghinani (in al-Hidayah) refutes al-Shafi'i by noting the narrator did not specify the Prophet as the orderer. The tarsil and hadr are established by the Prophet's command to Bilal: 'If you give adhan, be slow; if you give iqama, be quick.' Facing the qibla and not speaking are also Sunna, with the latter being strongly emphasized; the commentator mentions that even responding to a greeting is impermissible, and if one speaks unnecessarily, the adhan or iqama must be repeated unless the speech is insignificant. The turning is specific to the adhan (not iqama) and is done to face the congregations for effective notification. This passage exemplifies how the Hanafi school derives detailed rules from the practice of the Sahaba and the Prophet's instructions.

Key Terms
ترسل (tarsul): Slowness and pause between words in the adhan.
حدر (hadr): Quickness and connecting words in the iqama.
مثنى (mathna): Reciting each phrase twice in both adhan and iqama (Hanafi view).
فرادى (furada): Reciting each phrase once (Shafi'i view for iqama).
التفات (iltifat): Turning the face right and left during the adhan at the phrases 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times is the takbir recited at the beginning of the iqama?
A) Twice
B) Four times
C) Once
D) Three times

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the iqama is recited in twos (mathna) like the adhan, supported by the continuous practice of Bilal, and that the sunnah acts of tarsil, hadr, facing qibla, and turning are recommended for proper notification.

Mu'adhdhin's Actions: Turning in Minaret and Placing Fingers in Ears
Explains the recommended actions for the mu'adhdhin of turning around in the minaret and placing fingers in ears

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnah actions for the mu'adhdhin during adhan and identify their evidence and conditions.

Core Idea
Turning and placing fingers in ears are sunnah actions that enhance the adhan's voice.

The adhan has specific recommended actions that enhance its delivery and follow the Prophet's practice. This lesson covers two such actions: turning in the minaret to face all directions, and placing fingers in the ears to raise the voice. Both are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory, but observing them brings reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions
Name the two actions discussed in the text: turning in the minaret and placing fingers in the ears.
Both are separate recommended practices.
2
Determine the ruling level
From the text, note that both are mandub (recommended) or sunnah muakkadah. The text says 'وهما مندوبان'.
They are not obligatory; omission does not invalidate the adhan.
3
Locate the evidence
For turning, the practice is based on the actions of the Prophet and Companions. For fingers, the Prophet's command to Bilal is cited: 'اجعل إصبعيك في أذنيك، فإنه أرفع لصوتك'.
The hadith is a sunnah ahad, indicating recommendation, not obligation.
4
Identify the condition
Turning is only performed if the minaret is spacious; otherwise, the mu'adhdhin simply turns his face right and left while keeping his feet still.
The condition is mentioned: 'إذا لم يستطع سنة الصلاة والفلاح'.
5
Recognize the alternative
For fingers, placing the entire hand on the ears (as Abu Mahdhurah did with thumb and index finger) is also considered good (hasan).
Shows flexibility in following the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستدير في صومعته، ويجعل إصبعيه في أذنيه، وهما مندوبان. الصومعة بيت الراهب مأخوذ من قولهم: رجل أصمع أي لاصق الأذنين، سمي بيت الراهب لانضمام أطرافها ودقة رأسها، وأراد بها بيت الأذان ههنا، وهذه الاستدارة إذا لم يستطع سنة الصلاة والفلاح، وهي تحويل الوجه يميناً وشمالاً مع ثبات قدميه مكانهما كما هو السنة بأن كانت الصومعة متسعة، فأما غير حاجة من فلا يفعل ذلك. (مسكين) ويجعل إصبعيه : لأنه عليه السلام قال لبلال : "اجعل إصبعيك في أذنيك، فإنه أرفع لصوتك"، وإن جعل يديه على أذنيه فحسن؛ لأن أبا محذورة ضم الإبهام والسبابة من كل يد ووضعها على أذنيه. (فتح) في أذنيه: أي في صماخى أذنيه؛ لأنه أجمع للصوت. (ط)
And he should turn around in his 'sawma'ah' (minaret), and place his two fingers in his ears, and both are recommended. The 'sawma'ah' is the monk's cell, derived from their saying: a man 'asma' meaning sticking to the ears, named monk's cell because its sides converge and its top is narrow. Here it is intended to mean the place of the adhan. This turning is if he cannot perform the sunnah of (turning for) 'al-salah' and 'al-falah', i.e., turning the face right and left while keeping his feet in place, which is the sunnah if the minaret is spacious. As for the one who does not need to, he should not do that. (Miskin) And he places his two fingers because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Bilal: "Place your two fingers in your ears, for that raises your voice." And if he places his hands on his ears, that is good because Abu Mahdhurah cupped his thumb and index finger of each hand and placed them on his ears. (Fath) In his ears: i.e., in the hollow of his ears, because it collects the voice best. (T)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage provides the rulings for the mu'adhdhin's physical actions during the adhan. First, he should turn around (istidara) in the minaret (sawma'ah) if the minaret is spacious enough; otherwise, he simply turns his face right and left while keeping his feet still. Turning is recommended (mandub) and is intended to ensure the voice reaches all directions. The term 'sawma'ah' originally means a monk's cell, but here it refers to the minaret. Second, the mu'adhdhin should place his two fingers in his ears, as the Prophet instructed Bilal, because it amplifies the voice. Alternatively, placing the hands on the ears (as Abu Mahdhurah did) is also considered good. The fingers should be inserted into the earholes to gather the sound. These actions are sunnah, and omitting them is not sinful but leaves some merit.

Key Terms
صومعة (sawma'ah): Minaret; originally a monk's cell, here used for the place where the mu'adhdhin stands to call the adhan.
استدارة (istidara): Turning around in the minaret to face all directions during adhan.
إصبع (isba'): Finger; the mu'adhdhin places his index fingers or thumbs in his ears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school recommend the mu'adhdhin place his fingers in his ears during the adhan?
A) To prevent hearing his own voice
B) To raise the volume of his voice
C) It is a necessary pillar of the adhan
D) To signal the beginning of the prayer

Key Takeaway
The mu'adhdhin is recommended to turn in the minaret (if spacious) and place fingers in ears to amplify his voice, following the Prophet's practice.

Tathwib: The Additional Call in Adhan – Dispute on Permissibility
Explains tathwib and the disagreement on its permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of tathwib and explain why early Hanafis ruled it makruh while later Hanafis allowed it for necessity.

Core Idea
Early Hanafis: tathwib is a disliked innovation; later Hanafis approved it for heedless times.

Tathwib—an extra call after the adhan—has been practiced in various forms across Muslim communities. This passage from the commentary explores its four types and the strong disagreement among early Hanafi masters, who deemed it makruh, and later scholars, who allowed it in certain circumstances. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi fiqh balances textual evidence with practical need.

Guided Path
1
Define tathwib and its types
Read the definition and classifications of tathwib: the ancient form (for Fajr), the Kufan innovation between adhan and iqama, the general tathwib for all prayers, and the ruler-specific tathwib introduced by Abu Yusuf.
The ancient form 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is considered part of the adhan by Kufan scholars.
2
Identify the early Hanafi position
Early Hanafis (mutaqaddimin) and the majority ruled tathwib as makruh (disliked) and an innovation (bid'ah). Note the supporting proofs: the rebuke of Umar to the mu'adhdhin of Makkah, and Ali and Ibn Umar condemning the practice.
This is the stronger view among the mutaqaddimin.
3
Examine the opposing Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i and other imams outright prohibited tathwib, using the same narrations. Their position is that the adhan suffices and additional calls are unnecessary innovations.
The Hanafis acknowledge this as the 'most correct view' in the passage.
4
Analyze the later Hanafi shift
Later Hanafis allowed tathwib due to increased heedlessness and introduced specific forms for rulers and public officials, citing the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit as a precedent.
This shows istihsan (juristic preference) overriding the original prohibition for public benefit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In early Hanafism, tathwib is avoided; in later practice, it may be performed if custom or need requires. Shafi'is never perform it.
A mufti today should assess local custom and the level of heedlessness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثوب من التثويب وهو العود إلى الإعلام بعد الإعلام مثل أن يقول: الصلاة الصلاة أي مطلقاً في جميع الصلوات وهو أربعة: الأول قديم، وهو الصلاة خير من النوم، وكان بعد أذان الفجر إلا أن علماء الكوفة الحقوه بالأذان والثاني: محدث أحدثه علماء الكوفة بين الأذان والإقامة على الصلاة مرتين حي على الفلاح مرتين، وتثويب كل بلدة على ما تعارفوا به إما بالتنحنح أو بـ "الصلاة الصلاة" أو "قامت قامت"، والثالث ما استحسنه المتأخرون وهو التثويب في سائر الصلوات لزيادة غفلة الناس، وما أحدثه أبو يوسف للأمير بأن يقول: السلام عليك أيها الأمير حي على الصلاة حي على الفلاح، الصلاة يرحمك الله، وكذلك كل من اشتغل بمصالح المسلمين كالمفتي والقاضي يختص بنوع إعلام، لما روي أن زيد بن ثابت نصب لإعلامه بأوقات الصلاة وحضور الجماعة، ذكره محمد حله. وقال: أقامه لأبي يوسف حيث الأمراء للتثويب، وقال الشافعي وغيره من الأئمة: لا يثوب المؤذن، لهم ما روي أن عمر لما حج لقيه مؤذن مكة فآذنه بالصلاة فانتهره وقال: ألم يكن في أذانك ما يكفينا، وهو الأوجه، وعند المتقدمين هو مكروه، وهو قول الجمهور كما حكاه النووي في شرح المهذب لما روي أن علياً رأى مؤذناً يثوب في العشاء، فقال: أخرجوا هذا المبتدع من المسجد، وعن ابن عمر مثله، فعلى هذا التثويب بدعة فيمنع منه. (فتح)
And he performs tathwib, which is returning to notification after notification, like saying: 'al-salah al-salah' i.e., absolutely in all prayers. It is of four types: The first is ancient, which is 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' and it was after the Fajr adhan, except that the scholars of Kufa have attached it to the adhan. The second: an innovation introduced by the scholars of Kufa between the adhan and iqama: 'al-salah' twice, 'hayya 'ala al-falah' twice. And the tathwib of each town is according to their custom, either by clearing the throat or by 'al-salah al-salah' or 'qamat qamat'. The third: what the later scholars considered good: tathwib in all prayers due to the increased heedlessness of people. And what Abu Yusuf introduced for the ruler: saying 'al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-amir hayya 'ala al-salah hayya 'ala al-falah, al-salah yarhamuka Allah', and likewise every person engaged in the welfare of Muslims like the mufti and judge is distinguished by a type of notification, because it is narrated that Zayd ibn Thabit was appointed for his notification of prayer times and congregational attendance—Muhammad mentioned it. And he said: 'He established it for Abu Yusuf where the rulers (use) tathwib.' Al-Shafi'i and other imams said: The mu'adhdhin should not perform tathwib. Their proof is what is narrated that when Umar performed Hajj, he met the mu'adhdhin of Makkah who gave him the adhan for prayer, and he rebuked him and said: 'Is there not enough in your adhan for us?' And this is the most correct view. According to the earlier scholars, it is disliked, and it is the view of the majority as al-Nawawi narrated in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, because it is narrated that Ali saw a mu'adhdhin performing tathwib in the Isha prayer and said: 'Remove this innovator from the mosque!' And similar from Ibn Umar. So according to this, tathwib is an innovation and is prohibited. (Fath)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses the concept of tathwib, which means 'returning' to notification after the initial adhan. It includes additional phrases such as 'al-salah al-salah' or 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' in the context of Fajr. The commentator enumerates four types: the classic 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (which Kufan scholars consider part of the adhan), a later innovation between adhan and iqama, a general tathwib for all prayers introduced by later scholars, and a special tathwib for rulers and officials introduced by Abu Yusuf. The passage then presents the dispute: the early Hanafi masters and the majority considered tathwib disliked (makruh) and even an innovation (bid'ah) based on reports from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar. Al-Shafi'i also opposed it. However, the commentary notes that some later Hanafis adopted it for practical reasons. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) among the mutaqaddimin is that tathwib is makruh, but later Hanafi practice allowed it for necessity or custom.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwib): The act of returning to notification, i.e., an additional call after the adhan, with phrases like 'al-salah al-salah' or 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (in Fajr).
محدث (muhdath): An innovation (bid'ah) introduced after the time of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the ruling on tathwib according to the early Hanafi scholars (mutaqaddimin) as mentioned in the passage?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
Tathwib is a contested practice: early Hanafis and the majority deem it makruh, but later Hanafis allowed it for necessity.

Sitting Between Adhan and Iqama and Adhan for Missed Prayers
States rulings on pause and missed prayer adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the pause between adhan and iqama (including the exception for Maghrib) and on whether adhan is given for missed prayers, citing the supporting proofs and identifying the intra- and inter-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
A separation between adhan and iqama is required; Maghrib has a minimal pause. Missed prayers should be announced with both adhan and iqama.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two related yet distinct issues: the etiquette of the pause between the adhan and iqama, and the ruling on performing adhan for missed prayers. Both rulings are grounded in the Sunnah and have generated scholarly discussion, both within the Hanafi school (regarding the Maghrib pause) and between schools (regarding missed prayers). As we work through the text, pay close attention to the proofs cited and the nuanced positions of the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage treats two separate matters: first, the requirement of a pause (fasl) between adhan and iqama with an exception for Maghrib; second, the ruling on giving adhan for missed prayers (fāʼitah). Note the structure: 'ويجلس بينهما إلا في المغرب' then 'ويؤذن للفائتة'.
2
Analyze the proof for the pause
The author cites the hadith where the Prophet (ṣ) told Bilāl to leave a pause between adhan and iqama sufficient for people to complete wuḍūʼ or dinner. This establishes the principle that a pause is required (wājib) and that connecting them is disliked (makrūh). Note the absence of a fixed measure, leading to the estimations by Abū Ḥanīfa and the Ṣāḥibayn.
The text mentions different durations for different prayers, which are based on riwāyah from Ḥasan ibn Ziyād.
3
Examine the exception for Maghrib
The text states 'except in Maghrib' and then presents two views: Abū Ḥanīfa says the imam should stand silently for the length of three short verses; Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad say he should sit briefly. This is an intra-Hanafī ikhtilāf.
The rationale for the short pause is the tight time window of Maghrib.
4
Analyze the ruling on missed prayers
The text states that adhan is given for every missed prayer absolutely. It then mentions the opposing view of Mālik and al-Shāfiʻī, who consider the iqāma sufficient. The Hanafī proof is the hadith of Abū Qatāda, where the Prophet ordered Bilāl to give adhan for the missed Fajr prayer.
The hadith demonstrates the practice of the Prophet; the Hanafīs conclude that adhan is recommended (sunnah muʼakkadah) even for qaḍāʼ prayers.
5
Synthesize the two rulings and their practical implications
Now combine both: the pause between adhan and iqama is a general rule with a specific exception; the adhan for missed prayers is a recommended practice. Understand how these rulings affect daily worship and the importance of following the Sunnah even in making up prayers.
The muftā bihī for the Maghrib pause is to stand briefly (Abū Ḥanīfa), and for missed prayers, adhan is sunnah muʼakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجلس بينهما بقدر ما يحضر الملازمون للصلاة مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب لأنه لابد من الفصل بين الأذان والإقامة؛ إذ الوصل مكروه؛ لقوله عليه السلام لبلال : "اجعل بين أذانك وإقامتك نفساً يفرغ المتوضئ من وضوئه مهلاً والمتعشي من عشائه"، و لم يذكر مقدار الفصل، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة في الفجر قدر ما يقرأ عشرين آية، وفي الظهر والعشاء قدر أربع ركعات يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات وفي العصر بقدر ركعتين يقرأ فيهما عشرين آية، والأولى أن يصلى بينهما؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "بين كل أذانين صلاة" أي بين كل أذان وإقامة. (فتح) إلا في المغرب: فيسكت قائما قدر ثلاث آيات قصار، وقالا يجلس مقدار الجلسة بين الخطبتين. (مسكين) ويؤذن للفائتة: مطلقا أي كلها وقال مالك والشافعي يكتفي بالإقامة. (مسكين) وقال الشافعي: يكتفى بالإقامة، والحجة عليه ما روى أبو قتادة: كنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في غزاة، فعرسنا أي نزلنا آخر الليل، فما استيقظنا حتى أيقظنا حر الشمس، فارتحلنا حتى ارتفعت ثم نزلنا، فأمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بلالا فأذن، فصلينا ركعتين سنة، =
And he should sit between them (adhan and iqama) for a period sufficient for those who are regular in prayer to attend, while observing the preferred time. Because a separation between adhan and iqama is necessary; connecting them is disliked. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Bilal: 'Make between your adhan and iqama a pause enough for the one performing wudu to complete his wudu leisurely and the one eating dinner to finish his dinner leisurely.' He did not mention a specific amount. Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: In Fajr, the amount to recite twenty verses; in Zuhr and Isha, the amount of four rak'ahs reciting ten verses each; in Asr, the amount of two rak'ahs reciting twenty verses. And it is better to pray between them, because the Prophet said: 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' i.e., between every adhan and iqama. (Fath) Except in Maghrib: He remains standing silently for the amount of three short verses, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He sits for the amount of the sitting between the two khutbas. (Miskin) And he gives adhan for the missed prayer (fai'itah) absolutely, i.e., for all of them. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: The iqama suffices. (Miskin) And al-Shafi'i said: The iqama is sufficient. The proof against him is what Abu Qatada narrated: We were with the Messenger of God in a battle, and we camped at the end of the night, and we only woke up when the heat of the sun woke us. We traveled until the sun rose high, then we descended, and the Messenger of God ordered Bilal to give adhan, and we prayed two rak'ahs of sunnah, =
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage addresses two separate rulings: the pause between adhan and iqama, and the adhan for missed prayers. First, a separation (fasl) between adhan and iqama is required, as connecting them is disliked. The Prophet instructed Bilal to leave enough time for people to complete wudu or dinner. The specific duration varies: for Fajr, enough to recite 20 verses; for Zuhr and Isha, four rak'ahs; for Asr, two rak'ahs. It is recommended to pray voluntary prayers in between. For Maghrib, the pause is short: three short verses while standing, according to Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say one should sit briefly, like the sitting between the two khutbas of Jumu'ah. Second, the ruling on missed prayers: The Hanafi school holds that both adhan and iqama should be given for any missed prayer (fai'itah). Al-Shafi'i and Malik consider iqama sufficient. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada, where the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan for the missed Fajr prayer, and they prayed the sunnah first.

Key Terms
فائتة (fāʼitah): A missed obligatory prayer that is made up later (qaḍāʼ).
فصل (faṣl): The separation or pause between the adhan and iqama.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which prayer is the pause between adhan and iqama exceptionally short according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fajr
B) Maghrib
C) Isha
D) Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes a deliberate pause between adhan and iqama (shorter for Maghrib) and recommends adhan for all missed prayers, based on the practice of the Prophet.

The Ruling on Tathwib: A Hanafi-Shafi‘i Dispute
Rulings on tathwib with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tathwib, identify the Shafi‘i objection, and explain the Hanafi response using the evidence from the text.

Core Idea
Tathwib is permissible in Hanafi fiqh; Shafi‘is prohibit it as an innovation.

Tathwib refers to additional announcements made after the adhan. The Hanafi school allows it in various forms depending on need and custom, while the Shafi‘i school considers it a reprehensible innovation. This lesson unpacks the evidence for both positions and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Define tathwib and list its four types
Understand the linguistic meaning and identify the four categories mentioned in the text: old (as-salatu khairun mina al-nawm), Kufan innovation, later approval, and Abu Yusuf's introduction for authorities.
The four types show the evolution of tathwib.
2
Present the Hanafi evidence
Consider the practice of Kufan scholars, the appointment of Zayd ibn Thabit, and Abu Yusuf's action for the amir.
These indicate permissibility through custom and need.
3
Present the Shafi‘i evidence
Review the report of Umar rebuking the mu'adhdhin of Makkah and Ali's statement calling it innovation.
These form the basis for prohibition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and identify the practical difference
Hanafis respond that the objections target specific forms, not all tathwib; they restrict tathwib to custom and need. The result is that Hanafis permit tathwib; Shafi‘is consider it makruh.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثوب من التثويب وهو العود إلى الإعلام بعد الإعلام مثل أن يقول: الصلاة الصلاة] أي مطلقاً في جميع الصلوات وهو أربعة: الأول قديم، وهو الصلاة خير من النوم، وكان بعد أذان الفجر إلا أن علماء الكوفة الحقوه بالأذان والثاني: محدث أحدثه علماء الكوفة بين الأذان والإقامة على الصلاة" مرتين حي على الفلاح مرتين، وتثويب كل بلدة على ما تعارفوا به إما بالتنحنح أو بـ"الصلاة الصلاة" أو "قامت قامت"، والثالث ما استحسنه المتأخرون وهو التثويب في سائر الصلوات لزيادة غفلة الناس، وما أحدثه أبو يوسف للأمير بأن يقول: السلام عليك أيها الأمير حي . على الصلاة حي على الفلاح، الصلاة يرحمك الله، وكذلك كل من اشتغل بمصالح المسلمين كالمفتي والقاضي يختص بنوع إعلام، لما روي أن . نصب زيد بن ثابت لإعلامه بأوقات الصلاة وحضور الجماعة، ذكره محمد حله. وقال: أقامه لأبي يوسف حيث الأمراء للتثويب، وقال الشافعي وغيره من الأئمة: لا يثوب المؤذن، لهم ما روي أن نه لما حج لقيه مؤذن مكة فآذنه بالصلاة فانتهره وقال: ألم يكن في أذانك ما يكفينا، وهو الأوجه، وعند المتقدمين هو . مكروه، وهو قول الجمهور كما حكاه النووي في شرح المهذب" لما روي أن علياً رأى مؤذناً يثوب في العشاء، فقال: أخرجوا هذا المبتدع من المسجد، وعن ابن عمر مثله، فعلى هذا التثويب بدعة فيمنع منه. (فتح) ويجلس بينهما بقدر ما يحضر الملازمون للصلاة مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب] لأنه لابد من الفصل بين الأذان والإقامة؛ إذ الوصل مكروه؛ لقوله عليها لبلال : اجعل بين أذانك وإقامتك نفساً يفرغ المتوضئ من وضوئه مهلاً والمتعشي من عشائه ، و لم يذكر مقدار الفصل، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة في الفجر قدر ما يقرأ عشرين آية، وفي الظهر والعشاء قدر أربع ركعات يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات وفي العصر بقدر ركعتين يقرأ فيهما عشرين آية، والأولى أن يصلى بينهما؛ لقوله عليه: "بين" كل أذانين صلاة" أي بين كل أذان وإقامة. (فتح) إلا في المغرب: فيسكت قائما قدر ثلاث آيات قصار، وقالا يجلس مقدار الجلسة بين الخطبتين. (مسكين)
And tathwib - from al-tathwib which means returning to the announcement after the announcement, such as saying: 'as-salatu as-salatu (the prayer, the prayer)' - generally in all prayers. And it is four types: first, old, and it is 'as-salatu khairun mina al-nawm (prayer is better than sleep)', and it was after the fajr adhan, except that the Kufan scholars attached it to the adhan. Second, an innovation introduced by the Kufan scholars between the adhan and iqamah: 'as-salatu' twice, 'hayya 'ala al-falah' twice, and the tathwib of every town according to their custom, either by clearing the throat or by 'as-salatu as-salatu' or 'qamat qamat'. Third, what the later scholars approved: tathwib in all prayers due to the increased heedlessness of people. And what Abu Yusuf introduced for the amir: that he says 'as-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-amir, hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah, al-salatu yarhamuka Allah', and similarly anyone occupied with the interests of the Muslims like the mufti and judge is distinguished with a type of announcement, because it is narrated that Zayd ibn Thabit was appointed to inform him of the prayer times and congregation. Muhammad mentioned it. And he said: Abu Yusuf established it for him for the amirs for tathwib. Al-Shafi'i and other imams said: The mu'adhdhin should not perform tathwib. They have as evidence that when Umar performed Hajj, he met the mu'adhdhin of Makkah who called him to prayer, and he rebuked him and said: 'Was there not in your adhan enough for us?' And that is the most apparent. And according to the early scholars, it is makruh, and it is the opinion of the majority as al-Nawawi narrated in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, because it is narrated that Ali saw a mu'adhdhin performing tathwib in Isha and said: 'Expel this innovator from the mosque', and similar from Ibn Umar. So based on this, tathwib is an innovation and should be prevented. (Fath) And he sits between them for the duration that the constant attendees come for prayer while observing the preferred time, because a separation between adhan and iqamah is necessary; connecting them is makruh, due to his ﷺ saying to Bilal: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah a breath so that the one performing wudu can complete his wudu leisurely and the one dining can finish his dinner.' And he did not mention the amount of separation. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: in Fajr, the measure of reciting twenty verses; in Zuhr and Isha, the measure of four rak'ahs reciting ten verses in each rak'ah; in Asr, the measure of two rak'ahs reciting twenty verses in them. And it is better to pray between them, due to his ﷺ saying: 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' meaning between every adhan and iqamah. (Fath) Except in Maghrib: he remains silent standing for the measure of three short verses; and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he sits for the measure of the sitting between the two sermons. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage discusses tathwib, which is an additional call after the adhan. The author classifies tathwib into four types: (1) The ancient practice of saying 'as-salatu khairun mina al-nawm' after the Fajr adhan, which the Kufan scholars attached to the adhan itself. (2) An innovation (muhdath) by Kufan scholars of saying 'as-salatu' twice and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between adhan and iqamah. (3) The later scholars' approval of tathwib in all prayers due to people's heedlessness. (4) Abu Yusuf's introduction of tathwib for the amir with specific wording, also applied to muftis and judges. The Shafi'i school opposes all tathwib, citing the incident where Umar rebuked the mu'adhdhin of Makkah and the report that Ali called it an innovation. The Hanafi position acknowledges these reports but considers tathwib as recommended or permissible depending on need. The passage then discusses sitting between adhan and iqamah. It is makruh to connect them directly; the Prophet instructed a pause. The recommended interval varies by prayer: in Fajr, enough to recite twenty verses; in Zuhr and Isha, four rak'ahs with ten verses each; in Asr, two rak'ahs with twenty verses. It is better to pray voluntary prayers during the interval. For Maghrib, the mu'adhdhin should remain standing silently for about three short verses, not sit, according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said he should sit briefly.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwīb): Returning to the announcement after the adhan, such as saying 'as-salatu as-salatu' or other phrases to alert people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is haram.
D) It is makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tathwib as a flexible tool for alerting people, contrary to the Shafi'i view that it is an innovation.

The Sitting Between Adhan and Iqamah: Duration and Posture
Rulings on sitting between adhan and iqamah with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended duration of the pause between adhan and iqamah for each prayer, and identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding Maghrib.

Core Idea
A pause between adhan and iqamah is necessary; the duration varies by prayer, and for Maghrib the posture differs.

The Prophet instructed Bilal to leave a pause between the adhan and iqamah to allow people to prepare. The Hanafi scholars specified different lengths for each prayer. However, there is a difference of opinion on the posture during the Maghrib pause: Abu Hanifa says to stand silently, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say to sit briefly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: a pause is required
The text states that connecting adhan and iqamah directly is makruh; a separation is necessary. The Prophet's instruction to Bilal confirms this.
The pause is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Note the Prophet's instruction
The hadith: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah a breath so that the one performing wudu can complete his wudu leisurely and the one dining can finish his dinner.'
The instruction indicates a reasonable pause.
3
List the recommended durations for each prayer
Abu Hanifa specified: Fajr: twenty verses; Zuhr and Isha: four rak'ahs with ten verses each; Asr: two rak'ahs with twenty verses; Maghrib: standing for three short verses.
These durations are approximate.
4
Highlight the dispute on Maghrib posture
Abu Hanifa says the mu'adhdhin stands silently for three verses; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he sits briefly, like the pause between sermons.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

ويثوب من التثويب وهو العود إلى الإعلام بعد الإعلام مثل أن يقول: الصلاة الصلاة] أي مطلقاً في جميع الصلوات وهو أربعة: الأول قديم، وهو الصلاة خير من النوم، وكان بعد أذان الفجر إلا أن علماء الكوفة الحقوه بالأذان والثاني: محدث أحدثه علماء الكوفة بين الأذان والإقامة على الصلاة" مرتين حي على الفلاح مرتين، وتثويب كل بلدة على ما تعارفوا به إما بالتنحنح أو بـ"الصلاة الصلاة" أو "قامت قامت"، والثالث ما استحسنه المتأخرون وهو التثويب في سائر الصلوات لزيادة غفلة الناس، وما أحدثه أبو يوسف للأمير بأن يقول: السلام عليك أيها الأمير حي . على الصلاة حي على الفلاح، الصلاة يرحمك الله، وكذلك كل من اشتغل بمصالح المسلمين كالمفتي والقاضي يختص بنوع إعلام، لما روي أن . نصب زيد بن ثابت لإعلامه بأوقات الصلاة وحضور الجماعة، ذكره محمد حله. وقال: أقامه لأبي يوسف حيث الأمراء للتثويب، وقال الشافعي وغيره من الأئمة: لا يثوب المؤذن، لهم ما روي أن نه لما حج لقيه مؤذن مكة فآذنه بالصلاة فانتهره وقال: ألم يكن في أذانك ما يكفينا، وهو الأوجه، وعند المتقدمين هو . مكروه، وهو قول الجمهور كما حكاه النووي في شرح المهذب" لما روي أن علياً رأى مؤذناً يثوب في العشاء، فقال: أخرجوا هذا المبتدع من المسجد، وعن ابن عمر مثله، فعلى هذا التثويب بدعة فيمنع منه. (فتح) ويجلس بينهما بقدر ما يحضر الملازمون للصلاة مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب] لأنه لابد من الفصل بين الأذان والإقامة؛ إذ الوصل مكروه؛ لقوله عليها لبلال : اجعل بين أذانك وإقامتك نفساً يفرغ المتوضئ من وضوئه مهلاً والمتعشي من عشائه ، و لم يذكر مقدار الفصل، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة في الفجر قدر ما يقرأ عشرين آية، وفي الظهر والعشاء قدر أربع ركعات يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات وفي العصر بقدر ركعتين يقرأ فيهما عشرين آية، والأولى أن يصلى بينهما؛ لقوله عليه: "بين" كل أذانين صلاة" أي بين كل أذان وإقامة. (فتح) إلا في المغرب: فيسكت قائما قدر ثلاث آيات قصار، وقالا يجلس مقدار الجلسة بين الخطبتين. (مسكين)
And tathwib - from al-tathwib which means returning to the announcement after the announcement, such as saying: 'as-salatu as-salatu (the prayer, the prayer)' - generally in all prayers. And it is four types: first, old, and it is 'as-salatu khairun mina al-nawm (prayer is better than sleep)', and it was after the fajr adhan, except that the Kufan scholars attached it to the adhan. Second, an innovation introduced by the Kufan scholars between the adhan and iqamah: 'as-salatu' twice, 'hayya 'ala al-falah' twice, and the tathwib of every town according to their custom, either by clearing the throat or by 'as-salatu as-salatu' or 'qamat qamat'. Third, what the later scholars approved: tathwib in all prayers due to the increased heedlessness of people. And what Abu Yusuf introduced for the amir: that he says 'as-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-amir, hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah, al-salatu yarhamuka Allah', and similarly anyone occupied with the interests of the Muslims like the mufti and judge is distinguished with a type of announcement, because it is narrated that Zayd ibn Thabit was appointed to inform him of the prayer times and congregation. Muhammad mentioned it. And he said: Abu Yusuf established it for him for the amirs for tathwib. Al-Shafi'i and other imams said: The mu'adhdhin should not perform tathwib. They have as evidence that when Umar performed Hajj, he met the mu'adhdhin of Makkah who called him to prayer, and he rebuked him and said: 'Was there not in your adhan enough for us?' And that is the most apparent. And according to the early scholars, it is makruh, and it is the opinion of the majority as al-Nawawi narrated in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, because it is narrated that Ali saw a mu'adhdhin performing tathwib in Isha and said: 'Expel this innovator from the mosque', and similar from Ibn Umar. So based on this, tathwib is an innovation and should be prevented. (Fath) And he sits between them for the duration that the constant attendees come for prayer while observing the preferred time, because a separation between adhan and iqamah is necessary; connecting them is makruh, due to his ﷺ saying to Bilal: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah a breath so that the one performing wudu can complete his wudu leisurely and the one dining can finish his dinner.' And he did not mention the amount of separation. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: in Fajr, the measure of reciting twenty verses; in Zuhr and Isha, the measure of four rak'ahs reciting ten verses in each rak'ah; in Asr, the measure of two rak'ahs reciting twenty verses in them. And it is better to pray between them, due to his ﷺ saying: 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' meaning between every adhan and iqamah. (Fath) Except in Maghrib: he remains silent standing for the measure of three short verses; and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he sits for the measure of the sitting between the two sermons. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage discusses tathwib, which is an additional call after the adhan. The author classifies tathwib into four types: (1) The ancient practice of saying 'as-salatu khairun mina al-nawm' after the Fajr adhan, which the Kufan scholars attached to the adhan itself. (2) An innovation (muhdath) by Kufan scholars of saying 'as-salatu' twice and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between adhan and iqamah. (3) The later scholars' approval of tathwib in all prayers due to people's heedlessness. (4) Abu Yusuf's introduction of tathwib for the amir with specific wording, also applied to muftis and judges. The Shafi'i school opposes all tathwib, citing the incident where Umar rebuked the mu'adhdhin of Makkah and the report that Ali called it an innovation. The Hanafi position acknowledges these reports but considers tathwib as recommended or permissible depending on need. The passage then discusses sitting between adhan and iqamah. It is makruh to connect them directly; the Prophet instructed a pause. The recommended interval varies by prayer: in Fajr, enough to recite twenty verses; in Zuhr and Isha, four rak'ahs with ten verses each; in Asr, two rak'ahs with twenty verses. It is better to pray voluntary prayers during the interval. For Maghrib, the mu'adhdhin should remain standing silently for about three short verses, not sit, according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said he should sit briefly.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwīb): Returning to the announcement after the adhan, such as saying 'as-salatu as-salatu' or other phrases to alert people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib according to Abu Hanifa?
A) He sits as in other prayers.
B) He remains standing silently for about three short verses.
C) He must not sit at all.
D) He sits for the duration of the sermon pause.

Key Takeaway
The pause between adhan and iqamah is sunnah; its duration and posture vary by prayer, with a notable difference on Maghrib within the Hanafi school.
