Adhan for Missed Prayers (Fā'itah) – Wajib with Proof
Ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for missed prayers (fā'itah), cite the proof from the hadith of Abu Qatadah, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Maliki position.

Core Idea
Every missed fard prayer requires its own adhan and iqamah – this is wajib based on the Prophet's practice.

When a prayer is missed (fā'itah), should its make-up be announced with adhan and iqamah? The Hanafi school considers this obligatory, while some other schools permit only iqamah. This lesson examines the Hanafi proof from the Sunnah and the rule for multiple missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving adhan and iqamah for a missed obligatory prayer (fā'itah). The Hanafi ruling is that both are wajib (obligatory).
Wajib here means required; omission without excuse is blameworthy.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatadah: the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan for the missed Fajr prayer after they overslept.
The hadith is found in multiple collections; it is considered a sound (sahih) hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'so Bilal gave adhan' indicates obligation (wujub) because the default command for an act is obligation in Hanafi usul.
The absence of any contrary indication strengthens the wajh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that only iqamah is needed; adhan is not required. Their proof is based on other narrations or analogy with on-time prayers.
The Hanafi school responds that the explicit command in the hadith overrides analogical reasoning.
5
Apply the rule for multiple missed prayers
If several prayers are missed, there is a choice: either give adhan and iqamah for each, or give adhan and iqamah only for the first and iqamah for the rest. This flexibility comes from different reports of the Prophet's practice on the day of Khandaq.
The relied-upon position allows either method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم، أي المكلف المؤذن حال الأذان أي الأذان والإقامة ويستدير في صومعته... (مستخلص) ويؤذن للفائتة: [مطلقا أي كلها وقال مالك والشافعي يكتفي بالإقامة. (مسكين)] وقال الشافعي: يكتفى بالإقامة، والحجة عليه ما روى أبو قتادة كنا . مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في غزاة، فعرسنا أي نزلنا آخر الليل، فما استيقظنا حتى أيقظنا حر الشمس، فارتحلنا حتى ارتفعت ثم نزلنا، فأمر رسول الله له بلالا فأذن، فصلينا ركعتين سنة، =  ... ثم قام فصلينا الفرض و "للفائتة" : احتراز عن الفاسدة؛ فإنه لا أذان لها ولا إقامة. (فتح، مستخلص) وخير فيه: وجه التخيير أنه الله شغله المشركون يوم الخندق عن أربع صلوات، فقضاهن على الترتيب، كل صلاة بأذان وإقامة، وفي رواية أخرى بأذان وإقامة للأولى، وإقامة لكل واحدة من البواقي فلاختلاف الروايتين خيرنا في ذلك، والضابط عندنا أن كل فرض أداء وقضاء يؤذن له ويقام سواء أداه بجماعة أو منفرداً إلا الظهر يوم الجمعة في المصر، فإن أداءه بأذان وإقامة مكروه، ويروى ذلك عن علي، واستنان الأذان للقضاء محمول على ما إذا قضى في البيت، أما إذا قضى في المسجد فلا يؤذن له، ويكره القضاء في المسجد؛ لأن التأخير معصية فلا يظهرها. (فتح) للباقي: : إن اتحد مجلس القضاء فلو اختلف يؤذن ويقيم لكل ولزمه الإقامة للباقي. (مسكين) قبل وقت [مطلقاً أي في الجميع، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: يجوز للفجر في النصف الأخير من الليل. (ط)] بل يكره تحريماً؛ لقوله عليه: "يا بلال لا تؤذن حتى تتبين لك الفجر هكذا"، ومد يده عرضاً، وروى عبد العزيز بن أبي رواد عن نافع عن ابن عمر أن بلالاً أذن قبل طلوع الفجر، فغضب النبي الا الله وقال له: "ما حملك على ذلك؟" قال: استيقظت وأنا وسنان فظننت أن الفجر قد طلع، فأمره عليه أن ينادي أن العبد قد نام، ولأن الأذان إعلام بدخول الوقت، وقبل دخوله يكون كذبا، وذكر الحموي عن فتح الباري": أن من البدع المنكرة إيقاع الأذان الثاني قبل الفجر بنحو ثلاث ساعات في رمضان وكذا تأخير الأذان في المغرب بدرجة لتمكين الوقت، زعموا الاحتياط فأخروا الفطر وعجّلوا السحور، فخالفوا السنة فلذلك قلّ فيهم الخير وكثر فيهم الشر. (فتح) ويعاد فيه [ أي الأذان في الوقت إن أذن قبله (ع)] أي لعدم الاعتداد بالأوّل، وكذا الإقامة، لكن لو أقام في الوقت ولم يصل فوراً لا يجب إعادتها، لكن إذا طال الفصل أو وجد بينهما ما يعد قاطعاً كأكل ونحوه فينبغي الإعادة حينئذ. (فتح)
And he gives adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah... (Mukhtasar) And he gives adhan for the missed prayer: absolutely, i.e. all of it. And Malik and al-Shafi'i said: iqamah suffices. (Miskin) And al-Shafi'i said: iqamah suffices. The proof against him is what Abu Qatadah narrated: We were with the Messenger of Allah in a battle, and we stopped at the end of the night, and we did not wake up until the heat of the sun woke us. So we traveled until it rose, then we stopped, and the Messenger of Allah ordered Bilal to give adhan, so we prayed two rak'ahs of sunnah... then we stood and prayed the fard. And 'lit al-fā'itah' is a precaution against the invalid; for it has no adhan nor iqamah. (Fath, Mukhtasar) And he (the mu'adhdhin) is given a choice in it: the reason for the choice is that the Prophet was occupied by the polytheists on the day of Khandaq from four prayers, and he made them up in order, each prayer with adhan and iqamah. In another narration, with adhan and iqamah for the first, and iqamah for each of the remaining. Due to the difference of the two narrations, we are given a choice in that. The rule according to us is that every fard, whether performed on time or as make-up, has adhan and iqamah, whether done in congregation or alone, except Zuhr on Friday in the city, for performing it with adhan and iqamah is makruh, and that is narrated from Ali. And the desirability of adhan for qada' is based on when one makes it up at home. As for making it up in the mosque, he should not give adhan, and making up in the mosque is disliked because delay is a sin, so one should not publicize it. (Fath) For the remaining: if the place of qada' is the same, if it differs, he gives adhan and iqamah for each, and iqamah is necessary for the remaining. (Miskin) Before the time: absolutely, i.e. in all (prayers). And Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible for Fajr in the last half of the night. (T) Rather it is makruh tahriman, due to his saying: 'O Bilal, do not give adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you like this' and he spread his hand widthwise. And it is narrated from Nafi' from Ibn Umar that Bilal gave adhan before dawn, and the Prophet became angry and said: 'What made you do that?' He said: 'I woke up drowsy and thought dawn had broken.' So the Prophet ordered him to announce that the servant had slept. And because the adhan is an announcement of the entry of time, and before its entry it is a lie. Al-Hamawi mentioned from Fath al-Bari that among the reprehensible innovations is giving the second adhan about three hours before Fajr in Ramadan, and similarly delaying the adhan for Maghrib by a degree to ensure time, claiming caution, so they delayed breaking fast and hastened the pre-dawn meal, thus opposing the sunnah, and consequently good decreased among them and evil increased. (Fath) And it is repeated in it: meaning the adhan in the time if he gave it before the time, because the first is not considered, and similarly the iqamah. But if he gave iqamah in the time and did not pray immediately, it is not necessary to repeat it. However, if the interval is long or something that is considered a break occurs like eating etc., then repetition is appropriate then. (Fath)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage covers three sub-topics: (1) Adhan for missed prayers (fā'itah). The Hanafi position is that adhan and iqamah are given for every missed fard prayer, whether performed in congregation or alone. This is based on the hadith of Abu Qatadah where the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan for the missed Fajr prayer. Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that only iqamah suffices. The Hanafi school allows a choice for subsequent missed prayers: one may give both adhan and iqamah for all, or only for the first. The rule is that every fard, whether performed on time or as qada', requires adhan and iqamah, except Zuhr on Friday in a city where performing it with adhan and iqamah is makruh. If making up prayers in the mosque, it is disliked to give adhan there. (2) Adhan before the time is strictly prohibited (makruh tahriman). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i allow it for Fajr in the last half of the night, but Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon position forbid it. The proof is the Prophet's order to Bilal not to give adhan until dawn is clearly visible, and the incident where Bilal's premature adhan angered the Prophet. Adhan before time is considered a lie and a bad innovation, especially in Ramadan. (3) If adhan is given before time, it must be repeated when the time enters. Similarly, iqamah given before time must be repeated. However, if iqamah is given after time but prayer is delayed, it does not need repetition unless the delay is long or interrupted by eating, etc.

Key Terms
فائتة (fāʾita): A missed obligatory prayer that is made up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is not required; iqamah is enough
B) It is wajib (obligatory) to give both adhan and iqamah
C) It is makruh to give adhan
D) It is only required if praying in congregation

Key Takeaway
Every missed fard prayer requires its own adhan and iqamah – this is a wajib act established by the Prophet's practice.

Adhan Before Time – Prohibited Dislike
Ruling on adhan before time and its repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why adhan before the prescribed time is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) in the Hanafi school, identify the intra-Hanafi exception for Fajr, and state the ruling on repeating the adhan.

Core Idea
Adhan before time is a lie and an innovation – only allowed at the proper time, except for Fajr according to Abu Yusuf.

Giving the adhan before its time is a serious matter: it misleads people and distorts the Sunnah. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling of makruh tahriman, the proof from the Prophet's prohibition, and the exceptional view of Abu Yusuf regarding Fajr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving the adhan before the entry of the prayer time. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked), meaning it is sinful and must be avoided.
Makruh tahriman is close to haram in terms of prohibition, but the evidence is not absolutely definitive.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's statement to Bilal: 'O Bilal, do not give adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you.' Also the incident where Bilal gave adhan early and the Prophet became angry.
Both hadiths indicate prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'la tu'adhdhin' (do not give adhan) is a direct prohibition, which in Hanafi usul indicates tahrim (prohibition) unless there is a contrary indication. The anger at Bilal confirms the severity.
The phrase 'hata tatabayyana laka al-fajr' shows the condition for adhan is certainty of time entry.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf (and al-Shafi'i) allow adhan for Fajr in the last half of the night, considering it a form of preparation. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani prohibit it absolutely.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the prohibition, as the text states 'بل يكره تحريماً'.
5
Apply the ruling on repetition
If adhan is given before time, it must be repeated when the time enters. The first adhan is not valid. Similarly, iqamah given before time must be repeated, unless the prayer is performed immediately after the iqamah is given in the time.
A long break or a clear interruption (like eating) necessitates repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم، أي المكلف المؤذن حال الأذان أي الأذان والإقامة ويستدير في صومعته... (مستخلص) ويؤذن للفائتة: [مطلقا أي كلها وقال مالك والشافعي يكتفي بالإقامة. (مسكين)] وقال الشافعي: يكتفى بالإقامة، والحجة عليه ما روى أبو قتادة كنا . مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في غزاة، فعرسنا أي نزلنا آخر الليل، فما استيقظنا حتى أيقظنا حر الشمس، فارتحلنا حتى ارتفعت ثم نزلنا، فأمر رسول الله له بلالا فأذن، فصلينا ركعتين سنة، =  ... ثم قام فصلينا الفرض و "للفائتة" : احتراز عن الفاسدة؛ فإنه لا أذان لها ولا إقامة. (فتح، مستخلص) وخير فيه: وجه التخيير أنه الله شغله المشركون يوم الخندق عن أربع صلوات، فقضاهن على الترتيب، كل صلاة بأذان وإقامة، وفي رواية أخرى بأذان وإقامة للأولى، وإقامة لكل واحدة من البواقي فلاختلاف الروايتين خيرنا في ذلك، والضابط عندنا أن كل فرض أداء وقضاء يؤذن له ويقام سواء أداه بجماعة أو منفرداً إلا الظهر يوم الجمعة في المصر، فإن أداءه بأذان وإقامة مكروه، ويروى ذلك عن علي، واستنان الأذان للقضاء محمول على ما إذا قضى في البيت، أما إذا قضى في المسجد فلا يؤذن له، ويكره القضاء في المسجد؛ لأن التأخير معصية فلا يظهرها. (فتح) للباقي: : إن اتحد مجلس القضاء فلو اختلف يؤذن ويقيم لكل ولزمه الإقامة للباقي. (مسكين) قبل وقت [مطلقاً أي في الجميع، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: يجوز للفجر في النصف الأخير من الليل. (ط)] بل يكره تحريماً؛ لقوله عليه: "يا بلال لا تؤذن حتى تتبين لك الفجر هكذا"، ومد يده عرضاً، وروى عبد العزيز بن أبي رواد عن نافع عن ابن عمر أن بلالاً أذن قبل طلوع الفجر، فغضب النبي الا الله وقال له: "ما حملك على ذلك؟" قال: استيقظت وأنا وسنان فظننت أن الفجر قد طلع، فأمره عليه أن ينادي أن العبد قد نام، ولأن الأذان إعلام بدخول الوقت، وقبل دخوله يكون كذبا، وذكر الحموي عن فتح الباري": أن من البدع المنكرة إيقاع الأذان الثاني قبل الفجر بنحو ثلاث ساعات في رمضان وكذا تأخير الأذان في المغرب بدرجة لتمكين الوقت، زعموا الاحتياط فأخروا الفطر وعجّلوا السحور، فخالفوا السنة فلذلك قلّ فيهم الخير وكثر فيهم الشر. (فتح) ويعاد فيه [ أي الأذان في الوقت إن أذن قبله (ع)] أي لعدم الاعتداد بالأوّل، وكذا الإقامة، لكن لو أقام في الوقت ولم يصل فوراً لا يجب إعادتها، لكن إذا طال الفصل أو وجد بينهما ما يعد قاطعاً كأكل ونحوه فينبغي الإعادة حينئذ. (فتح)
And he gives adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah... (Mukhtasar) And he gives adhan for the missed prayer: absolutely, i.e. all of it. And Malik and al-Shafi'i said: iqamah suffices. (Miskin) And al-Shafi'i said: iqamah suffices. The proof against him is what Abu Qatadah narrated: We were with the Messenger of Allah in a battle, and we stopped at the end of the night, and we did not wake up until the heat of the sun woke us. So we traveled until it rose, then we stopped, and the Messenger of Allah ordered Bilal to give adhan, so we prayed two rak'ahs of sunnah... then we stood and prayed the fard. And 'lit al-fā'itah' is a precaution against the invalid; for it has no adhan nor iqamah. (Fath, Mukhtasar) And he (the mu'adhdhin) is given a choice in it: the reason for the choice is that the Prophet was occupied by the polytheists on the day of Khandaq from four prayers, and he made them up in order, each prayer with adhan and iqamah. In another narration, with adhan and iqamah for the first, and iqamah for each of the remaining. Due to the difference of the two narrations, we are given a choice in that. The rule according to us is that every fard, whether performed on time or as make-up, has adhan and iqamah, whether done in congregation or alone, except Zuhr on Friday in the city, for performing it with adhan and iqamah is makruh, and that is narrated from Ali. And the desirability of adhan for qada' is based on when one makes it up at home. As for making it up in the mosque, he should not give adhan, and making up in the mosque is disliked because delay is a sin, so one should not publicize it. (Fath) For the remaining: if the place of qada' is the same, if it differs, he gives adhan and iqamah for each, and iqamah is necessary for the remaining. (Miskin) Before the time: absolutely, i.e. in all (prayers). And Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible for Fajr in the last half of the night. (T) Rather it is makruh tahriman, due to his saying: 'O Bilal, do not give adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you like this' and he spread his hand widthwise. And it is narrated from Nafi' from Ibn Umar that Bilal gave adhan before dawn, and the Prophet became angry and said: 'What made you do that?' He said: 'I woke up drowsy and thought dawn had broken.' So the Prophet ordered him to announce that the servant had slept. And because the adhan is an announcement of the entry of time, and before its entry it is a lie. Al-Hamawi mentioned from Fath al-Bari that among the reprehensible innovations is giving the second adhan about three hours before Fajr in Ramadan, and similarly delaying the adhan for Maghrib by a degree to ensure time, claiming caution, so they delayed breaking fast and hastened the pre-dawn meal, thus opposing the sunnah, and consequently good decreased among them and evil increased. (Fath) And it is repeated in it: meaning the adhan in the time if he gave it before the time, because the first is not considered, and similarly the iqamah. But if he gave iqamah in the time and did not pray immediately, it is not necessary to repeat it. However, if the interval is long or something that is considered a break occurs like eating etc., then repetition is appropriate then. (Fath)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage covers three sub-topics: (1) Adhan for missed prayers (fā'itah). The Hanafi position is that adhan and iqamah are given for every missed fard prayer, whether performed in congregation or alone. This is based on the hadith of Abu Qatadah where the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan for the missed Fajr prayer. Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that only iqamah suffices. The Hanafi school allows a choice for subsequent missed prayers: one may give both adhan and iqamah for all, or only for the first. The rule is that every fard, whether performed on time or as qada', requires adhan and iqamah, except Zuhr on Friday in a city where performing it with adhan and iqamah is makruh. If making up prayers in the mosque, it is disliked to give adhan there. (2) Adhan before the time is strictly prohibited (makruh tahriman). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i allow it for Fajr in the last half of the night, but Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon position forbid it. The proof is the Prophet's order to Bilal not to give adhan until dawn is clearly visible, and the incident where Bilal's premature adhan angered the Prophet. Adhan before time is considered a lie and a bad innovation, especially in Ramadan. (3) If adhan is given before time, it must be repeated when the time enters. Similarly, iqamah given before time must be repeated. However, if iqamah is given after time but prayer is delayed, it does not need repetition unless the delay is long or interrupted by eating, etc.

Key Terms
فائتة (fāʾita): Missed prayer (not directly used in this lesson but referenced in the source).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on giving adhan before the proper time?
A) It is permissible (ja'iz)
B) It is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked)
C) It is recommended (sunnah)
D) It is forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Adhan before the prescribed time is prohibitively disliked; it must be repeated when the time enters.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on Disliked Mu'adhdhin (Adhan Givers)
Rulings on who is disliked to give the adhan: junub, minor impurity, woman, fasiq, and sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which persons are makruh to give adhan, explain the Hanafi ruling for each category, and state which adhan should be repeated.

Core Idea
Adhan from a junub or woman is valid but makruh; only the adhan (not iqamah) should be repeated.

The adhan is a sacred call, and the mu'adhdhin should ideally be in a state of purity and integrity. However, what if the caller is in major impurity, or a woman, or an open sinner? The Hanafi school rules that such adhan is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihan). This lesson unpacks each category, the intra-Hanafi difference on minor impurity, and the ruling on repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of disliked mu'adhdhin
List all persons mentioned: junub, muhdith (with dispute), woman, khuntha, fasiq, sitting, lying down, intoxicated.
The muhdith has two narrations; the relied-upon (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is not makruh.
2
Understand the ruling for each
For each, the adhan is valid but makruh tanzihan. The exception is the muhdith where the stronger narration says it is not makruh.
The text also notes the reasoning: for junub, he calls others to what he cannot respond; for woman, raising voice is sinful or fails announcement.
3
Analyze the dalil for junub
The hadith 'No one gives adhan except the one with wudu' is cited, along with logical reasoning.
This hadith is a dalil for dislike, but the adhan remains valid because the requirement of wudu is not a condition of validity in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the ruling on repetition (i'ada)
For the junub, the preferred view is to repeat only the adhan (not the iqamah) because adhan is prescribed to be repeated. For a woman, her adhan is also repeated.
Iqamah is not repeated because its repetition is not established in the sunnah.
5
Distinguish between adhan and iqamah
Note why adhan can be repeated but not iqamah: the sunnah allows repeating adhan for a better call, but iqamah is done just before prayer and is not typically repeated.
This distinction is important for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أذان الجنب إلخ شروع في صفات المؤذن بعد الفراغ من صفات الأذان، أن وينبغي يكون المؤذن عالماً بالسنة وأوقات الصلاة طالباً للثواب في أذانه، وأذان الجنب مكروه باتفاق الروايات، وأذان المحدث في رواية، ولا يكره في ظاهر الرواية، وكراهته؛ لقوله : "لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ ، ولأن الجنب يدعو الناس إلى ما لا يجيب إليه بنفسه، وكذا أذان المرأة، وكذا الخنثى، والفاسق وهو الخارج عن أمر الشرع بارتكاب كبيرة، وأذان القاعد مكروه إلا إذا أذن لنفسه، وعلم منه كراهة أذان المضطجع بالأولى، وأذان السكران ولو مؤمن مباح مكروه. (فتح) أذان الجنب وإقامته لأن لهما شبها بالصلاة فيعادان في رواية وفي رواية لا يعادان والأشبه أن يعاد الأذان لمشروعية تكراره دون الإقامة (ع) وإقامة المحدث: وفي كراهة أذانه روايتان كما في إقامة. وأذان المرأة: أي كره أيضاً؛ لأنها إن رفعت صوتها ارتكبت معصية، وإن لم ترفع فقد أخلت بالإعلام فإن أذنت يعاد. (ع)
And the adhan of the junub is disliked, etc. This is the start of the description of the mu'adhdhin after finishing the description of the adhan. It is fitting that the mu'adhdhin be knowledgeable of the sunnah and the prayer times, seeking reward in his adhan. The adhan of the junub is disliked by agreement of the narrations. The adhan of one with minor impurity (muhdith) is disliked in one narration, and not disliked in the apparent narration. Its dislike is due to his saying: 'No one gives adhan except the one who has wudu.' And because the junub calls people to what he himself does not respond to. Similarly, the adhan of a woman, and similarly the hermaphrodite (khuntha), and the fasiq (sinner who commits major sins), and the adhan of one sitting is disliked unless he gives adhan for himself. From this, the dislike of the adhan of one lying down is known by priority. And the adhan of an intoxicated person, even if he is a believer of permissible intoxication, is disliked. (Fath) The adhan and iqamah of the junub: because they resemble prayer, they are repeated in one narration, and in another narration they are not repeated. The more appropriate view is that the adhan is repeated due to the prescribed repetition, but not the iqamah. (Ayni) And the iqamah of the one with minor impurity: there are two narrations concerning the dislike of his adhan, as with his iqamah. And the adhan of a woman: it is also disliked. Because if she raises her voice, she commits a sin, and if she does not raise it, she fails in the announcement. If she gives adhan, it is repeated. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage deals with the qualifications of the mu'adhdhin (the caller to prayer). After listing the desirable qualities (knowledge of sunnah, prayer times, seeking reward), it discusses whose adhan is disliked (makruh). The following are disliked: (1) The junub (person in major impurity) – by agreement of all narrations, his adhan is makruh. (2) The muhdith (person without wudu) – there are two narrations: one considers it makruh, the other not. The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is not makruh, but the text also cites evidence for dislike. (3) A woman – because if she raises her voice, it is sinful (since women should not raise voices in public); if she doesn't, the announcement is not effective. (4) The khuntha (hermaphrodite) – by analogy to women. (5) The fasiq (open sinner) – his word is not trustworthy. (6) The one sitting – unless he gives adhan for himself. (7) The one lying down – by greater priority. (8) The intoxicated person – even if the intoxication is from a permissible substance. Regarding repetition (i'ada): For the junub, there is a difference of narration whether both adhan and iqamah are repeated; the preferred view is to repeat the adhan but not the iqamah. For a woman and the muhdith, similar considerations apply.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): Person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl.
المحدث (al-muhdith): Person without wudu (minor impurity).
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): Person who commits major sins openly; untrustworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the adhan given by a junub (person in major impurity)?
A) The adhan is invalid and must be repeated
B) The adhan is valid but disliked, and it is better to repeat only the adhan
C) The adhan is valid and no repetition is needed
D) The adhan is valid but both adhan and iqamah must be repeated

Key Takeaway
Adhan from a junub, woman, fasiq, etc. is valid but disliked, and only the adhan (not iqamah) should be repeated for the junub.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Adhan for Missed Prayers and Its Timing: Rulings and Proofs
Rulings on adhan for fawa'it, choice, timing, and repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for missed prayers and for adhan before time, apply the distinction between the first missed prayer and the remaining ones, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute on adhan before Fajr.

Core Idea
Adhan is tied to the time; giving it before time is invalid and must be repeated.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explained by Fath al-Qadir, presents two key rulings: the obligation of adhan for the first of missed prayers with a choice for the rest, and the absolute prohibition of adhan before the prescribed time. Both rulings are grounded in the Prophet's ﷺ practice and explicit commands. Let's unpack the legal reasoning and the dispute within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
Read the opening lines: adhan is given for the first missed prayer, and for the remaining there is a choice. Then, adhan before time is prohibited and must be repeated.
2
Understand the choice (ikhtiyar) for remaining fawa'it
The choice arises from two narrations from the Khandaq incident: one says each missed prayer had adhan and iqama; the other says adhan for the first and iqama for the rest. The Hanafi school allows either, but the recommended practice is to give adhan for the first and iqama for the rest.
The choice is due to differing reports, not personal preference.
3
Locate the dalil for prohibiting adhan before time
The text cites the hadith: 'O Bilal, do not give adhan until the dawn appears to you like this' and the incident where Bilal gave adhan early and the Prophet ﷺ became angry. These are clear prohibitions.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning (dalala) is qati' for Hanafis.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i allow adhan for Fajr in the last half of the night. The text rejects this as makruh tahrimi, relying on the explicit hadith.
The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if adhan is given before Fajr, according to Abu Hanifa it is invalid and must be repeated; according to Abu Yusuf it is valid and no repetition is needed.
This affects whether the congregation relies on that adhan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأذان. وكذا لأولىٰ الفوائت، وخير فيه للباقي، ولا يؤذن قبل وقت، ويعاد فيه. ثم قام فصلينا الفرض و "للفائتة" : احتراز عن الفاسدة؛ فإنه لا أذان لها ولا إقامة. (فتح، مستخلص) وخير فيه: وجه التخيير أنه الله شغله المشركون يوم الخندق عن أربع صلوات، فقضاهن على الترتيب، كل صلاة بأذان وإقامة، وفي رواية أخرى بأذان وإقامة للأولى، وإقامة لكل واحدة من البواقي فلاختلاف الروايتين خيرنا في ذلك، والضابط عندنا أن كل فرض أداء وقضاء يؤذن له ويقام سواء أداه بجماعة أو منفرداً إلا الظهر يوم الجمعة في المصر، فإن أداءه بأذان وإقامة مكروه، ويروى ذلك عن علي، واستنان الأذان للقضاء محمول على ما إذا قضى في البيت، أما إذا قضى في المسجد فلا يؤذن له، ويكره القضاء في المسجد؛ لأن التأخير معصية فلا يظهرها. (فتح) للباقي: : إن اتحد مجلس القضاء فلو اختلف يؤذن ويقيم لكل ولزمه الإقامة للباقي. (مسكين) قبل وقت [مطلقاً أي في الجميع، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: يجوز للفجر في النصف الأخير من الليل. (ط)] بل يكره تحريماً؛ لقوله عليه: "يا بلال لا تؤذن حتى تتبين لك الفجر هكذا"، ومد يده عرضاً، وروى عبد العزيز بن أبي رواد عن نافع عن ابن عمر أن بلالاً أذن قبل طلوع الفجر، فغضب النبي الا الله وقال له: "ما حملك على ذلك؟" قال: استيقظت وأنا وسنان فظننت أن الفجر قد طلع، فأمره عليه أن ينادي أن العبد قد نام، ولأن الأذان إعلام بدخول الوقت، وقبل دخوله يكون كذبا، وذكر الحموي عن فتح الباري": أن من البدع المنكرة إيقاع الأذان الثاني قبل الفجر بنحو ثلاث ساعات في رمضان وكذا تأخير الأذان في المغرب بدرجة لتمكين الوقت، زعموا الاحتياط فأخروا الفطر وعجّلوا السحور، فخالفوا السنة فلذلك قلّ فيهم الخير وكثر فيهم الشر. (فتح) ويعاد فيه [ أي الأذان في الوقت إن أذن قبله (ع)] أي لعدم الاعتداد بالأوّل، وكذا الإقامة، لكن لو أقام في الوقت ولم يصل فوراً لا يجب إعادتها، لكن إذا طال الفصل أو وجد بينهما ما يعد قاطعاً كأكل ونحوه فينبغي الإعادة حينئذ. (فتح)
Chapter of Prayer. Chapter of Adhan. And likewise for the first of missed prayers, and there is a choice in it for the remainder, and one should not give adhan before the time, and it is repeated in it. Then he stood and we prayed the obligatory prayer, and "for the missed" : a precaution against the invalid; for there is no adhan or iqama for it. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And choice in it: the reason for the choice is that Allah occupied the polytheists on the day of Khandaq from four prayers, so he made them up in order, each prayer with an adhan and iqama, and in another narration with adhan and iqama for the first, and iqama for each of the remaining; due to the difference of the two narrations we have a choice in that. And the rule with us is that every obligatory prayer, whether performed on time or made up, has adhan and iqama, whether performed in congregation or alone, except for Zuhr on Friday in the city, for performing it with adhan and iqama is disliked, and that is reported from Ali. And the recommendation of adhan for making up is understood when making up at home; but if making up in the mosque, then no adhan is given, and making up in the mosque is disliked because the delay is a sin and should not be displayed. (Fath) For the remainder: if the gathering for making up is one, but if it differs, he gives adhan and iqama for each, and iqama is incumbent for the rest. (Miskin) Before time: absolutely, i.e. in all prayers, and Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible for Fajr in the last half of the night. (T) Rather it is prohibitively disliked; because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'O Bilal, do not give adhan until the dawn appears to you like this,' and he spread his hand wide. And Abdul Aziz ibn Abi Rawad narrated from Nafi' from Ibn Umar that Bilal gave adhan before dawn, so the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, became angry and said to him: 'What made you do that?' He said: I woke up drowsy and thought that dawn had come, so he ordered him to announce that the servant had slept. And because the adhan is an announcement of the entrance of the time, and before its entrance it is a lie. And al-Hamawi mentioned from Fath al-Bari that among the reprehensible innovations is performing the second adhan before Fajr by about three hours in Ramadan, and likewise delaying the adhan for Maghrib by a degree to secure the time, claiming precaution, so they delayed the breaking of the fast and hastened the pre-dawn meal, contradicting the Sunnah, so goodness among them became little and evil became much. (Fath) And it is repeated in it, i.e. the adhan in the time if he gave it before it (A), i.e. because the first is not counted, and likewise the iqama, but if he performed iqama in the time and did not pray immediately, it is not obligatory to repeat it, but if the interval becomes long or a break occurs between them like eating and the like, then repetition is recommended at that time. (Fath)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage combines rulings from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq along with the sharh of Fath al-Qadir. It opens by establishing that adhan is given for the first of missed prayers (fawa'it), and for the remaining ones there is a choice (ikhtiyar) based on two narrations from the incident of the Khandaq (trench) when the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions missed four prayers. The rule agreed upon in the Hanafi school is that every obligatory prayer—whether performed on time (ada') or made up (qada')—has both adhan and iqama, except for Zuhr on Friday in the city where it is disliked. A key principle is that adhan for qada' is recommended only when making up at home; if in the mosque, it is not given because the delay is a sin. The second part deals with adhan before the time, which is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i allow it for Fajr after half the night. The proof is the Prophetic hadith telling Bilal to wait until dawn is clear. The third ruling says that if adhan was given before time, it must be repeated in the time. Similarly, iqama given before time must be repeated, unless the prayer is performed immediately after the time enters. If there is a long gap or a break, repetition is recommended.

Key Terms
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed prayers (plural of fa'itah) that are made up after their time.
التخيير (al-takhyir): Choice or option; in this context, the option to give adhan for the remaining missed prayers or not, based on two narrations.
مكروه تحريماً (makruh tahrimi): Prohibitively disliked; an act that is sinful to perform but not as severe as haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a person gives adhan for Fajr before the true dawn?
A) The adhan is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) The adhan is invalid and must be repeated in the time.
C) The adhan is valid but the iqama must be repeated.
D) The adhan is recommended and should be repeated only if the person wishes.

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a time-bound announcement; premature adhan is invalid and must be repeated.

Disliked Adhan: Whose Adhan is Makruh and Why
Rulings on whose adhan and iqama are disliked and their repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which individuals' adhan is disliked in the Hanafi school, state the evidence from the hadith, and explain the relied-upon view on repetition.

Core Idea
Adhan of a junub is disliked by consensus; adhan of a muhdith is not disliked in the strong narration.

This lesson explores the qualities of the mu'adhdhin and the legal ruling on adhan given by various individuals. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists several persons whose adhan is disliked, and the commentary from Fath al-Qadir expands on the proof and the intra-madhhab differences. Understanding these rulings ensures that the call to prayer is performed in the most proper manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the adhan (and iqama) of a junub, muhdith, woman, fasiq, qa'id, and sakran. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The matn begins with 'وكره أذان الجنب' (and the adhan of the junub is disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ' (Only one with wudu should give adhan). This is an ahad hadith.
The commentary explains the dislike is based on this hadith and the analogy that a junub calls people to something he cannot respond to.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling. The command form 'لا يؤذن' indicates prohibition, but here it is interpreted as dislike because the adhan itself is valid but the state of the caller is disliked.
Hanafi usul: a command from the Prophet indicates obligation unless there is evidence to the contrary.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the muhdith and the repetition of adhan. For muhdith, one narration says disliked, the apparent narration says not disliked. For repetition of adhan from a junub, there are two narrations.
The commentary says 'الأشبه أن يعاد الأذان' (the more appropriate is to repeat the adhan).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: adhan of a junub is disliked and should be repeated; the iqama is not repeated. For muhdith, the adhan is not disliked.
This is from the zahir al-riwayah and the tarjih of the commentator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أذان الجنب إلخ شروع في صفات المؤذن بعد الفراغ من صفات الأذان، أن وينبغي يكون المؤذن عالماً بالسنة وأوقات الصلاة طالباً للثواب في أذانه، وأذان الجنب مكروه باتفاق الروايات، وأذان المحدث في رواية، ولا يكره في ظاهر الرواية، وكراهته؛ لقوله : "لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ"، ولأن الجنب يدعو الناس إلى ما لا يجيب إليه بنفسه، وكذا أذان المرأة، وكذا الخنثى، والفاسق وهو الخارج عن أمر الشرع بارتكاب كبيرة، وأذان القاعد مكروه إلا إذا أذن لنفسه، وعلم منه كراهة أذان المضطجع بالأولى، وأذان السكران ولو مؤمن مباح مكروه. (فتح) أذان الجنب وإقامته لأن لهما شبها بالصلاة فيعادان في رواية وفي رواية لا يعادان والأشبه أن يعاد الأذان لمشروعية تكراره دون الإقامة (ع) وإقامة المحدث: وفي كراهة أذانه روايتان كما في إقامة. وأذان المرأة: أي كره أيضاً؛ لأنها إن رفعت صوتها ارتكبت معصية، وإن لم ترفع فقد أخلت بالإعلام فإن أذنت يعاد. (ع) ثم صفحة 66: والسكران لفسقه أو لعدم معرفته بدخول الوقت، ويستحب إعادته وكذا حكم صبيّ لا يعقل ومجنون ومعتوه. (رمز الحقائق: ٤٩/١]
And the adhan of the junub is disliked, etc. Beginning of the section on the qualities of the mu'adhdhin after finishing the qualities of the adhan. And it is proper that the mu'adhdhin be knowledgeable of the Sunnah and the prayer times, seeking reward in his adhan. The adhan of the junub is disliked by agreement of the narrations. The adhan of the one with minor impurity is disliked in one narration and not disliked in the apparent narration, and its dislike is because of his statement: 'Only one who has wudu should give adhan,' and because the junub calls people to that which he himself does not respond to. Likewise the adhan of a woman, likewise the hermaphrodite, and the fasiq who is one who leaves the command of the Sharia by committing a major sin. And the adhan of one sitting is disliked unless he gives adhan for himself, and from this it is understood that the adhan of one lying down is disliked as a priority. The adhan of a drunk person, even if he is a believer and excused, is disliked. (Fath) The adhan of the junub and his iqama: because they have a resemblance to prayer, so they are repeated in one narration, and in another narration they are not repeated, and the more appropriate is that the adhan be repeated due to the legislated nature of its repetition, not the iqama (A). And the iqama of one with minor impurity: regarding the dislike of his adhan, there are two narrations as in the iqama. And the adhan of a woman: it is also disliked because if she raises her voice she commits a sin, and if she does not raise it she fails in the announcement. If she gives adhan, it is repeated. (A) Then page 66: And the drunk person: due to his fasiq-ness or his lack of knowledge of the entrance of the time, and it is recommended to repeat it. Likewise the ruling of a child who does not reason, a madman, and an idiot. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage addresses the qualities of the mu'adhdhin and lists those whose adhan is disliked (makruh). The matn (Kanz) mentions junub, muhdith, woman, fasiq, and qa'id. The commentary (Fath al-Qadir and others) adds the sakran (drunk). It explains that the mu'adhdhin should be knowledgeable and seeking reward. The dislike for the junub is agreed upon; for the muhdith (one in minor impurity) there is a difference of narration: in one it is disliked, in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) it is not disliked. The proof is the hadith 'Only one with wudu should give adhan.' The dislike for a woman is because she cannot fulfill the announcement properly (either by raising her voice - which is sinful - or not raising it enough). The adhan of a fasiq is disliked because his word is not trustworthy. The adhan of a sitting person is disliked unless he is alone. The adhan of a drunk person is also disliked due to his lack of awareness. Regarding repetition of the adhan and iqama when given by a junub or muhdith, there are two narrations: the more appropriate view is that only the adhan is repeated, not the iqama, because adhan is legislated to be repeated. The commentary also extends the ruling to a child, madman, and idiot.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl.
المحدث (al-muhdith): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath) that invalidates wudu.
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A person who openly commits major sins or persists in minor sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view, if a junub gives adhan, what must be done?
A) The adhan is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) The adhan is disliked but valid, no repetition.
C) The adhan should be repeated, but the iqama need not be.
D) Both adhan and iqama must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The adhan of a junub is disliked by consensus, and the relied-upon view is to repeat only the adhan; the adhan of a muhdith is not disliked in the strong narration.

Adhan of Specific Individuals: Permissibility and Reasoning
Adhan of certain persons is not disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the individuals whose adhan is not disliked and explain the Hanafi reasoning for each.

Core Idea
The adhan of a slave, child of adultery, blind, and bedouin is not disliked — only the fasiq's adhan is disliked.

In this passage, we learn that the Hanafi school does not consider the adhan of certain individuals as disliked, even though they may have social or moral shortcomings. The key distinction turns on whether the person's word is accepted in religious matters (like the bedouin) versus being a fasiq (open sinner). This lesson explores each category and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
List the individuals
From the matn: slave, child of adultery (walad al-zina), blind (a'ma), and bedouin (a'rabi). Also later: drunk (sakran), child who does not reason (sabi la ya'qil), madman (majnun), and idiot (ma'tuh).
The commentary adds that the drunk's adhan is disliked due to his fasiq-ness or ignorance of time.
2
State the ruling for each
The matn says 'لا أذان' meaning their adhan is not disliked (i.e., it is permissible and valid). For the drunk, it is recommended to repeat the adhan. For the child, madman, and idiot, the same rule applies as the drunk.
Repeat of adhan is recommended only if the first was invalid due to time error or fasiq-ness.
3
Explain the reasoning for bedouin
The commentary states that the word of these individuals (slave, etc.) is accepted in religious matters (their testimony is accepted for matters like sighting the new moon), unlike the fasiq whose word is rejected.
The fasiq's adhan is disliked because his word is not accepted.
4
Distinguish the fasiq
A fasiq is an open sinner whose testimony is rejected. Therefore, his adhan is disliked. The others are not necessarily sinners, so their adhan is not disliked.
This highlights the importance of moral probity (adala) in religious office.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا أذان العبد وولد الزنا والأعمى والأعرابي، وكره تركهما للمسافر لا لمصل أي لا يكره في بيته في المصر، وندبا لهما لا للنساء. والسكران لفسقه أو لعدم معرفته بدخول الوقت، ويستحب إعادته وكذا حكم صبيّ لا يعقل ومجنون ومعتوه. (رمز الحقائق: ٤٩/١] والأعرابي : لأن قول هؤلاء يقبل في الأمور الدينية بخلاف الفاسق. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٩/١] وتركهما : لقوله عليها لابني أبي مليكة: "إذا سافرتما فأذنا وأقيما"؛ ولأنه يكون تاركاً للصلاة بالجماعة حقيقةً وتشبيها، وترك الصلاة بالجماعة مكروه. (مستخلص) للمسافر: لأن السفر لا يسقط الجماعة، فلا يسقط ما هو من لوازمها. (ع) لا لمصل في بيته : أي مطلقا لقول ابن مسعود الله: "أذان الحي يكفينا" حين صلّى بعلقمة والأسود في بيته، فقيل له: "ألا تؤذن وتقيم؟"، وقيد بالمصر؛ لأنه يكره تركهما في السفر مطلقا، وقال مالك: إذا صلى وحده في الصحراء أو في بيته لا يؤذن ولا يقيم؛ لأنهما من شعار الجماعة فلا تقام بدونها. (فتح) وندبا لهما [ أي للمسافر وللمصلي في بيته ليكون الأداء على هيئة الجماعة رمز الحقائق: ٤٩/١)] خلافاً للمالك. تتمة: رجل في المسجد يقرأ القرآن فسمع الأذان لا يترك القراءة؛ لأنه أجابه بالحضور، ولو كان في منزله يترك القراءة ويجيب والإجابة: أن يقول كل ما يقول المؤذن إلا في الحيعلتين فإنه يقول مكانهما: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم ومكان قوله: "الصلاة خير من النوم" : "صدقت وبررت وبالحق نطقت، ويجيب الإقامة ندباً، ويقول عند قد قامت الصلاة: "أقامها الله وأدامها، وفي الظهيرية : يقول مثل قول المؤذن في الجميع، وهكذا روي عن النبي ، و الأذان بغير العربية لا يصح وإن عرف أنه أذان، دخل المسجد والمؤذن يقيم يقعد إلى قيام الإمام، في مصلاه رئيس المحلة لا ينتظر إلا إذا كان شريراً والوقت متسع، يكره له أن يؤذن في مسجدين، ولاية الأذان والإقامة لباني المسجد مطلقاً، وكذا الإمامة لو عدلاً. (فتح) لا للنساء: لأنهما من سنن الجماعة المستحبة، فلا يندبان لهن سواء صلين بجماعة أو لا. كشف الحقائق: ٣٩/١]
There is no adhan (disliked) for the slave, the child of adultery, the blind, and the bedouin. And leaving them (both; adhan and iqama) is disliked for the traveler, not for one who prays in his house, i.e. it is not disliked in his house in the city. And they are recommended for them both (traveler and one alone), not for women. And the drunk: due to his fasiq-ness or his lack of knowledge of the entrance of the time, and it is recommended to repeat it. Likewise the ruling of a child who does not reason, a madman, and an idiot. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49) And the bedouin: because the word of these (slave, etc.) is accepted in religious matters unlike the fasiq. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49) And leaving them: because of his statement, peace be upon him, to the two sons of Abi Mulayka: 'When you travel, give adhan and iqama'; and because he becomes one leaving congregational prayer in reality and by imitation, and leaving congregational prayer is disliked. (Mustakhlas) For the traveler: because travel does not remove congregation, so it does not remove what is necessary for it. (A) Not for one who prays in his house: i.e. absolutely, because of the statement of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The adhan of the neighborhood suffices us' when he prayed with Alqama and al-Aswad in his house, and it was said to him: 'Will you not give adhan and iqama?', and it is restricted to the city because leaving them in travel is disliked absolutely. And Malik said: If one prays alone in the desert or in his house, he does not give adhan or iqama because they are symbols of congregation and are not performed without it. (Fath) And they are recommended for them, i.e. for the traveler and for the one praying in his house so that the performance is in the form of a congregation (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49) contrary to Malik. Supplement: A man in the mosque reciting Quran when he hears the adhan does not leave recitation because he responds by attending; but if he is in his house, he leaves recitation and responds. And the response is to say everything the mu'adhdhin says except the two hay'alahs (hayya ala) where he says in their place: 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billahi al-aliy al-azeem' and in place of his saying 'Al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm': 'Sadaqta wa bararta wa bil-haqqi nataqta.' He responds to the iqama by way of recommendation, and says when 'Qad qamati al-salah' is said: 'Aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha.' In al-Zahiriyya, he says like what the mu'adhdhin says in all, and this is reported from the Prophet. And the adhan in a language other than Arabic is not valid even if it is known as adhan. If one enters the mosque while the mu'adhdhin is performing iqama, he sits until the imam stands. The head of the district in his prayer place does not wait unless he is evil (and time is ample). It is disliked for him to give adhan in two mosques. The authority of adhan and iqama belongs to the builder of the mosque absolutely, and likewise the imamate if he is just. (Fath) Not for women: because they (adhan and iqama) are from the recommended sunan of congregation, so they are not recommended for them whether they pray in congregation or not. (Kashf al-Haqa'iq 1/39)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on who may give adhan. The matn states that the adhan of a slave, child of adultery, blind, and bedouin is not disliked. The commentary explains that their word is accepted in religious matters, unlike the fasiq. Then it discusses the ruling for a traveler and one who prays alone in his house: it is disliked to leave adhan and iqama for the traveler (because travel does not exempt one from congregation), but it is not disliked for one in his house in the city. The proof is the hadith to the two sons of Abi Mulayka commanding adhan and iqama when traveling, and the action of Ibn Mas'ud who did not give adhan when praying in his house because the neighborhood adhan sufficed. The Maliki position is that no adhan is given when alone, but the Hanafi position is that it is recommended (sunnah muakkadah) for both traveler and the one in his house to give adhan and iqama, as it makes the prayer resemble congregation. The passage then provides a supplement on answering the adhan, the ruling on adhan in non-Arabic, entering the mosque during iqama, the head of the district waiting, and who has the authority over the adhan. Finally, it confirms that adhan and iqama are not recommended for women, as they are not obligated to attend congregation.

Key Terms
الأعرابي (al-a'rabi): A bedouin (a desert Arab) who may be ignorant of some rulings, but his word is accepted in religious matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following individuals' adhan is disliked according to the Hanafi school?
A) A slave
B) A bedouin
C) A fasiq
D) A blind person

Key Takeaway
The adhan of a bedouin, slave, child of adultery, and blind person is valid and not disliked; only the fasiq's adhan is disliked.

Adhan for Traveler and Solitary Worshipper: Recommendation and Proof
Adhan for traveler and solitary worshipper is recommended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommendation for adhan and iqama for a traveler and one praying alone, cite the hadith proof, and compare the Hanafi and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqama are recommended for the traveler and the solitary worshipper to maintain the form of congregation.

This lesson explores the ruling that it is recommended (sunnah) for a traveler and for a person praying alone in his home in the city to give adhan and iqama. The hadith of the Prophet to the sons of Abi Mulayka supports this, and the Hanafi school differs from Malik who holds that adhan is only for congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The traveler (musafir) and the one who prays alone in his house in the city (musalli fi baytihi fi al-misr).
The ruling differs: leaving adhan is disliked for the traveler but not for the one at home.
2
State the ruling
It is recommended (sunnah muakkadah) for both to give adhan and iqama. The matn says: 'و ندبا لهما' (and they are recommended for them two).
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the dalil
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet to the two sons of Abi Mulayka: 'إذا سافرتما فأذنا وأقيما' (When you travel, give adhan and iqama). The imperative indicates recommendation.
Also, leaving adhan makes one resemble someone who abandons congregation, which is disliked.
4
Consider the Maliki position
Imam Malik holds that if one prays alone, he should not give adhan or iqama, because they are symbols of congregation.
The Hanafi school counters that the command in the hadith is general and includes travel.
5
Note the exception for women
Women are not recommended to give adhan or iqama, even if they pray in congregation among themselves.

There is no adhan (disliked) for the slave, the child of adultery, the blind, and the bedouin. Likewise the ruling of a child who does not reason, a madman, and an idiot. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49) And the bedouin: because the word of these (slave, etc.) is accepted in religious matters unlike the fasiq. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49) And leaving them: because of his statement, peace be upon him, to the two sons of Abi Mulayka: 'When you travel, give adhan and iqama'; and because he becomes one leaving congregational prayer in reality and by imitation, and leaving congregational prayer is disliked. (Mustakhlas) For the traveler: because travel does not remove congregation, so it does not remove what is necessary for it. (A) Not for one who prays in his house: i.e. absolutely, because of the statement of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The adhan of the neighborhood suffices us' when he prayed with Alqama and al-Aswad in his house, and it was said to him: 'Will you not give adhan and iqama?', and it is restricted to the city because leaving them in travel is disliked absolutely. And Malik said: If one prays alone in the desert or in his house, he does not give adhan or iqama because they are symbols of congregation and are not performed without it. (Fath) And they are recommended for them, i.e. for the traveler and for the one praying in his house so that the performance is in the form of a congregation (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/49) contrary to Malik. Supplement: A man in the mosque reciting Quran when he hears the adhan does not leave recitation because he responds by attending; but if he is in his house, he leaves recitation and responds. And the response is to say everything the mu'adhdhin says except the two hay'alahs (hayya ala) where he says in their place: 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billahi al-aliy al-azeem' and in place of his saying 'Al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm': 'Sadaqta wa bararta wa bil-haqqi nataqta.' He responds to the iqama by way of recommendation, and says when 'Qad qamati al-salah' is said: 'Aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha.' In al-Zahiriyya, he says like what the mu'adhdhin says in all, and this is reported from the Prophet. And the adhan in a language other than Arabic is not valid even if it is known as adhan. If one enters the mosque while the mu'adhdhin is performing iqama, he sits until the imam stands. The head of the district in his prayer place does not wait unless he is evil (and time is ample). It is disliked for him to give adhan in two mosques. The authority of adhan and iqama belongs to the builder of the mosque absolutely, and likewise the imamate if he is just. (Fath) Not for women: because they (adhan and iqama) are from the recommended sunan of congregation, so they are not recommended for them whether they pray in congregation or not. (Kashf al-Haqa'iq 1/39)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on who may give adhan. The matn states that the adhan of a slave, child of adultery, blind, and bedouin is not disliked. The commentary explains that their word is accepted in religious matters, unlike the fasiq. Then it discusses the ruling for a traveler and one who prays alone in his house: it is disliked to leave adhan and iqama for the traveler (because travel does not exempt one from congregation), but it is not disliked for one in his house in the city. The proof is the hadith to the two sons of Abi Mulayka commanding adhan and iqama when traveling, and the action of Ibn Mas'ud who did not give adhan when praying in his house because the neighborhood adhan sufficed. The Maliki position is that no adhan is given when alone, but the Hanafi position is that it is recommended (sunnah muakkadah) for both traveler and the one in his house to give adhan and iqama, as it makes the prayer resemble congregation. The passage then provides a supplement on answering the adhan, the ruling on adhan in non-Arabic, entering the mosque during iqama, the head of the district waiting, and who has the authority over the adhan. Finally, it confirms that adhan and iqama are not recommended for women, as they are not obligated to attend congregation.

Key Terms
المصلي في بيته (al-musalli fi baytihi): One who prays alone at home in the city, not in a congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the ruling on adhan for a traveler according to the Hanafi school?
A) Obligatory
B) Recommended and leaving it is disliked
C) Recommended and leaving it is not disliked
D) Prohibited

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqama are recommended for the traveler and solitary worshipper to maintain the form of congregation, differing from the Maliki school.

Salah — Prayer

Supplementary Rulings on Adhan: Response, Language, and Authority
Supplementary adhan rulings: response, language, authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how to respond to adhan and iqama, state the conditions for a valid adhan in terms of language and place, and identify who has authority over adhan and imamate.

Core Idea
Responding to adhan is recommended with specific phrases; adhan must be in Arabic; the mosque builder has authority over adhan and imamate.

This lesson covers additional rulings from the same passage: the manner of responding to adhan, the invalidity of non-Arabic adhan, etiquette when entering the mosque during iqama, and who holds the right to appoint the mu'adhdhin and imam. These details are essential for the practical implementation of the adhan in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Learn how to respond to adhan
One should repeat what the mu'adhdhin says, except for 'hayya ala' where one says 'la hawla wa la quwwata...' and for 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' where one says 'sadaqta wa bararta...'. For iqama, one says 'aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha' at 'qad qamati al-salah'.
There is a difference of opinion: in al-Zahiriyya, one repeats everything.
2
Understand the ruling on adhan in non-Arabic
Adhan in any language other than Arabic is not valid, even if the listener understands it.
This is because adhan is a ritual with specific wording.
3
Know the etiquette when entering during iqama
If a person enters the mosque while the mu'adhdhin is performing iqama, he should sit until the imam stands, not stand for prayer immediately.
This is to wait for the congregation.
4
Recognize the authority of the mosque builder
The builder (bani al-masjid) has the right to appoint the mu'adhdhin and the imam, provided he is just.
This authority is absolute.
5
Note the ruling for women
Adhan and iqama are not recommended for women, even if they pray in congregation.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on Adhan and Iqamah: Sunnah Mu'akkadah for Men
Exposition of adhan rulings: who gives, traveler, response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for men and women, explain the proof from the hadith of the sons of Abu Mulayka, and apply the ruling to the traveler and one praying alone in the city.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for men, not fard, and are not required for women.

This lesson examines the legal status of adhan (call to prayer) and iqamah (second call) in the Hanafi school. While some may think they are obligatory, the Hanafi position is that they are strongly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah) for men in congregational prayer, but not for women. We will explore the primary evidence from the hadith and the reasoning behind the school's position, as well as key exceptions for travelers and those praying alone.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah
Identify the hukm level (sunnah mu'akkadah) for men, and that it is not prescribed for women.
The ruling applies to congregational prayers.
2
Analyze the primary proof
Examine the hadith: 'When you travel, give adhan and iqamah.' Discuss the Hanafi interpretation that the imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) due to other evidence.
The hadith is from the Prophet to the two sons of Abu Mulayka.
3
Identify the exception for a traveler
Note that it is disliked to omit them when traveling, even if praying alone.
Travel does not drop the congregation, so its emblems are not dropped.
4
Distinguish the case of one praying alone in the city
It is not disliked to omit them, based on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud who said 'the adhan of the tribe suffices us'.
This is specific to those in a city where congregational adhan is heard.
5
Explain the cross-madhhab difference
Compare with the Maliki position that adhan is not done when praying alone at all.
The Hanafi view considers it sunnah even for the traveler and recommended for the one alone in the city.

Source Text

The Book of Prayer. Chapter of Adhan. And the drunkard, no adhan of the slave, the illegitimate child, the blind, and the bedouin. And it is disliked to leave them (adhan and iqamah) for the traveler, but not for one who prays alone in his house in the city. And they are Sunnah for these two but not for women. i.e. adhan and iqamah are not Sunnah. i.e. it is not disliked to leave them. And the drunkard because of his sin or his lack of knowledge of the entry of time, and it is recommended to repeat it, and similarly the ruling of an unintelligent child, a madman, and an imbecile. Code of Realities: 49/1] And the bedouin: because the statement of these is accepted in religious matters unlike the sinner. [Code of Realities: 49/1] And leaving them: due to his saying, peace be upon him, to the two sons of Abu Mulayka: 'When you travel, give adhan and iqamah'; and because he becomes a person leaving prayer with congregation in reality and by comparison, and leaving prayer with congregation is disliked. (Extract) For the traveler: because travel does not drop the congregation, so it does not drop what is necessary for it. (Ayni) Not for one who prays in his house: i.e. absolutely, due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The adhan of the tribe suffices us' when he prayed with 'Alqamah and al-Aswad in his house, and it was said to him: 'Will you not give adhan and iqamah?', and it is restricted to the city; because leaving them is disliked in travel absolutely. And Malik said: If he prays alone in the desert or in his house, he does not give adhan nor iqamah; because they are from the emblems of congregation, so they are not established without it. (Fath) And they are Sunnah for these two [i.e. for the traveler and for the one praying in his house so that the performance is in the manner of congregation (Code of Realities: 49/1)] contrary to Malik. Addendum: A man in the mosque reciting Quran when he hears the adhan does not leave recitation; because he has answered it by attending. And if he is in his house, he leaves recitation and answers. And the answering is that he says everything that the mu'adhdhin says except in the two hay'alahs, for he says in their place: 'There is no power nor strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Magnificent', and in place of his saying: 'Prayer is better than sleep', he says: 'You have spoken truth, and done good, and with the truth you have spoken.'. And he answers the iqamah as Sunnah, and says at the saying: 'The prayer has been established': 'May Allah establish it and perpetuate it.' And in al-Zahiriya: He says like the saying of the mu'adhdhin in all, and thus it is narrated from the Prophet. And the adhan in other than Arabic is not valid even if it is known that it is adhan. He enters the mosque while the mu'adhdhin is saying iqamah, he sits until the imam stands. In his prayer place, the leader of the neighborhood does not wait unless he is evil and the time is ample. It is disliked for him to give adhan in two mosques. The authority of adhan and iqamah belongs to the builder of the mosque absolutely, and likewise the imamate if he is just. (Fath) Not for women: because they are from the recommended Sunnahs of congregation, so they are not Sunnah for them whether they pray in congregation or not. Kashf al-Haqa'iq: 39/1]
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Adhan from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by listing those whose adhan is not valid or not recommended: a drunkard, a slave, an illegitimate child, a blind person, and a bedouin. The commentary explains that the blind person's adhan is acceptable because his testimony is accepted in religious matters, unlike the sinner. The ruling that it is disliked to leave adhan and iqamah for a traveler is supported by a hadith where the Prophet told two travelers to give adhan and iqamah. The reason given is that travel does not remove the obligation of congregation, so it does not remove what is necessary for it. However, for a person praying alone in his house within a city, it is not disliked to omit adhan and iqamah, based on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud who prayed without adhan in his house, saying 'the adhan of the tribe suffices us'. Imam Malik held that one should not give adhan when praying alone at all, but the Hanafi position is that it is Sunnah (recommended) for the traveler and for the one praying alone in the city, so that the prayer resembles congregational prayer. The passage then details the etiquette of responding to the adhan: one in the mosque should not stop reading Quran, but one at home should stop and repeat the mu'adhdhin's words, except at the hay'alah where one says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', and at 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' one says 'sadaqta wa bararta'. Responding to the iqamah is also Sunnah, and at 'qad qamat al-salah' one says 'aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha'. Adhan in non-Arabic is invalid. Other rulings include sitting during iqamah, not giving adhan in two mosques, and that the authority for adhan belongs to the mosque's founder. Finally, women are not prescribed adhan or iqamah even if they pray in congregation, because these are from the Sunnahs of congregation that are not recommended for women.

Key Terms
الأذان (al-adhān): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, announced to indicate the entry of prayer time and invite to congregation.
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): The second call immediately before the start of the congregational prayer, similar to adhan but with the addition 'qad qamat al-salah'.
الحيعلة (al-ḥay‘alah): The phrases 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan.
السكران (al-sakrān): A drunk person; his adhan is invalid due to lack of sobriety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it NOT disliked to omit adhan and iqamah?
A) When a traveler is alone.
B) When a person prays alone in his house in the city.
C) When a person prays in congregation at the mosque.
D) When a person prays alone in the desert.

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for men, not fard, and their omission is disliked only for a traveler.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Purity as a Condition for Prayer: Body, Garment, and Place
Definition and proof of purity conditions for prayer, with detailed scope of garment and place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on purity (taharah) from hadath and khabath as a condition for prayer, cite the Quranic evidence, and identify which parts of the body/garment/place require purity.

Core Idea
Purity from hadath (legal impurity) and khabath (physical impurity) is an external condition for prayer, proven by Quranic imperatives and a fortiori reasoning.

In this passage, the commentator explains the first condition of prayer: purity from both legal impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (khabath) on the body, garment, and place. He begins by defining what a 'condition' (shart) means in Hanafi legal theory, distinguishing it from a pillar (rukn), cause (sabab), and sign. Then he provides the Quranic proofs and clarifies the scope of what must be purified: the body from hadath, and the garment and place from khabath. This lesson will walk you through the definition, the proof, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi definition of shart
Identify the technical meaning of 'shart' (condition) as stated in the passage: something external to the act on which the act depends. Distinguish it from rukn (internal integral), sabab (cause that leads to the act), and alamah (sign like adhan).
Al-Hamawi's classification helps: if external and affecting → hillah (cause of permissibility); if external and leads to → sabab; if external and dependency exists → shart; if no dependency → sign.
2
Identify the three types of conditions for prayer
The passage divides conditions into: (1) condition of inception only (e.g., intention, takbir), (2) condition of continuance (e.g., purity, covering), (3) condition that must precede but not necessarily coincide (e.g., purity of body for prayer? Actually purity is required at the time of prayer, so it is of continuance). Note that the author says purity is among the conditions of continuance.
This classification helps in understanding when each condition must be present.
3
Recognize purity as the first condition
The passage states that purity of the body from hadath (minor/major legal impurity) and khabath (physical impurity) is the first of six conditions of prayer. The commentator explains it is given priority because it is generally not excused, unlike other conditions.
There is an exception: a person without hands/feet with a facial wound may pray without wudu or tayammum, but this is a rare case.
4
Examine the Quranic proofs
For purification from hadath, the proof is Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6: 'When you rise to prayer, purify yourselves.' For purification from khabath on garment, the proof is Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4: 'And your garment purify.' The obligation to purify the place is derived via an a fortiori argument (qiyas awla): since a garment, which can be removed, must be pure, the place, which cannot be removed, is even more deserving of purity.
The hadith 'la salata illa bi-tuhur' (no prayer without purity) is also cited.
5
Apply the scope: garment and place
The term 'garment' (thawb) includes anything worn on the body: cap, slippers, shoes, and even a child carried if it does not hold itself. 'Place' (makan) refers only to the parts that touch the body during prayer: feet, forehead (on the correct view), hands, and knees. The place of the nose is not included by agreement.
This limits the requirement: a small impure spot outside those contact points (e.g., the nose area) does not invalidate prayer.
6
Note the recommended and disliked practices
The passage mentions that it is recommended to pray in three garments (shirt, waist wrapper, turban) and disliked to pray in a single sirwal (trousers).
This is related to proper attire, though not a condition for validity.

(فتح، مستخلص وغيره) وثوبه أي الشرط الثاني طهارة ثوب المصلي لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَثِيَابَكَ فَطَهِّرْ﴾ (المدثر : ٤) (ع)
Chapter of Conditions of Prayer. They are: Purity of his body from hadath and khabath, and his garment. i.e. the place of prayer. ... Chapter of Conditions i.e. in explanation of its conditions, and conditions (shurut) is plural of shart meaning sign, and in terminology what a thing depends on and is not part of it. (Ayni) Conditions of prayer: plural of shart with sukun, unlike ashrat which is plural of shart with fatha, and sharait is plural of shirtah. Al-Hamawi said: What relates to a thing: if it is internal, it is a rukn like bowing for prayer; if it is external, then if it has an effect, it is a cause like the marriage contract for permissibility; if it does not have an effect, then if it leads to it in general, it is a cause (sabab) like time for the obligation of prayer; if it does not lead to it, then if the thing depends on it, it is called a condition like purity for prayer; if it does not depend, it is a sign like adhan for prayer. Then know that the conditions of prayer are of three types: condition of inception only like intention, its existence at the time of remaining is not required, and the takbir and sermon? and condition of continuance like purity and covering the private parts, and the third: what is required in advance and not conjunction, that is purity of the body. (Fath) And they: i.e. conditions of prayer are six: First: purity of the body of the worshiper. (Ayni) Purity of his body: It was said: Purity has been given precedence over other conditions because it is more important than others; since it is not dropped due to a [normal] excuse unlike others. This is open to consideration because the one who has lost his hands and feet, if he has a wound on his face, he prays without purity and without tayammum, and does not repeat at all, unless what is meant by ‘does not drop due to excuse’ is generally. (Miskin) From hadath i.e. minor and major, and it is with two fathas: legal impurity. (Ayni, Tahawi) And khabath etc. [with two fathas: heavy or light impurity, i.e. light. And the meaning in summary is that among the conditions is that the worshiper purify his body from events (ahdath) due to His saying, the Most High: {When you rise to prayer and you are in a state of ritual impurity, purify yourselves} (5:6). And he purifies his garment and his place from impurities (akhbath) due to His saying, the Most High: {And your garment purify} (74:4). The text indicates the obligation of purification in the garment, and by its indication, the obligation of purification in the place; because separation from the garment is possible, but from the place is not possible. So when the obligation of purity is known for the garment which can be removed, the obligation of purity for the place which cannot be removed is known by the primary method (awla). And due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is no prayer except with purification.' And because standing before Allah, the Exalted, with a pure body, pure garment, and pure place is more profound in reverence and more complete in service. And hadath and janabah, even if they are not visible impurity, they are moral impurity. And hadath was given precedence over khabath because hadath occurs more frequently than khabath i.e. actual impurity. And what is meant by garment is what touches the body of the worshiper, so it includes the cap, the slippers, and the shoes, and likewise what moves with his movement or what is considered a carrier for him like a child that is impure if it does not hold itself. And it hints that the removal of impurity is a preventive. Then it is recommended that he pray in three garments: a shirt, a waist wrapper, and a turban. And it is disliked that he pray in a single sirwal. And what is meant by place is the place of his feet or one of them if he lifts the other, and the place of his forehead on the correct view, and his hands and knees if he prostrates on them, not the place of his nose. So if the place of his feet, hands, knees, and forehead is pure, but the place of his nose is impure, it is permissible without disagreement. (Fath, Extract and others) And his garment i.e. the second condition: purity of the garment of the worshiper due to His saying, the Most High: {And your garment purify} (74:4) (Ayni)
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Conditions of Prayer from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins with a linguistic and terminological definition of 'shart' (condition) and distinguishes between rukn, sabab, shart, and sign. It then states that the conditions of prayer are three types: condition for inception (like intention only at first), condition for continuance (like purity and covering), and condition of advance (like purity of body). From a practical standpoint, there are six conditions, and the first is purity of the body from hadath (major and minor) and khabath (impurity). The commentator explains why purity is given precedence: it is generally not excused, though a person without hands and feet with a face wound may pray without wudu or tayammum. He then provides Quranic proofs for purification from hadath (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) and from khabath in garment and place (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4). The obligation to purify the place is derived as an a fortiori argument: since the garment, which can be removed, must be pure, the place, which cannot be removed, is even more due. The hadith 'la salata illa bi-tuhur' is also cited. The passage details what constitutes 'garment' for the ruling (anything worn on the body, including cap, shoes, and even a child carried if it does not hold its impurity) and what constitutes 'place' (only the parts that touch the body in prayer: feet, forehead, hands, knees). It is recommended to pray in three garments (shirt, waist wrapper, turban), and disliked to pray in a single pair of trousers. The passage concludes that if the prayer place is pure for the required parts but the nose area is impure, it is permissible by consensus.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): That upon which something depends but is not part of it, i.e. an external prerequisite for validity.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): Legal impurity (minor or major) that requires wudu or ghusl, which is not a physical impurity but a moral one.
الخبث (al-khabath): Physical impurity (najasah) on the body, garment, or place, whether heavy or light.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first condition of prayer according to this passage?
A) Covering the private parts
B) Purity of the body from hadath and khabath
C) Facing the qiblah
D) The intention

Key Takeaway
Purity from hadath and khabath on body, garment, and place is the first condition of prayer, proven by Quranic imperatives and required for the prayer's validity.
