Awrah of an Enslaved Woman in Prayer
Ruling on 'awrah of enslaved women with textual evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the 'awrah of an enslaved woman in Hanafi fiqh and EXPLAIN the evidence from 'Umar's practice and the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
An enslaved woman's 'awrah in prayer is like a man's: from navel to knee, reflecting her work needs and preventing fitna.

This passage clarifies a key difference in the Hanafi school regarding the 'awrah of enslaved women. Understanding this ruling helps avoid common misconceptions and highlights the school's consideration of social context and hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling on the 'awrah of an enslaved woman (amah) in prayer: from below navel to below knee, like a man.
This includes full-owned, mudabbara, mukataba, etc.
2
Examine the evidence
Analyze the proof: 'Umar's command to a slave girl to remove her khimar (headcover), the Quranic verse 33:59 about being known and not harmed, and the wisdom of preventing fitna and hardship.
The Quranic verse is used as general principle.
3
Understand the scope
Note that this ruling applies to all categories of enslaved women, and that back and belly are also considered 'awrah.
The side follows the belly. Hermaphrodite slave treated like amah, free hermaphrodite like free woman.
4
Contrast with other views
Compare with the Shafi'i view that there is no distinction between free and enslaved woman's 'awrah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

(فتح) لم تجز: صلاته لأن للربع حكم الكل كما في الإحرام. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٠/١] وخير بين أن يصلي عريانا قاعدا بإيماء وبين أن يصلي قائما بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل، وكذا إذا كان كله متنجساً؛ لأن النظر إليهما بسبب للفتنه. (ع)] وقال زفر ومحمد: لزمه أن يصلي فيه بركوع وسجود، ولا يجوز له أن يصلي عرياناً؛ لأن خطاب التطهير سقط عنه لعجزه و لم يسقط عنه خطاب الستر لقدرته عليه، فصار بمنزلة الطاهر في حقه؛ ولأن في الصلاة فيه ترك فرض واحد، وهو طهارة الثوب النجس، وفي الصلاة عرياناً ترك فروض من ستر العورة والقيام والركوع والسجود ، ولنا أن المأمور به الستر بالطاهر، فإذا لم يقدر عليه سقط، فيميل إلى أيها شاء، والجواب عن ترك الفروض أنه وإن صلى قاعداً قد أتى ببدلها، وهو الإيماء، فلا يكون تاركاً لها لقيام البدل مقام الأصل، والأصل في جنس هذه المسألة أن من ابتلي ببليتين يختار أهونهما؛ لأن مباشرة الحرام لا تجوز إلا لضرورة، مثاله: رجل لو قام وركع وسجد ينفلت ريحه، وإن جلس ويؤمئ لا ينفلت فيصلى قاعداً بإيماء؛ لأن ترك القيام والركوع والسجود أهون؛ لأن له عوضاً، وقيد تقيد تركه في بعض الصور كالتطوع على الدابة. (فتح) ولو عدم ثوبا إلخ أراد بالثوب ما يستر عورته، وبالعدم عدم القدرة حتى لو أبيح له ثوب ثبتت القدرة على الأصح، وإذا وعد به ينتظر ، ولو قدر عليه بالشراء بثمن المثل وله ثمنه يلزمه الشراء، وإلا صلى قاعداً مؤمياً؛ لما روى أنس بن مالك أن أصحاب رسول الله الله ركبوا في السفينة فانكسرت بهم السفينة، فخرجوا من البحر عرياناً فصلوا قعوداً بالإيماء، وهذا قول روي عنهم، و لم يرو عن أقرانهم خلاف ذلك، فجعل محل الإجماع. (فتح، مستخلص) ثوباً : أي ساتراً ولو حريراً أو نباتاً أو طيناً يلطخها به. (ط) قاعدا نهارا أو ليلا في بيت أو صحراء. (فتح)
And the heavy 'awrah: it is the anus, penis, and testicles; meaning its ruling is the ruling of the shin in that uncovering a quarter of it prevents. (T) And the enslaved woman: [the full-owned, the mudabbara, the mukataba, and others.] Due to the saying of 'Umar: 'Take off your khimar, O Daffar (i.e. the stinking one), do you imitate free women?' when he saw a slave girl wearing a headcover. The wisdom in forbidding her from imitating free women is that foolish people used to harass slave girls, and 'Umar feared confusion leading to greater fitna. Allah said: 'That is more likely that they will be known and not be harmed' (Quran 33:59). And because she goes out for her master's needs in service clothes usually, so her situation is considered like that of women with mahrams regarding men to avoid hardship. (Fath) Like a man in that her 'awrah is from below her navel to below her knee. (T) And her back and belly: because looking at them is a cause [؟] because they are places of desire besides him, and both the back and belly are desired places. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/537] Also 'awrah, and the side follows the belly. The hermaphrodite slave is like the enslaved woman, the free hermaphrodite is like the free woman. 'And if he finds a garment' etc. meaning if the majority of the quarter is pure, it is more appropriate that his prayer is not valid; because the quarter represents the whole. This applies if he does not find something to remove the impurity or reduce it; then he prays with it and does not repeat, but it is not permissible for him to pray naked. (Fath) 'It is not valid' is his prayer because the quarter has the ruling of the whole, as in ihram. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/50] He has the choice between praying naked sitting with gestures or praying standing with bowing and prostration, and the latter is better. Likewise if the entire garment is impure. (A) Zufar and Muhammad said: He must pray in it with bowing and prostration, and it is not permissible for him to pray naked; because the command to purify fell from him due to inability, but the command to cover did not fall from him because he is able, so it is like pure for him. And because praying in it leaves one obligatory act (purity of garment), while praying naked leaves multiple obligations (covering 'awrah, standing, bowing, prostration). Our evidence: The commanded thing is covering with a pure garment; if he is unable, it falls, so he may choose whichever he wishes. The answer regarding leaving obligations: even if he sits, he has performed their substitute (gesturing), so he is not leaving them because the substitute stands in place of the original. The principle in such matters is that if one faces two afflictions, he chooses the easier of them, because direct commission of what is forbidden is only allowed due to necessity. Example: a man who, if he stands and bows and prostrates, his wind escapes, but if he sits and gestures it does not, then he prays sitting with gestures; because leaving standing, bowing, and prostration is easier since they have substitutes. 'And if he lacks a garment' etc. He means by 'garment' what covers his 'awrah, and by 'lack' inability; so if a garment is loaned to him, ability is established according to the correct view, and if promised, he waits. If he can purchase it at the standard price and has the money, he must buy it; otherwise he prays sitting gesturing, due to the hadith of Anas ibn Malik that the Companions were on a ship that broke, so they came out of the sea naked and prayed sitting with gestures. This is a narration from them, and no opposition from their peers is reported, so it is considered a locus of consensus. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Garment' i.e. a cover, even if silk, plant material, or mud that he smears on. (T) 'Sitting' day or night, in a house or desert. (Fath)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on conditions of prayer, addressing the 'awrah of enslaved women, the ruling on praying with an impure garment, and what to do if one has no garment. First, it defines the 'heavy 'awrah' (anus, penis, testicles) which have the same quarter rule as the shin. Then the 'awrah of an enslaved woman is stated to be like that of a man: from below navel to below knee. This is derived from the practice of 'Umar who ordered a slave girl to remove her khimar, and supported by Quran 33:59 and the rationale of avoiding fitna and hardship. The back and belly are also considered 'awrah. Next, the passage discusses a situation where one has a garment that is impure: if more than a quarter of it is pure, it is preferable not to pray in it (i.e., prayer is invalid), but if less than a quarter is pure, one has the option to pray naked sitting with gestures or to pray standing in the impure garment. The text mentions a difference between Zufar and Muhammad (the two companions) and Abu Hanifa: Zufar and Muhammad hold that one must pray in the impure garment, as the inability to purify is excused but covering is still possible; Abu Hanifa gives a choice, arguing that the command to cover with pure is impossible, so it falls. The passage then explains that the principle is to choose the easier of two afflictions. Finally, if one has no garment at all (or is unable to obtain one), one prays sitting with gestures (i.e., lowering the head for ruku' and sujud), based on the practice of the Companions who were shipwrecked and prayed naked sitting. This is considered a transmitted consensus. The garment can be any cover, even silk, leaves, or mud.

Key Terms
أمة (amah): Enslaved woman (full-owned, mudabbara, mukataba, etc.). Her 'awrah in prayer is like that of a man: from below navel to below knee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the 'awrah of an enslaved woman in Hanafi fiqh?
A) From below navel to below knee
B) From neck to ankle
C) Only the private parts (front and back)
D) Entire body except face and hands

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school specifies an enslaved woman's 'awrah in prayer as from navel to knee, based on evidence from 'Umar and the Quran.
